Report on the results of parallel checks on the administration of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The submitted material informs about the progress and results of the parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic Control Authority, which focused on the administration of Value Added Tax Exchange System (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so revenues from value added tax affect not only the national budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
Parallel control actions were aimed in particular at checking the progress of tax administrations in examining the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions between Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of VIES enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of value added tax payers in individual Member States of the European Union and on commercial transactions carried out by such payers.
Mismatch between data in the VIES system and data in the VAT return filed by the payer should alert the tax administrator to suspicious cases and allow detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefit of the parallel checks was not only the exchange of information on the procedure of the financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular the examination of the use of the VIES system in checking the application of the right to value added tax in intracommunity transactions.
The knowledge gained in the implementation of parallel controls is beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of further parallel checks in cooperation with the audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel checks on the administration of value added tax for the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of control: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Control of tax authorities' procedures for the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and the performance of VIES tasks for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic ("SAO, Czech Republic") and the Czech Audit Office of the Republic ("SAO SR") concluded on 12.9.2005 the Surveillance Cooperation Agreement.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implementation of the parallel control actions "Value Added Tax Administration," included in the SAO Control Plan for 2005 under No. 05/19 and "Control of the Tax Procedure control and enforcement of VAT on value added and tasks under the VIES system on exchange of funds by Member States, " included in the SAO's audit plan under No 22/2005.
Parallel control actions were coordinated.
The result of the joint coordinated control was developed within the meaning of European Enforcement Regulation No 31 for INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent specified by the Treaty and drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated inspection was to verify selected cases of delivery and acquisition of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between the taxpayers of value added tax from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic") and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Slovak Republic").
Both parties contractually undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the Value Added Tax Information Exchange System (VIES) and data on requests received and sent to verify commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and SR.
The checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the control was carried out by the state budget department and the territorial unions of central Bohemia, northwestern Bohemia, southern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the Ministry of Finance and 12 Financial Offices: The Financial Office in Mladá Split, Tax Office in Cologne, Tax Office in Teplice, Tax Office in Karlovy Vary, Tax Office in Tábor, Financial Office Brno III, Tax Office in Znojmo, Tax Office in Zlín, Tax Office in Šumperk, Tax Office in Ostrava I, Tax Office for Prague 7 and Tax Office for Prague 9.
The control on the territory of the SR was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with Exposures of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: Tax department Bratislava I, Tax department Komárno, Tax department Trenčín, Tax department Prievidza, Tax department Prievidza
Objective of checks:
The aim of the parallel control actions was to examine the procedure of the financial and tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") after the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the Single Internal Market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "the EU") and to examine the use of the electronic information system VIES, in particular when checking the application of the VAT exemption claim.
The controlled period of coordinated control was the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions In EU Member States, an electronic VIES system is introduced to enable tax administrations to check whether the supplier has been entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and to verify in the country of destination whether the purchaser has properly declared and taxed the goods acquired.
VIES is not centralised within the EU, each Member State develops its own system.
The examination identified differences of national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and SR in the following areas:
The aggregated reports shall indicate the delivery values of the goods to other EU Member States, the values of the services provided shall not be included in the summary reports.
Data from summary reports filed by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the tax authorities, where they compare with data on deliveries of goods to other EU Member States listed in VAT tax returns.
The tax authorities transmit data from summary reports to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In SR, data from summary reports filed by Slovak payers at tax offices are only transferred to electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of SR (Customs).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of supplies of goods and the value of services to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT returns, which allows to compare the values listed in the aggregated reports with the value of supplies of goods according to the VAT return and to identify any differences.
In the SR, the values of the goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are aggregated on the common line of the VAT return.
Consequently, in SR, the system does not allow to automatically identify differences between the values of delivery of goods according to tax returns and summary reports.
Separate reporting of the value of supplies of goods in VAT tax returns enables the data comparison results to be used to check the VAT exemption for supplies to the EU.
The received data from the summary reports filed by payers in other EU Member States are processed into Customs and compared with the value of the acquisition of goods indicated by the payers from the Czech Republic or SR in the VAT tax returns.
In the SR, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities themselves decide which cases of differences will be examined.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values of delivery and acquisition of goods must be examined by the tax administrators and transmits the list of these cases to the local tax authorities.
This ensures that, for the most significant derogations, it will be checked whether the VAT was declared at the correct level when the goods were acquired.
The audit also highlighted some problems in the VAT management system due to the different reporting of intracommunity transactions (i.e. delivery and acquisition of goods by payers from different EU Member States):
Summary reports are made in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum time limit for processing and dispatching data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
Reducing the period for which summary reports are submitted to one month, together with reducing the time limit for processing, would allow earlier access to VIES data.
The tax authorities could thus more effectively verify whether VAT was declared at the correct level in intracommunity transactions.
At the same time, the submission of VAT returns and summary declarations for the same tax period (month) would allow for a faster verification of whether the payer has reported in both the aggregated report and the VAT return the same value of the delivery of goods to the EU.
Differences between the delivery values reported by EU payers and the acquisition values reported by payers from the Czech Republic and SR were due, among other things, to different reporting of intracommunity and acquisition data in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the presentation of advances received in summary reports or the reporting of intracommunity deliveries in the supplier's summary report in a different quarter than intracommunity acquisitions in the purchaser's VAT return.
A harmonisation of the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would make the control activities of the national tax administrations more effective.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was also aimed at examining selected intracommunity transactions between the two countries.
Together, 40 cases of commercial transactions between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined, where there were doubts about their implementation or suspected tax evasion on VAT.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR have identified among others the following:
tax entities have declared in their VAT returns, for the purpose of unduly obtaining excessive VAT deduction, intracommunity transactions which have not actually taken place;
tax entities reported intracommunity deliveries in the context of carousel transactions that deliberately reduced the value of supplies multiple times in order to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers reported in their VAT returns and summary reports intracommunity supplies of exempt goods to purchasers who were so-called "lost companies" and did not grant tax on acquired goods;
suppliers have made intracommunitary supplies of VAT-exempt goods to tax entities which have not been registered for VAT in another Member State.
In such cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been taxed in the supplier's country;
suppliers reported intracommunity supplies in their VAT returns at a higher value than the intracommunity acquisition declared by the purchasers, and in some cases VAT was declared incorrectly.
The knowledge gained in the control action showed that the VIES system provides tax administrations with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracommunity transactions.
Tax administrations should pay particular attention to the rigorous examination of the differences between data reported by VAT payers and data in the VIES system and the use of all information in tax procedures.
Issue of value added tax after Czech and Slovak accession to the EU
Value Added Tax
On 1.5.2004 the Czech Republic and SR became members of the EU.
Internal borders and border controls on intra-EU movements of goods have been abolished after EU accession.
The VAT administrator was by 30 April 2004 the competent financial and tax office, with the exception of imports of goods and occasional bus services in the country where the tax administrator was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter "Act No. 235/2004 Coll.") and Act No. 222/2004 Z. z., on value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 222/2004 Z. z. ") the VAT administration transferred from customs offices to financial and tax offices when purchasing goods and services (formerly imported) from other EU Member States.
By delivering the goods in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as owner.
The delivery of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is the delivery of goods that have actually been shipped or transported to another EU Member State.
According to the provisions of Section 64 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. this is an exempt taxable transaction with a right to deduct VAT when the goods are delivered to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
For the delivery of goods in SR according to the provisions of Section 8 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z. considers the supply of tangible property to change ownership.
The supply of goods shall also be deemed to involve the transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the country to another Member State where such goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
According to the provisions of Section 43 of Law No 222/2004 Z. z. the supply of goods from the country to another Member State shall be exempt from VAT where the purchaser is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
By acquiring goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 16 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods dispatched or transported to the purchaser by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer purchases goods at a price excluding VAT and is obliged in the Czech Republic to declare VAT according to the provisions of Section 25 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., and in fulfilment of the conditions laid down in Section 73 of this Act he is entitled to deduct VAT.
The acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic from another EU Member State is in the Slovak Republic according to the provisions of Section 11 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. the acquisition of the right to dispose as an owner of movable tangible property dispatched or transported by the purchaser by the supplier or the purchaser, or for their account, to the territory of another Member State.
The tax liability in the SR is incurred by the payer when acquiring goods from another Member State in accordance with the provisions of Section 20 of Act No. 222/2004 Z.z.
According to the provisions of Section 49 of Act No 222/2004 Z, the payer can. z. deduct VAT if the tax is applied to the acquisition of goods domestically from another Member State in accordance with the provisions of Sections 11 and 11a of this Act.
Triangular business is understood according to Section 17 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., or Section 45 of Act No. 222/2004 Z. z. a transaction concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, the subject of which is the supply of the same goods between the three.
Intracommunity transactions mean the supply and acquisition of goods between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intracommunity transactions between the Czech Republic and SR are shown in the table below.
VIES
In order to control the application of the VAT exemption right to intracommunity supplies of goods, a system of exchange of VAT information has been established within the EU.
It includes an electronic VIES system that allows EU tax administrations to check whether the supplier has been entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and vice versa whether the purchaser has properly declared and taxed the goods acquired.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State shall develop its own VIES system.
National systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through the EU Common Communication Network (CCN); see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was connected to the automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "ADIS"), in SR to the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "APV DIS").
These systems are used by financial and tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and charges.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU Member State receives information on tax entities that it would not be able to obtain on its own without such cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax losses.
Under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State, within its internal organisational structure, establishes a central unit in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the administration of VAT, the Central Liaison Office.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance - Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in VAT Administration (hereinafter referred to as "MF Customs") has been established, performs the tasks resulting from international cooperation.
The function of the Customs Office in SR is carried out by the Tax Directorate of SR, Department of International Administrative Cooperation (hereinafter referred to as "DR Customs").
These departments inter alia communicate with EU foreign administrations in particular in the field of information exchange within the VIES system, exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of the EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax controls, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as "VAT creditors") in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to verify an intracommunity transaction or to obtain other information related to a particular tax entity, the financial and tax authorities send requests for information to the EU via the MF Customs and DR Customs.
Through these requests, they receive information from the requested Member States that they can use to correct the VAT.
Requests for information are sent mostly in electronic form between EU Member State Customs using the standardised SCAC form.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was focused mainly on the examination of selected intracommunity transactions between the two countries and on the level of use of information obtained through international cooperation by financial and tax authorities.
The SAO, the Czech Republic requested the SAO to examine in 30 cases commercial transactions between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
SAO SR requested the SAO, Czech Republic to examine in 10 cases commercial transactions between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
The examination of intracommunity transactions revealed:
o
The SAO, the Czech Republic requested the SAO SR to examine the tax administration procedure, to which a reply to the request for information was sent.
The Slovak Tax Office requested the delivery of goods (footwear) in the third quarter of 2004 from a Slovak payer totalling SK 2,847 thousand.
The Tax Office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer indicated the acquisition of goods of this value only in an additional VAT return and delivered the same goods to Slovak tax entities worth CZK 2,550 by the end of 2004.
On the basis of international cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the local tax authority fully recognised the Slovak supplier as entitled to an excessive deduction of VAT incurred, inter alia, on the basis of this supply.
This tax office did not provide information about the suspected reexportation to the local tax authorities of the relevant customers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
This will give rise to further examination of commercial activities in connection with possible carousel fraud.
o
Through the SCAC form the Czech tax administrator requested an examination of the delivery of the technology line to SR totalling CZK 4,850 in the second quarter of 2004.
The tax procedure carried out in SR showed that only part of the technological line was supplied. The components totalling CZK 3,395 thousand were not delivered.
The SAO SR found during the examination of this case that the VAT on the taxable transactions made was declared by the Slovak tax entity on the amount of CZK 4,850 in the VAT return (hereinafter referred to as "DAP") for the tax period 7/2004.
The SAO, Czech Republic also found that the Czech taxpayer reported excessive VAT deduction of CZK 655 thousand for that quarter in its DAP, resulting from the application of the VAT deduction on the purchase of this technology line from another domestic payer.
On the basis of the results of the investigation, the Czech Tax Office concluded that the Czech and Slovak tax entities established a business relationship for the purpose of unduly obtaining an excess VAT deduction, questioned the taxable transactions and did not recognise the Czech taxpayer's part of the right to deduct CZK 647 thousand.
o
In 2004, the Slovak tax administrator applied to the Czech taxpayer by means of the SCAC form for verification of the supply of goods (copying machines) in the value of SK 24,246 in December 2002.
In November 2002, the Slovak payer purchased these goods from another tax entity worth Sk. 29,667 and subsequently sold them to a Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity applied excessive VAT deduction for the relevant tax period.
The tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic found that the Czech tax entity does not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not submit the DAP for the 4 quarter of 2002 or for the subsequent period.
SAO SR found that the Slovak tax administration did not recognise, on the basis of the result of the tax check, an overcompensation of SK 5,541 000 applied in DAP for the month 11/2002 and established a tax liability of SK 1,750 000.
At the same time, the tax entity was not granted an exemption from VAT on exports of goods in December 2002.
o
The Czech tax administrator received an order from the MF Customs to verify the value of the goods acquired for Q3 2004.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer was to acquire from SR goods (diluent) worth 3,767 thousand Sk.
This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, DAP did not file and the VAT for the months 7 to 12/2004 was calculated from the official authority of CZK 0.
The Czech tax administrator requested a SCAC form to verify whether the supplies of goods from SR to the Czech Republic took place, in what quantity and price (according to invoices).
In reply, the Slovak local tax office sent a copy of the invoice, consignment notes and an invitation to pay the invoice.
SAO SR found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with a right to deduct VAT on this supply.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech tax administrator evaluated the response to the request for information received from the SR as evidence that the company acquired goods from another EU Member State.
On the basis of further investigation, the tax authority in the Czech Republic will request a review of the tax liability.
o
The Slovak company supplied goods (woodpecker products) to an American company, which stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free zone.
The operator of this free zone was indicated on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, for example, an American company purchased from a Slovak payer a wooden tile worth USD 57,600 (at a unit price of USD 100/unit), which it placed in a free zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred the property rights to the goods to a Swiss company worth USD 14,400 (unit price USD 25/unit) and the goods were exported back to the SR.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the area of the free zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator initiated tax checks on the supplier of goods for suspected carousel transactions in the various tax years 2004 and 2005.
Examination of transactions was requested by the Czech local tax administrators using several SCAC forms.
The individual replies gradually created a picture of business and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in carousel business.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO SR, found that these trade relations deliberately resulted in a gradual multiple depreciation of the value of goods.
On the basis of the information obtained, the Tax Directorate of SR concluded that in this case carousel trade is free pricing (i.e. the import of underserved goods and its overvaluation by domestic companies located in the chain between the importer and the exporter), which is not a breach of the VAT Act in the SR.
In the current legislation, the excessive deduction of VAT to export companies cannot be avoided as they fulfil all the conditions of the Act on VAT exemption.
o
Registration for VAT was cancelled at the date of 12.7.2005.
On 27.10.2005, on the basis of a voluntary application for VAT registration, the entity became again a taxpayer.
The Czech taxpayer entered in DAP for the month of 8/2005 (i.e. the period in which he was not a VAT payer) the value of the acquisition of goods from SR amounting to CZK 1,174 thousand and claimed the VAT deduction.
This value corresponded to the delivery of goods by the Slovak payer amounting to Sk 1,530 thousand, which the Slovak payer indicated in the DAP as the delivery of goods to another EU Member State with a right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the delivery by means of the SCAC form because the Slovak supplier did not demonstrate how the goods delivered to the Czech Republic were acquired.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech taxpayer does not cooperate with the tax administrator and does not reside at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the Czech Republic by the local tax administrator for the purpose of examining the data.
o
The Slovak payer entered in the summary report for Q3 2004 the delivery of goods worth 956 thousand Sk to the tax entity from the Czech Republic.
The Czech subject's DIČ was flawed by the VIES system.
Verification in the payer database revealed that such VAT was never allocated in the Czech Republic.
According to the invoices issued by the Slovak payer, the Company carried out electrical assembly works on real estate in the Czech Republic. It was not the delivery of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT as the Czech entity informed the Slovak entity that it was registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax administrator requested that these facts be verified using the SCAC form.
The SAO, Czech Republic found out by inquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the tax entity listed on the invoices as a customer was never registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, did not grant tax on the received services from the Slovak entity and did not grant tax on the acquisition of goods.
Neither local investigations nor tax checks have been carried out on the Czech entity, its current whereabouts are unknown.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity had become a VAT payer by law.
The Slovak tax entity will be subject to a tax check for the 1 to 4 2004 quarter.
o
The Slovak payer entered in the summary report for Q3 2004 the delivery of goods worth 1,055 thousand Sk to the Czech payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, electrical assembly works were carried out on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not the delivery of goods from SR to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The Slovak tax administrator requested that these facts be verified using the SCAC form.
The SAO, Czech Republic found out by inquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of delivery and that a local investigation was carried out to verify the acquisition of goods from other EU Member States in Q3 2004.
On the basis of this local investigation, it was found that in this case it was not actually the acquisition of goods, but the acquisition of services, which was also reported by the Czech entity in the proper DAP.
The Tax Office also found that the Czech entity did not deduct VAT in the correct amount for the third quarter of 2004 due to poor VAT calculation procedure.
The tax entity shall submit an additional DAP.
By enquiry with the local tax office, the SAO discovered that the Slovak payer had erroneously indicated the provision of the service in the summary report and would be subject to a tax check for the first to fourth quarter of 2004.
o
The Czech tax entity voluntarily registered as a VAT payer from 10. 3. 2004.
For the first quarter of 2004, DAP submitted a high turnover in both input and output.
The local tax administrator initiated the tax procedure, the body did not cooperate with the tax administrator, so due to suspicion of involvement in the carousel trade a VAT of CZK 0 was charged.
Another DAP was no longer filed by this payer.
Due to non-compliance with the statutory obligations, his VAT registration was cancelled on 4.1.2005.
According to VIES data, this entity was to acquire goods worth SK 7,846 thousand from the Slovak payer in the third and fourth quarters of 2004.
In order to verify the execution of these transactions, the Czech tax administrator sent two requests for information to SR.
The SAO SR found out by inquiry with the local tax office that the Czech company executive denied in witness testimony the execution of the examined transactions and questioned the authenticity of its signature on invoices and other documents.
On the basis of a tax proceeding in the Slovak Republic, the intracommunitary supply to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer was called into question.
The payer will not be recognised as entitled to VAT exemption and will be charged VAT on the above amount.
o
According to VIES data, the Czech payer was to acquire goods from SR in the first quarter of 2005 (working clothes) totalling SK 39,970 thousand.
In this quarter, the Czech payer reported the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only in DAP for the month of 3/2005, totalling CZK 11,292 thousand.
The local tax administrator carried out local investigations with the entity for the purpose of examining the data in this DAP.
As the Company did not submit any documents or otherwise substantiate the taxable transactions, the tax administrator charged it CZK 0 on 9 June 2005.
Due to doubts regarding the acquisition of goods, the tax administrator sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic in May 2005.
According to the reply to the requests for information, the tax administrator in SR had doubts about the implementation of business cases as well as about the payment.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent an initiative to DR CLO to carry out simultaneous checks with the Czech tax administration, which would be carried out on stakeholders.
At the time of the coordinated inspection, the local tax administrator carried out further inquiries in the Czech Republic concerning the Czech entity and at the same time an investigation was carried out by the Police of the Czech Republic.
o
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of being involved in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (working clothes) were carried out between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
Slovak payer No. 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered them back to SR payer No. 4 (see scheme No. 2).
(A)
Czech payer No. 2 was to acquire goods (working garments) worth CZK 4,847 thousand in the fourth quarter of 2004 from the Slovak payer No. 1 and 17,050 thousand in the first quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the local tax administrator sent a request for information to SR on 25. 5. 2005.
In reply, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the implementation of business cases and about the payment.
On 8. 6. 2005, a request for information was received from the MF Customs Office of the Slovak Republic concerning goods worth 16,575 thousand Sk, which was to be delivered by Slovak payer No. 1 to Czech payer No. 2 in December 2004.
The Slovak party requested to verify whether the Czech payer No. 2 actually accepted the goods, admitted in DAP and paid VAT.
The official record produced by the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech payer No. 2 no longer resides at an address registered in the Commercial Register.
Although they were VAT payers with a monthly tax period, DAP submitted for the quarterly tax period.
In view of this fact, the Czech tax administrator could not calculate VAT.
The taxable transaction between the Slovak payer No. 1 and the Czech payer No. 2 mentioned in the application of SK 16,575 could not be verified in view of the above.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel trade in order to obtain excessive VAT deduction.
B)
Czech payer No. 3, engaged in the purchase and sale of passenger cars, submitted DAP for the tax period 1 and 2/2005, in which he reported delivery of goods (working clothes) to Slovak payer No. 4 totalling T CZK 21,935.
These work clothes were to be purchased by Czech payer No. 3 from Czech payer No. 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The local tax office sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic, in particular to verify whether the Slovak payer No. 4 acquired goods worth CZK 1,025 thousand from the Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004 and CZK 21,935 thousand in the first quarter of 2005.
The reply to this request for information received from the SR showed that in DAP 12/2004 the Slovak payer No 4 reported zero value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in DAP 1 and 2/2005 the value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only amounted to SK 1,193 thousand.
Slovak taxpayer No 4 did not respond to the call for tax documents for the tax period from 10/2004 to 3/2005.
The local investigation carried out in the SR revealed that the company was not present at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
The reply further stated that this payer fulfils all the characteristics of the so-called "lost company" and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator had sent an initiative to DR CLO to carry out simultaneous checks with the Czech tax administration, which would be carried out on interested tax entities.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or disprove the existence of goods.
VAT will be charged according to the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also dealt with by the Police of the Czech Republic.
Progress of the control action
In preparation of the parallel control actions, a coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO, Czech Republic with representatives of the SAO SR took place in the first half of July 2005.
Participants of this meeting were familiar with the VAT legislation in both countries and the integration of the electronic VIES system into national databases.
The negotiations resulted in a specification of the extent of cooperation and the conditions for sampling.
Both parties agreed that cooperation will focus on the following areas: (a) verification of the validity and accuracy of VAT creditors in the Czech Republic and SR in intracommunity supplies; b) examination of data on intracommunity acquisitions specified in the DAP payer in the Czech Republic using information from summary reports (hereinafter referred to as "SH") of SR payers contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and Slovakia on business transactions.
It was also agreed that the collection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out following the volume of intracommunity supplies between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and SR via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intracommunitary transactions
The procedure for processing information by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic during intracommunity delivery and acquisition of goods shows the following diagram.
5.1.1 Intracommunitary supply
If the VAT payer makes an intracommunity delivery, he is obliged to lodge an SH by the 25th day following the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic gives summary information in SH about the supplies of goods to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The taxpayer in the SR is obliged to enter into the SH the value of the exempt goods delivered from the country to other EU Member States for the period of the calendar quarter.
Data on the value of the delivered goods are given in the SH in the Czech and Slovak currencies, broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their tax credits, under which they were registered in their country.
Service data shall not be entered in SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds that he has given incorrect data in SH, he is obliged to submit subsequent SH.
If a payer in the SR finds that the information provided in the SH was incomplete or incorrect, he shall submit a corrective SH before the expiry of the deadline for submission of the SH, after the expiry of that period he shall submit an additional SH.
The VIES system allows the exchange of information on the registration data of VAT registered payers in EU Member States.
Payers from the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic can verify whether the customer's tax account is registered in the EU Member State.
Data from filed SHS are grouped on the MF CLO or DR CLO by the VIES system according to the individual tax payers.
The total value of all deliveries is created for each purchaser's tax receipt and the performance code of all its Czech and Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files.
The data from the L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intracommunity transactions between the Czech Republic and SR (from L1QD files) is shown in the table below.
If the VIES system in another Member State detects erroneous purchaser's tax rates in the sent files, it will generate a so-called  report that contains all the wrong TACs indicating the type of error.
This message is subsequently sent to the MF CLO or DR CLO.
The O_MCTL report may contain 4 types of errors: formally incorrect TP, the TP is not registered or has never been allocated in that country, the purchaser with a specific TP was not a VAT payer in that quarter, the registration for VAT of the purchaser was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, the MF transmits data from received reports to the tax authorities.
If the incorrect EU tax rate is used in one of the SH lines sent or subsequent SH, the ADIS system generates the so-called "VAT ID Notification of Doubt" at the competent tax office.
The tax office will verify whether the delivery to a VAT-registered payer in another EU Member State has actually taken place and will record the result of the verification into the system.
In the SR, DR Customs will process all the messages O_MCTL in the VIES system and send them electronically to the local tax authorities together with the identification of the tax payers who have reported erroneous taxes in their SH.
The tax authorities subsequently invite the payer to submit an additional SH and the tax office will verify the delivery of the goods to the payer when reporting the invalid TP in the filed SH.
The following table shows the number of incorrect taxes relating to intracommunity transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Out of a total of 41,728 Czech taxpayers, listed in the SH of Slovak payers in the period from Q2 2004 to Q1 2005, 929 were incorrect TAC, i.e. 2.23%.
Of the total number 62,997 DIČ Slovak payers listed in the SH of Czech payers in the same period, 416 were incorrect TAC, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intracommunity transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, Czech taxpayers reported on average fewer incorrect VAT payments in their SH.
When examining the activities of the financial and tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not in all cases provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations.
For example:
- although the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax entity in the 4 quarter of 2004 when asked by the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, a report was subsequently generated O_MCTL due to the termination of the registration of the payer in this quarter.
The investigation revealed that the termination of the marketing authorisation did not take place until 1.1.2005;
- SAO SR further found that 6 tax entities submitted SHS in which the incorrect TTC was indicated, but the reports O_MCTL did not include these TTs.
In the SR, filed by the SH shall be transferred to the tax authorities in electronic form and data from which shall be sent to the DR Customs Office.
After the subsequent processing of these data in the VIES system, DR CUSTOMS will send to the relevant tax authorities the so-called breakdown of errors in SH filed by tax entities for the respective quarters.
The SAO has compared data on the incidence of erroneous data in the SH to 26.7.2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the inspection) and to 2.2.2006 (i.e. data processed after the completion of the inspection).
The data comparison shall include the following table.
From the above data, it is apparent that the SAO SR control not only affected the reduction of the number of SHs with an erroneous TP (by an average of SH 199 per quarter), but also the reduction of the number of unrepaired errors in SH (by an average of 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intracommunity deliveries listed by the payer in the relevant DAP lines is compared with the value of intracommunity deliveries indicated by this payer in the quarterly SH.
ADIS automatically indicates differences between these values.
The tax administrator should examine the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the data obtained to determine the tax liability.
SAO, Czech Republic found that audited tax authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the SH and DAP values was CZK 537,231.
As of Q3 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values listed in SH and DAP of up to 0.5% of the total value of intracommunity supplies according to SH as a match and set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intracommunity deliveries for one quarter, 0,5% of the value represents a significant amount, so tax administrations should not set the SH and DAP's compliance in these cases without clarifying the reasons for the differences.
Eg. The tax administrator set a match for the value difference of CZK 1,561 without examination.
The examination of differences in the Czech Republic and Slovakia was complicated by the fact that SH was filed by payers for each calendar quarter within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
Tax administrators were unable to compare the intracommunity delivery values specified in these DAPs with the SH values for the first two months of the calendar quarter.
In these cases, the tax administrators found out about any inconsistency of data in the DAP and SH only when the tax liability or excessive deduction of VAT was charged. returned.
5.1.2 Intracommunitary acquisition
The VIES system provides, inter alia, information on the values of intracommunity transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, received data from SH filed by payers from other EU Member States (delivered L1QD) are processed by MF Customs.
During the processing the data are calculated at the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the value of the acquisition indicated by the Czech payers in the DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods reported by payers in the DAP should be within the minimum and maximum converted value of L1QD (values L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is lower than the L1min value, a so-called verification order is generated for the payer with the most significant irregularities.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a reminder of problematic tax entities and are forwarded to locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders concerning audited financial authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the table below.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the audited tax authorities in 33 cases did not investigate irregularities in intracommunity acquisitions, to which the orders for verification were submitted.
The total difference between the SH values of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases was at least CZK 148,319 thousand.
The SAO, the Czech Republic selected 533 files of tax entities for which the audited tax authorities received an order of verification from the MF Customs.
The check identified the following most common causes of differences between the values specified in the purchaser's DAP and the supplier's SH: on the purchaser's side (Czech payer) in 263 cases, the purchaser did not indicate the acquisition of goods in the proper DAP, in 93 cases the payer declared the acquisition of goods in a different tax period than the one in which he was liable to tax, in 6 cases the purchaser entered the value of the goods in the wrong DAP line, on the supplier's side (EU payer) in 88 cases, EU payers included in their SH the values of the services provided to the Czech payer, of these, 54 were SR payers, in 39 cases suppliers have included in the SH the supply of goods in a different tax period than the Czech Republic purchasers in their DAP, in 22 cases, suppliers reported incorrect Czech payer's VAT in SH, In 16 cases, suppliers reported incorrect delivery values in SH, in 12 cases suppliers have included in the SH the value of goods delivered to the Czech Republic before 1.5. 2004, In 5 cases, suppliers have included in the SH the value of the advance received.
On the part of SR payers, the value of the services provided was most often incorrectly included in SH.
54 such cases have been identified in audited financial authorities.
Eg. when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974 thousand was created by the fact that the Slovak payer introduced the 1 of the provision of services (construction work and delivery of goods including assembly in the Czech Republic) to SH for the 2005 quarter.
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of the received advances in SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers reported in SH received advances from Czech payers, resulting in an order to verify the difference of CZK 3,580 thousand.
Orders to verify acquired goods are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where subsequent changes in SH data occur in EU Member States, such as the change of the customer of goods in the Czech Republic or the increased value of the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
Since the VIES does not automatically alert those changes, the local tax administrator does not need to know the goods purchaser without any other suggestion of the facts relevant for the correct determination of the tax liability of the goods acquired and there is a high likelihood of VAT evasion.
The audit of the SAO, Czech Republic found that this situation occurred for example in the following cases:
Slovak payer in SH for Q2 2004 reported the value of delivery of goods for Czech payer amounting to 1,504 thousand Sk.
On 1.2.2005, the Tax Office sent a request for information to the local Czech payer because the Czech payer granted the purchase of goods totalling only CZK 425 thousand.
On the basis of the tax procedure, the Slovak payer submitted an additional SH on 1.3.2005 in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the supply for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 thousand Sk and by increasing the value of the goods delivered to another Czech payer from 194 thousand Sk to 1,160 thousand Sk.
Four Slovak payers reported in their SH for the second quarter of 2004 intracommunity delivery to Czech payers totalling SK 10,240 thousand (i.e. CZK 8,183 thousand).
However, Czech buyers did not report intracommunity acquisitions at DAP.
On the basis of an international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer who was not mentioned in the SH filed by Slovak payers.
During the first quarter of 2005, Slovak payers increased the value of intracommunity deliveries for this Czech payer by a total of SK 10,240 thousand during the second quarter of 2004.
In view of the above, the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data in DAP for Q2 2004, even if the actual purchaser did not comply with the obligation to declare intracommunity acquisitions for this quarter.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the above mentioned Czech payer was additionally charged VAT for the tax years 5 and 6/2004 amounting to CZK 3,640 thousand and 3,305 thousand CZK for the third quarter of 2004.
It is clear from the above that tax administrations have had to examine not only differences arising from errors in the purchaser's DAP, but also differences due to different reporting of intracommunity and acquisition data in individual EU Member States.
The harmonisation of the reporting conditions for this data would lead to a more efficient control activity of the tax administrations.
Acquisition of goods in SR
In the SR, the APV DIS system allows to compare data on the value of the goods acquired through the VIES system from other EU Member States with data contained in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
The method used to compare the data is called the "MIN-MAX method."
This method will convert the value of supplies of goods listed in SH to payers from other EU Member States at a minimum and maximum exchange rate for the relevant quarter.
The MIN-MAX interval will be created, which is used for comparison with the value of acquisition of goods listed in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DR CUSTOMS shall send information to the tax administrations on the intracommunity acquisition values specified in the DAP and the EU VIES delivery values.
The tax administrator decides which persons registered for VAT will be checked for the difference, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
On the basis of data provided by DR CLO, the SAO has selected 57 files of Slovak purchasers of goods from audited tax offices, of which 25 payers have acquired goods from the Czech Republic, for which the highest differences were found between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and those declared in the DAP.
The audit carried out by the SAO SR confirmed the fact that the tax administrations did not rigorously investigate the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and thus did not verify the accuracy of the data contained in the Slovak purchasers "DAP.
As part of the audit, the SAO requested the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations on specific tax entities.
During the audit of the SAO SR at the tax offices, 31 local investigations were completed.
For Slovak companies with significant differences in MIN-MAX values in the acquisition of goods from EU Member States, the following facts were identified:
In DAP 2004 Q4, the Slovak payer did not indicate the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The Tax Office found that the company from the Czech Republic reported this payer in SH for the fourth quarter of 2004 by mistake, while delivering goods worth CZK 19,184 thousand to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, the Slovak company was to acquire goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria worth MIN 682,692 thousand Sk and MAX 715 105 thousand Sk.
This company submitted DAP for the given periods, in which it indicated the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU amounting only to SK 480,599.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation, finding that the tax entity purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not indicate intracommunity deliveries according to the date of issue of invoices, but according to the date of delivery.
In view of other irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU countries, the tax administrator will request verification of the value of the goods delivered by means of SCAC forms.
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer did not mention the acquisition of goods from EU Member States in DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer was to purchase goods worth MIN 11 286 thousand Sk and MAX 11 845 thousand Sk.
A local investigation was carried out by the Tax Office and the inspection showed that no goods from EU Member States were acquired by the tax entity in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The SAO SR recommended that the tax office request a verification of the supply of goods from EU Member States by means of a SCAC form.
VIES recorded the delivery of goods for a Slovak customer worth MIN 557 thousand Sk and MAX 565 thousand Sk.
In the DAP for the tax period from 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not declare any acquisition of goods.
A local investigation by the tax administrator found that the tax entity received an invoice from a supplier from the Czech Republic on 10. 12. 2004 for material consumed in the repair of the hydraulic loader.
The SAO SR recommended that a tax check be carried out on the payer.
During the audit of the SAO SR in 16 cases, the tax authorities did not terminate local investigations.
In 10 cases, the SAO SR asked the tax administrator to carry out a tax check on tax entities.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax checks will be submitted by the tax authorities after their implementation by the SAO SR.
These were, for example, the following cases:
The Slovak purchaser did not provide any tax in DAP for the fourth quarter of 2004 on the acquisition of goods from EU Member States and did not grant any tax for the tax period from 10 to 12/2004 and claimed an excess VAT deduction totalling SK 1,236 thousand.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation which revealed that the tax entity acquired EUR 683 000 worth of goods from the Czech Republic (approximately SK 27,080 thousand).
These goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to a customs office in the town of Split, where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak customer payer in the Russian Federation issued an invoice for EUR 683 000, which he did not mention in the DAP.
For the tax entity, the tax administration carries out a tax check.
The difference between the acquisition data in the Slovak payer's DAP for Q3 2004 to Q1 2005 and the delivery data reported by EU Member State payers for each quarter totalled SK 4,800 thousand.
The tax office found that the tax entity purchased goods from suppliers from the Czech Republic and Belgium and subsequently sold them to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by export single declarations.
The acquisition of goods in DAP was not indicated by the tax entity. According to the Company Executive, the goods in transit were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine.
The taxpayer submitted no VAT records to the local investigation.
A tax check was initiated on the payer.
5.2 International exchange of information level L3
The exchange of information at L3 level is initiated by locally competent tax administrations, which send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "JHA") or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as "SPI") relating to a particular tax entity or transaction via the MF to the CLO, respectively.
DR CUSTOMS to another EU Member State. The aim of the JHA is, for example, to demonstrate the execution of the transaction in the context of intracommunity transactions, examination of a certain TAC, etc.
The SPI is a communication of information relevant to tax administrations in another EU Member State.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is governed by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum period for replying to the JHA was set out in Article 2 (1) of the basic Regulation. 8 of this Regulation for 3 months.
The conditions for admissibility of applications are laid down in the Commission Decision of 15.11.2004 of the European Communities, which provides that, unless the participating States agree otherwise, the Ryanair must cover commercial transactions worth at least EUR 1,500 net of VAT.
The requested authority may refuse to respond to a commercial transaction worth less than EUR 15,000 net of VAT if the RU relates to a transaction worth less than EUR 10.
The procedure for handling incoming JORs by the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including the indication of internal time limits set for processing at individual organisational levels, illustrates the following diagram.
In the SR, the deadline for the discharge of the JHA by the tax authorities was set at 2 months so that the three-month period under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 could be respected.
From 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005, the MF accepted a total of 29 JHA and 3 SPI.
Of the 29 JHA received, 26 (i.e. 89.7%) were settled within a period of 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10.3%) were settled after that deadline.
In the same period, DR CUSTOMS from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 JHA and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 accepted JHA, 64 (i.e. 90.1%) were settled within a specified period of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were settled after that period (for the other 2 cases it was not possible to determine the time limit of discharge from the submitted materials).
The following chart provides more details on the time of handling of the MFCLO and DR CLO.
The following table contains the reasons for sending the JOI on SCAC forms.
Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT and the use of the VIES system to exchange information between EU Member States have been examined, in particular in monitoring the application of the VAT exemption claim.
International cooperation made it possible to examine selected intracommunitary transactions between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
By examining the selected transactions, it was found that, on the basis of an international exchange of information, the tax administrations of both countries detected cases of companies carrying out fictitious intracommunitarian commercial transactions in order to obtain excessive VAT deductions, as well as cases where the purchasers did not grant VAT on received supplies of goods at the correct amount.
The examination also identified differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of the two countries.
The audit also highlighted problems caused by different reporting of data on intracommunity supplies and acquisitions of goods in individual EU Member States.
A harmonisation of the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would make the control activities of the national tax administrations more effective.
By examining the procedure of the financial or tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system, it was found that the financial or tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all the possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal authorisations.
It was also found that the VIES system did not in all cases provide up-to-date information on the supply of goods and the validity of the registration of tax entities for VAT.
SAO SR compared data on the incidence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the inspection, with data processed after the completion of the inspection.
It was clear from the comparison of these data that the SAO SR control had an effect not only on the reduction of the number of SHs with the erroneously mentioned TS, but also on the reduction of the number of unrepaired errors in the SH.
In the event of irregularities in the reported SAO data, the SAO requested the tax authorities to carry out local investigations and, where appropriate, to carry out tax checks.
The SAO, the Czech Republic did not have such an option under the applicable legislation in the Czech Republic.
The knowledge gained by the control action showed that VIES provided tax administrations with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracommunity transactions.
Given that there remains scope for tax evasion in this area, there is a need for increased attention to be paid to intracommunity transactions when administering VAT.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in the Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Czech Audit Office of the Czech Republic.
Parallel control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material gives an overview of the progress and results of the parallel control actions carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the General Audit Office of the Republic of Slovenia, which were focused on the area of value added management and excise duties.
Cooperation between the Supreme Audit Offices of both countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement in the control activity concluded in February 2004.
The theme of parallel control actions was selected in view of the fact that indirect taxes contribute significantly to the revenues of the national budgets of both countries.
The design of the value added tax, enabling the excess deduction to be recovered, provides room for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise duties, especially on tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean high profits for those who escape taxation by illegally selling these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Due to the need to address this issue comprehensively throughout the European Union, a working group of VAT Working Groups has been set up by the supreme audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union, with the highest audit authorities of both countries actively involved.
The greatest benefits of the audits can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in the joint effort to identify problems in the management of indirect taxes in order to limit the scope for tax evasion.
The experience and knowledge gained will be used in the framework of planned controls on indirect taxes, mainly aimed at involving the tax administrators of both countries in the VIES system, which can control the movement of goods between Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the control of the administration of value added tax and excise duties for 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duties
(SK) Control of the tax administrator's procedures for the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise duties
On 11.2. 2004, a Contract for cooperation in control activities was concluded between the Supreme Audit Office (SAO) and the Czech Audit Office of the Republic (SAO SR). The subject of the contract was cooperation in the implementation of the parallel control actions "Value Added Tax and Excise Duty," included in the SAO's control plan for 2004 under No 04/07, and "Audit of the SAO's practice of the tax administrator in relation to the collection, control and enforcement of value added tax and other taxes," included in the SAO's control activity plan under No. 18/2004
Cooperation consisted of the exchange of information to the extent provided for in the Treaty and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
In the contract, both parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the customs database and from the files of tax entities maintained by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the contracting parties could not obtain when controlling the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the relevant state.
The checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
In the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic"), the control was carried out by the state budget department and the territorial unions of southern Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the Directorate-General of Customs and the 12 selected tax offices: Tax Office for Prague 1, Tax Office for Prague 3, Tax Office in České Budějovice, Tax Office in Frýdk-Místek, Tax Office in Hodonín, Tax Office in Jihlava, Tax Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, Tax Office in Kroměříz, Financial Office in Písko
The inspection on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter "SR") was carried out by the SAO Section of Tax and Customs in cooperation with Exposures of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
Tax department Bratislava for selected tax entities, Tax department Bratislava III, Tax department Trnava, Tax department Pu-breeding, Tax department Banská Bystrica I, Tax department Liptovský Mikuláš, Tax department Žilina I, Tax department Žilina II, Tax department Košice I and
Control objective
The aim of the audits was to examine the fulfilment of the obligations of the financial and/or tax offices and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise duties, focusing on the collection of these taxes in the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of SR and their subsequent verification in tax returns on the relevant financial and tax offices.
The audited period was 2002 and 2003.
2. Recapitulation of control results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
Within the framework of international cooperation of the SAO, the SAO has transferred from the customs database of the Czech Republic 22,206 items of the Uniform Customs Declarations (hereinafter referred to as the "JCD") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and, conversely, the SAO has transmitted to the SAO from the customs database SR 30,221.
A comparison was made between the printed JCD items from the Czech Customs Database and the SR Customs Database.
Out of 5,883 selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic, 43% of related JCD items were assigned.
Of the 12 343 selected JCD items from the SR customs database, a total of 26% of the related JCD items were assigned.
Based on the unassigned items of the JCD, the financial and/or tax offices included a selection of files of tax entities for which the reported imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Based on the exchange of information from the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and the financial and tax authorities, the implementation of reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified in the territory of the other State.
The SAO and the SAO SR carried out a joint pilot inspection at the border crossing point Old Hrozenkov - Drietoma, where both parties cooperated closely in verifying the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The audit did not identify deficiencies in the record of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation enabled the examination of trade transactions between trading partners from both countries and highlighted weaknesses in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of control results
In the field of international cooperation, the SAO and SAO control focused on imports and exports of alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, or other types of goods.
On the basis of a review of the tax records of selected financial and tax authorities, the SAO requested verification of the realization of exports of goods reported at 40 JCD totalling CZK 15,301,093 and the SAO SR to verify exports at a statistical value of SK 56,989.
The SAO and the SAO have identified, inter alia, the following:
- commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the SR,
- error in entering data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- for certain exports from the Czech Republic, the corresponding imports to the SR have not been demonstrated.
In these cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of undue application of value added tax deductions,
- tax entities have failed to comply with certain obligations laid down by law in the reporting of imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- weaknesses have been identified in the activities of the financial and tax offices in the administration of value added tax and excise duties and in their cooperation with the customs authorities.
In the area of value added tax and excise duties, international trade will continue to need to be addressed in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activities of tax administrations in the administration of value added tax.
The basis for effective control of excise duties is control of the circulation of documents, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information on import and export of goods.
3. Description of the situation in the field of value added tax and excise duties
Value Added Tax
Value added tax (VAT) was levied by the financial and/or tax authorities on taxable transactions effected domestically and by the customs authorities on importation of goods.
The tax revenues were due to the difference between the tax liability collected and the excess VAT deductions recovered.
VAT revenues at customs offices were given by the amount of their tax collected.
The tax collected by the customs authorities, in accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, was reflected in the tax deductions applied to the financial and tax offices.
For most financial and tax authorities, excessive VAT deductions exceeded tax obligations.
VAT is one of the flagship taxes in terms of revenue of the state budget, as it accounted for approximately 31% of the tax revenue of the Czech state budget in 2003 and approximately 42% of the tax revenue of the state budget of SR.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic reached CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The tax and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions refunded totalled CZK 231.4 billion.
The total VAT collection in Slovakia totalled SK 83.8 billion in 2003.
Tax and customs authorities collected SK $187.0 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions were reimbursed totalling SK $103.2 billion.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (SPD) was carried out by the relevant financial and/or tax authorities and the customs authorities when importing products subject to SPD.
SpD's share of state budget tax revenues in the Czech Republic was approximately 16% in 2003 and about 19% in the Slovak Republic.
The total collection of SPD collected in the Czech Republic by the financial and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to CZK 85.6 billion and in the Slovak Republic amounted to Sk 38.0 billion.
4. Progress of the control action
Cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR took place in two stages.
The first stage included a comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia. In the second stage, the results of this comparison were used to verify the implementation of selected commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and SR.
4.1.
Preparation of the control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel checks of VAT and SPD was presented at a working meeting of representatives of SAO and SAO SR in April 2003.
A coordination meeting was held in November 2003, where the selection of commodities - the types of goods which posed a significant risk in compliance with customs and tax rules - was agreed, inter alia: - alcohol and spirits, tariff items Nos 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff items No.2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff subheadings No 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff subheadings No 8525,20,91,8525,20,99,8529,90,40.
Both parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out: (a) from unassigned items found by comparison of exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and SR, (b) from entities carrying out imports and exports on a regular or one-off basis in large volumes, (c) based on findings from controls carried out by selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
In the first stage, the JCD item assignment mechanism registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR was tested on the sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002.
Subsequently, part of the exports from the Czech Republic were compared with imports into the Slovak Republic for 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
- 2207 Undenatured ethyl alcohol with an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol. or more; ethyl alcohol and other distillates denatured, of any alcoholic strength,
- 2208 Undenatured ethyl alcohol with an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% vol; distillates, liqueurs and other spirit drinks,
- 2401 Unprocessed tobacco; tobacco waste,
- 2402 Cigars (whether or not with cut-off ends), cigarillos and cigarettes of tobacco or tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other tobacco products and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and punishments (essence),
- 8525 20 91 Transmitters containing reception equipment: For cellular network (mobile phones),
- 8525 20 99 Transmitters containing reception equipment: Other,
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling within subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
The JCD entries from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia were assigned to each other on the basis of the conformity of the individual paragraphs of the JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration mark of the vehicle carrying the cargo, date of crossing the national border, tariff entry, etc.).
The results of the comparison are presented in the following tables and graphs.
Inter alia, the fact that commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides made it difficult to assign individual imports and exports.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic declared in one export JCD were declared in the Slovak Republic for several import JCDs, or the export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors that affected the success of the assignment were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia, as well as the time shift between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the registration of corresponding imports in the customs database of the other country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at the audited financial and tax offices.
Priority was given to certain tax entities that made imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, which could not be identified in both databases.
In addition, some tax entities were collected to verify the transactions reported in the VAT tax returns for which data on imports and exports between the Czech Republic and SR were found in both databases.
Pilot control at the border crossing point Old Hrozenkov-Drietoma
The border customs crossing for pilot inspection was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of unassigned JCD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and SR.
On the basis of a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and SR, the use of checkpoints has been introduced at border crossing points between the Czech Republic and SR since 1.6.1998.
