The aim of this measure was to eliminate customs and tax evasion as far as possible, to ensure an overview of the movements of commercial goods in the customs area and to create conditions for cross-comparison of customs records.
The joint pilot inspection was carried out between 8.3.2004 and 26.3.2004 and aimed at verifying this customs control system.
Procedure for the use of checkpoints at the Old Hrozenkov-Drietoma border crossing point:
1) Weighing the vehicle, issuing the check sheet and giving it to the driver.
2) Weaning of the vehicle in the indicated sector in the parking lot.
Customs discussion in the check-in hall by the Police of the Czech Republic, the Police of Slovakia, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic.
The check-in process was confirmed by individual components by stamping on the checklist.
3) Attachment of the vehicle to the physical inspection area.
Presentation of the certificate of inspection, JCD, or other documents to a customs official, as appropriate - checking the execution of all the prescribed acts and documents.
Carrying out physical checks by the relevant constituents.
Release of the vehicle from the customs compartment.
Pozru: When the goods were imported into the Czech Republic, weighted vehicles were carried out directly by the staff of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
When the goods were imported into the SR, the weighted vehicles were carried out by staff of the authorised legal person.
The vehicles were registered in computer records after weighing.

4.4 Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
Within the framework of international cooperation, the implementation of imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia was verified on the basis of customs administrations and financial and tax offices in the territory of the other state.
For selected tax entities:
- whether the submitted JCDs were registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia,
- fulfilment of the legal conditions for the application of the VAT deduction on importation, the reimbursement of excessive VAT deduction and the application of the VAT exemption on export.
Verifying business transactions revealed:
1. SAO SR requested verification of the realization of the export of alcohol in the statistical value of 56,989 Sk.
The SAO identified corresponding imports in the customs database of the Czech Republic at a statistical value of 42,624 CZK.
2. The Company involved in the import and export of photographic equipment and accessories applied an excessive VAT deduction of CZK 3,740,664 for the month of December 2002.
In order to check the reported exports from the Czech Republic, the SAO selected 3 JCDs (16 items) at a statistical value of CZK 1,274,822.
The SAO SR has identified 3 corresponding import JCDs (17 items) at a statistical value of SK 1 724 321.
VAT was paid in SR to the competent customs office.
3. The Company, which was mainly engaged in the business of optical equipment, applied a total excess VAT deduction of CZK 4,1,36,000 higher than the tax liability in 2002.
To verify the reported business activity, the SAO selected an export JCD (32 items) with a statistical value of CZK 7,154,124.
The SAO SR found that this JCD corresponds to the import JCD (12 items) with a statistical value of 9,653,827 Sk.
VAT was paid in SR to the competent customs office.
4. The company engaged in, inter alia, the purchase of goods for resale and sale did not declare any exports of goods in the tax returns submitted in 2002 and 2003.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 totalled CZK 3,439,888.
On this basis, the SAO selected 5 export JCDs (5 items) in total statistical value of CZK 669,839 for verification.
SAO SR has identified 5 corresponding import JCDs (5 items) at a statistical value of 1,012,656 Sk.
The audit of the SAO SR at the competent tax office demonstrated the implementation of the declared imports and payment of VAT.
5. The Company, which included the purchase of goods for resale and the sale, production, installation and repair of electrical machinery and equipment, reported exports of goods worth CZK 12,966,706 in 2002 in VAT returns.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, in 2002 the total value of exports was CZK 14,474,381.
The SAO submitted 17 export JCDs (59 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,975,122.
The SAO SR has identified in the customs database SR 13 JCD (50 items) the statistical value of 3 621 370 Sk.
The SLOVAK customs database failed to identify the corresponding import JCD to 4 export JCDs (9 items) totalling CZK 399,776.
The competent tax authority in the SR verified these imports with the tax entity.
The tax entity listed on the JCD as an importer in the SR stated in the local investigation that imports declared on the Czech export JCD were not realised.
The SAO SR therefore requested the local competent tax authority to carry out a tax check on VAT and corporate tax for the 2002 and 2003 tax years.
6. According to the Customs Database of the Czech Republic, the company involved in importing and selling cigarettes exported tobacco stickers with a statistical value of CZK 7,338,199 in 2002 and a statistical value of CZK 12,228,545 in 2003.
No exports were recorded in the 2002 and 2003 VAT returns.
The SAO selected 5 export JCDs (5 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,471,598 for verification.
To 4 export JCDs (4 items) totalling CZK 2,246,860, the SAO SR identified in the customs database SR 7 JCD (7 items) a statistical value of SK 2,919,514.
The export JCD (1 item) totalling CZK 224,738 could not be assigned to the corresponding imports in the SR customs database.
7. The software company did not declare exports of goods in the VAT returns for 2002 and 2003.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 and 2003 totalled CZK 1,630,198.
The SAO selected 9 JCDs (9 items) for verification in the total statistical value of CZK 755,588.
In the customs database of SR SAO SR, 8 JCDs (8 items) identified a statistical value of 915 601 Sk.
The export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 68 286 could not be assigned corresponding imports in the SR customs database.
In these cases, the customs database SR failed to identify the corresponding imports to 6 JCDs at a statistical value of CZK 692,800.
Of which:
- on 2 export JCDs from the customs database of the Czech Republic with a statistical value of CZK 293,024, the customs database of SR failed to identify the corresponding import JCD (see paragraphs 6 and 7).
Due to a certain error in entering data into the customs database, it was not possible to identify certain registered imports, e.g. in cases where the name of the importer was missing or an error in the tax identification number ("TIER").
It is therefore not possible to state with certainty that these exports did not materialise.
- on 4 export JCDs from the customs database of the Czech Republic, imports corresponding to exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic were not proven at a statistical value of CZK 399,776 (see paragraph 5).
In such cases, suspicion of fictitious export of goods for the purpose of undue application of the VAT deduction is justified.
5. Control of imports and exports of goods and services under the control of selected financial and tax authorities
5.1. Control sample
In order to verify the fulfilment of the obligations of tax authorities on imports and exports of goods and services and to evaluate the level of cooperation between the financial and customs authorities, the files of the tax entities were collected at the audited financial and tax offices in accordance with the following criteria:
1st tax entities were collected from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia: (a) with the highest import volume, (b) with the highest amount of VAT, (c) with the highest export volume,
Tax entities were collected from the financial and/or tax offices according to the amount: (a) VAT deductions applied on importation, (b) excessive VAT deductions applied, (c) the right to refund the SPD, (d) the VAT exemption applied on export,
3 tax entities where the tax check has been carried out.
Sampling was carried out irrespective of the country of destination, focusing on risk commodities.
5.2. Control findings in the Czech Republic
An overview of imports into the Czech Republic and exports from the Czech Republic for risk commodities in 2002 and 2003 is given in the following table:
5.2.1. Control of the selected sample at the financial offices
The SAO focused on:
- the procedure of the financial authorities to verify the accuracy of VAT declared,
- cooperation between the tax authorities and the customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with the JCD database at the tax offices with a view to comparing the declared value, applying the correct VAT rate following the classification of goods or services, etc. comparison of data on the JCD and accompanying invoices with data in the customs database,
- a comparison of VAT return data on transactions effected and received from abroad with data in the JCD database at the tax offices or in the customs database,
- the method of verifying the right to VAT exemption when goods or services are exported abroad,
- a comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services provided declared in VAT returns with the data from the customs database.
The JCD database at the tax authorities contained only records of those imports and exports for which tax entities were obliged to place imports or exports on the tax return.
The audited financial offices examined the files of tax entities which showed total imports totalling CZK 60,396,379 thousand in VAT returns in the years 2002 and 2003 and corresponding VAT totalling CZK 12,644,052 thousand.
In addition, the records of tax entities reporting exports totalling CZK 47,33,111 were checked in the 2002 and 2003 tax returns.
Tax entities for which imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia were examined, according to the Czech Customs Database in 2002 and 2003 imports into the Czech Republic from the Slovak Republic totalling CZK 3,759,352 thousand, VAT of CZK 767,607 and exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic with a total statistical value of CZK 1,989,090 thousand.
The differences found between the records in the JCD database at the tax offices and in the customs database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- JCD items missing from the customs database of the Czech Republic were requested directly by the Directorate-General of Customs of the Czech Republic,
- for JCD items missing from the database of financial authorities, it has been verified that they are not cancelled documents,
- for items of the JCD for which different values were found between the customs database of the Czech Republic and the database of the financial authorities, they were requested by the Directorate-General of Customs of the Czech Republic to the relevant JCD in writing, including the invoices attached.
The examination revealed that the JCD database at the tax offices did not contain, for example, records of import JCD totalling CZK 3,622 thousand and export JCD records totalling CZK 9,359 thousand.
5.2.1.1. Differences detected
By comparing the JCD database at the tax authorities and the accumulated tax liabilities for 2002 and 2003 in the VAT returns of the selected sample, the following differences were found:
Differences in values were mainly due to:
- A time shift between the realization of imports and the application of the right to deduct VAT charged on imports of goods.
The taxpayer could claim a deduction for the importation of goods within 3 years of the end of the tax period during which the goods were placed under the relevant procedure or, in the case of temporary importation, no later than 3 years after the end of the tax period during which the scheme was terminated.
- The time shift between the realisation of exports and the moment when the tax entity received the JCD.
The taxpayer was obliged to provide information on exports made exempt from the obligation to apply the output tax on the VAT return at the earliest for the tax period in which the goods left the country, provided that it also had the tax document which was the JCD.
- Failure to fulfil the obligations of tax entities to report imports and exports in VAT returns.
In some cases, tax entities did not provide correct data on imports and exports on VAT returns.
As tax entities did not have to attach the JCD lists to the VAT returns submitted, it was difficult to check the right to deduct VAT or VAT exemption from the tax authorities.
5.2.2. Synergies between financial and customs authorities
In the audited period, import or export duties and VAT were repaid or remitted at the discretion of the customs authorities.
Tax entities were obliged by law to reduce the previously claimed VAT deduction entitlement by the amount of tax refunded by the customs office in the tax return for the period during which the tax was refunded.
No legislation provided for the sending of information on changes in customs duty and VAT to tax offices.
Some audited tax authorities received this information, but irregularly or with considerable time delays and only from certain customs offices.
One audited tax authority did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office did not receive information on the changes in the amount of customs duty and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the information needed to check compliance with the legal obligation on tax entities.
In 2002, the customs authorities refunded more than 319 million VAT. CZK and in 2003 in the amount of over 398 million. CZK.
The results of the audit highlighted persistent shortcomings in the activities of tax administrations, some systemic errors in the cooperation of tax authorities with customs authorities and the failure to fulfil certain obligations of taxpayers filing VAT and SPD tax returns.
When administering VAT and SPD, weaknesses were identified in particular in the following areas:
a) when VAT registrations were cancelled, the fulfilment of the payers' obligation to pay VAT on commercial assets registered or to be registered at the date of the cancellation of the registration for which the payer applied the tax deduction was only rarely verified,
b) the tax authorities did not consistently use the possibility of tax checks or local investigations.
This has in some cases underestimated the legitimacy of the right to deduct VAT,
(c) the official records and oral protocols did not contain all the necessary data to demonstrate the legitimacy of the excessive VAT deductions applied,
d) the tax authorities did not adequately verify imports and exports declared in VAT returns.
5.3. Control findings in SR
5.3.1. Check of selected sample at tax offices
For the selected sample, the SAO has verified or the tax office has carried out a tax check for the 2002 and 2003 tax years.
After analysing tax returns and refund requests for selected tax entities of the SAO SR, the Tax Office requested that the relevant JCDs attest to imports and exports, invoices and proof of payment of tax.
Subsequently, SAO SR checked whether the submitted JCDs were registered in the customs database of imports and exports and fulfilled the decisive facts and legal conditions by applying the deduction of the entry tax on imports, the refund of the excess VAT deduction, the application of the export tax exemption and the refund of the SPD.
SAO SR verified selected cases of imports and exports of goods between SR and CR in 10 audited tax offices in the structure according to the JCD headings and the sum of statistical values listed in the table below.
Total imports at a statistical value of 856,2 million were checked. SK, representing 5,11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic into the SROV.
Exports of selected commodities were checked at a total statistical value of 176 million. Sk, which represents 6.87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from SR to the Czech Republic.
In addition, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white equipment, packaging equipment and software) from the EU States to the Slovak Republic were checked for a total statistical value of 532.8 million. Sk.
5.3.2. Synergies between tax and customs authorities
The SAO SR found irregularities at the tax offices between data recorded in the SR customs database and data reported in specific VAT returns, such as:
- 2 tax entities (natural persons) indicated in their tax returns imports of goods totalling Sk 1 589 261, on the basis of which they claimed the refund of excessive VAT deductions.
In the local investigations carried out at the initiative of the SAO SR, the tax authorities were unable to prove to the tax office the legitimacy of the application of the entry tax by the relevant evidence of the importation and payment of VAT,
- the tax entity (s. r. o.) in the tax return for the tax year January 2003 declared the taxable transactions received in the value of 77 167 576 Sk, the export of goods in the value of 18 006 041 Sk and applied an excess VAT deduction of 17 157 101 Sk.
The 2003 VAT returns show that the difference between the purchase and export volumes of Sk 59 161 535 incurred in January 2003 was not offset throughout 2003.
In the abovementioned cases, the SAO SR requested the competent tax authorities to carry out a tax check on the excessive VAT deductions applied.
- in another case, the tax entity (s. r. o.) for the tax period January to June 2002 indicated in the VAT returns the export of goods totalling 87 199 Sk.
The verification in the SR customs database revealed that the tax entity carried out exports at a statistical value of Sk 296 747 during that period.
The Tax Office carried out multiple local investigations at the company's head office, finding that the company manager (a UK citizen) had travelled and that the company had left the leased premises without terminating the lease in August 2002.
At the time of auditing the SAO, the tax administrator filed a complaint with the law enforcement authorities on suspicion of a non-tax offence.
On the basis of the results of the audit at selected tax offices, the SAO notes that the main problems in the administration and control of VAT and SPD occurred mainly in the following areas:
- not making use of the possibility of carrying out VAT tax checks on problematic tax entities, in particular in cases where excessive VAT deductions are applied,
- the tax control protocols did not contain an inventory of the audited documents
- JCD when importing and exporting goods,
- insufficient verification of reported imports and exports of goods in tax returns,
- lengthy management of tax administrations in the issuing of decisions, in particular in the context of the assessment procedure, as well as the termination of the right to sanction,
- non-compliance with the legal conditions for granting deferrals,
- the non-offsetting of VAT arrears within the time limit for the refund of the excess VAT deduction,
- insufficient use of all forms of security and recovery of tax arrears.
Based on the audit of the SAO's deficiencies, the competent tax authorities requested VAT to be reviewed, focusing on the justification of the excessive VAT deductions applied to 14 tax entities.
Measures have been taken at all audited tax offices to remedy the deficiencies identified, which the SAO will monitor and control.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation enabled the examination of trade transactions between trading partners from both countries and highlighted weaknesses in the registration of imports and exports.
The checks also resulted in the identification of persistent deficiencies in the fulfilment of the obligations of VAT and SPD payers, in the activities of the financial and tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs authorities, which ultimately reduced the efficiency and efficiency of tax controls.
The lessons learned also showed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have basic data on imports and exports from the customs database of the Czech Republic. In the SR, there is no similar system of transmission of information on imports and exports of goods between the customs and tax administrations.
The procedure for verifying the performance of VAT and SPD administration was not identical due to different legislation and conditions in the territory of both States.
The SAO verified the necessary data from the information obtained from the customs administration of the Czech Republic and from the supporting documents available at the audited financial offices. SAO SR verified the execution of commercial transactions from documents of tax entities requested through tax offices.
If irregularities were found, he asked the tax authorities to carry out tax checks.
The parallel VAT and SPD checks carried out assessed the state of administration of these taxes in the period prior to accession to the European Union and highlighted the need for further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will be further deepened in the control of the activities of the financial and tax authorities in connection with the adoption of the new VAT Act.
One of the new obligations related to the delivery of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of a summary report.
This declaration must be made by all VAT payers who have delivered goods to another Member State to a person registered for VAT in another Member State.
Tax administrations are obliged to enter data from summary reports into the VAT Information Exchange System (VIES), to which tax administrations from the Member States of the European Union have access.
The financial and/or tax authorities are then able to compare these data with those given in the tax returns filed.
This system is also used to verify the validity of VAT registrants, to verify the lawfulness of the VAT exemption applied when goods are delivered to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel control actions showed the possibilities of cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR.
The results of these control actions will be confronted with the outputs of the forthcoming control actions, which will focus, among other things, on screening the VIES system to prevent tax evasion in so-called "intracommunity supplies."
Given the importance of VAT and SPD for budgetary revenues, control activities need to be focused primarily on monitoring and identifying risk areas in order to limit the scope for tax evasion in indirect taxes.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Czech Audit Office.
Report on the results of inspections at asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
State property and funds intended to safeguard the activities of the Refugee Facilities Administration of the Ministry of the Interior
Control Action No. 04/23 "State Property and Funds for Securing the Activities of the Refugee Facilities Administration of the Ministry of the Interior"
Control Action No 15/2004 "Control of the economy with assets and financial provisions intended for asylum and temporary refuge in the Slovak Republic"
1. Introduction
Population migration is one of the phenomena of a global nature and has become an inseparable part of the current development phase of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Its main cause is the escape of citizens from the country of origin or last permanent residence from persecution, in particular for reasons of racial, religious, national, political, as well as the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
They aim to gain asylum and integration into society, especially in one of Europe's advanced democratic countries.
The large group is also composed of foreigners whose reasons for migration are unfavourable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The adoption of the 1951 Geneva Agreement and the 1967 New York Protocol on the Status of Refugees, by which the governments of the signatory countries undertook to apply them in their foreign-policy orientation, has already produced concrete principles for helping refugees.
The Czech and Slovak Federative Republics ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
Both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic declared their position on the refugee issue after the division in 1993 by continuing to implement the adopted international documents and confirmed their binding in the framework of national legislation by means of a legal act.
Both republics have enshrined asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the International Audit Office of the Republic were focused on the asylum process and related issues, the results of which are contained in the joint final report.
Cooperation between the Supreme Audit Offices of both countries was carried out on the basis of the "Surveillance Cooperation Treaty" ("the Treaty") concluded in April 2004.
In the Treaty, both Parties undertook to provide each other with information on the legislation governing asylum procedures in the State of the other Party, selected statistics on the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as on asylum facilities.
The aim of the parallel control action was to identify the same problem lines and highlight the implications for the area of population migration.
Cooperation consisted of the alignment of the programme of control actions, the exchange of information to the extent provided for by the Treaty and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
The first joint meeting, which took place between 5.4 and 7.4.2004, established the same categories of controlled issues and control procedures for the preparation of control actions.
The second meeting, which took place between 28.6 and 30.6. 2004, clarified the common points for the control action programme.
The third joint meeting, which took place during the control action from 8.11 to 10.11.2004, exchanged experiences from ongoing inspections.
The forms of outputs from the checks have been specified and the structure and content of the joint final report drawn up at the last joint meeting on 14 February to 17 February 2005 have been provisionally established.
The checks were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, inspectors of the Department of Defence and Security and selected territorial unions carried out the inspection.
The audited persons were the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as "MV") and the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as "SUZ").
In the Slovak Republic carried out the control of the defence section, the army and the Czech Republic.
The audited body was the Migration Department of the Ministry of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Ministry of Education").
The audited period was 2001, 2002, 2003 (the audited period).
In some cases, statistics for a longer period of time are also used in the joint report.
2. Recapitulation of control results
2.1. Evaluation of control activities
The subject of parallel checks was: - asylum process, - asylum facilities, - management of funds and state property, - internal control system.
The mutual exchange of experience between the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Czech Audit Office of the Czech Republic took place during the preparation and implementation of the control actions.
This exchange enabled a more thorough evaluation of the evidence submitted, analysing the causes of the detected differences in securing the asylum process.
This made it possible to concentrate on the critical problems affecting the activities of asylum facilities.
Ultimately, this positively affected the quality of the performance of the control activity.
2.2 Summary of control results
The harmonisation of the asylum law of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with European Union documents ("the EU") has been the subject of evaluation reports by the European Commission on the preparedness of both countries to join the EU.
The adoption of legislation on this issue is continuing after both countries have joined the EU with a view to further harmonisation with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants is on a steadily growing trend, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security for asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements.
The national budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the national budget of both countries is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the granting or granting of asylum and also by the state of health of the applicants.
The amount of some selected doses is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic established asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of the parties to asylum proceedings.
Asylum facilities provide asylum seekers with accommodation, food, healthcare and basic material and hygiene supplies during their stay.
At the same time, leisure activities are organised and conditions for cultural and sporting activities are created for applicants.
Asylum facilities include reception centres and residential centres, in the Czech Republic and integration centres.
The cost per day depends on the Centre's occupancy and equipment and is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is in principle stabilised.
In the Slovak Republic, it is projected to increase by almost 1,000 seats in the next two years.
The aim is to create conditions for applicants, which are expected to continue to apply the Dublin Convention for years to come.
In the Czech Republic, the highest proportion of approved budgetary expenditure was spent on security of services. The decisive expenditure of this item was expenditure on accommodation and catering of applicants in asylum facilities operated on the basis of a contract, expenditure on healthcare provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service ensuring the protection of asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work carried out and premiums contributed significantly to the overall expenditure.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of migration policy and the asylum process was marked by many budgetary measures that addressed legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and premiums, expenditure on materials and services and expenditure on security services contributed decisively to the absorption of current expenditure.
The results of the audits in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings that did not have a major impact on the financial management and management of state property.
These were weaknesses in particular in the use of State budget resources contrary to the purpose for which they were determined by the State Budget Act when current expenditure covered actions having the character of technical evaluation of long-term tangible assets.
The Accounting Act in the area of inventory and non-compliance with the accounting curriculum was also violated.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies in the handling of state property were also identified when it was left for use by another person without a contract.
Failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in land registry data violated the Land Registry Act and leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not a person entitled to waste management violated the Waste Act.
In the Slovak Republic, shortcomings in the provision of disproportionately high reserves for the consumption of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in public procurement and the management of State property were also identified when its records were not adequately secured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not proven.
The internal control system was ensured in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic within the meaning of the generally binding legislation governing the way financial control is carried out.
The submitted written dossier did not identify deficiencies.
Despite some deficiencies identified, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic have positively assessed the procedure of the SUZ and the MU in providing services for asylum seekers.
Based on the knowledge gained during the inspection, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic's Supervisory Authority note that despite a significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the relevant organisational units of both countries have managed the tasks associated with the care of asylum seekers at the appropriate level.
The evaluation shows that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the audit were discussed with interested statutory representatives of the relevant organizational units of the state on the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the inspection, we recommend that positive methodological experience from control be used in other joint control actions within the framework of international cooperation of supreme audit institutions.
3. Legislative framework
In both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, asylum law is based on the 1951 Geneva Convention (the Refugee Status Convention followed by the 1967 New York Protocol).
The first legislation was implemented by Act No. 498/1990 Coll., on refugees.
Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum and Amending Act No. 83/1991 Coll., on the Police of the Czech Republic, has been effective in the Czech Republic since 1 January 2000.
This Act was amended five times (Act No. 2/2002 Coll., Act No. 217/2002 Coll., Act No. 320/2002 Coll., Act No. 519/2002 Coll. and Act No. 222/2003 Coll.).
Two other amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, are currently in the legislative process and the adoption of further amendments will be linked to European legislation.
At the time of the Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum, asylum was part of the third pillar of the EU and asylum documents were binding political documents.
The adoption of this law already sought to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
A major change for asylum policy within the EU was the shift of asylum from the 3rd to the 1st pillar, when asylum law became part of Community law from 1.5. 1999 on the basis of the Treaty of Amsterdam.
This shift has created the need to create appropriate legislation, i.e. to create legal instruments in the appropriate legal obligation.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents has been the subject of regular evaluation reports by the European Commission.
Key Community regulations in the field of asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic entered the EU and their transposition period at the time of Supreme Audit Office inspection, the Czech Republic has not yet expired.
After their implementation into the Czech legal order, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission how it transposed.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure of state authorities in the procedure for granting refugee status and determining the obligations of foreigners who have applied for refugee status or who have been granted temporary refuge in the Slovak Republic was laid down by Law No 283/1995 of the National Council of the Slovak Republic with effect from 1.1.1996. z., the fugitive.
Since 2003, the Refugee Act has been replaced by Act No 480/2002 Z. "on asylum and amending and supplementing certain laws, incorporating the harmonisation of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with the Council of Europe Directive 2001/55/ES from the 20.7.2001 on minimum standards for the granting of temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote a balance of efforts between Member States to recruit such persons and to endure the resulting consequences.
Following two amendments to Act No 480/2002 of the Asylum Act 2003 and 2004, a third amendment was approved in early 2005, which means further harmonisation of the law of the Slovak Republic with EU legislation on migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the obligation for asylum seekers to attend a course on the basis of Slovak language during their stay in the integration centre, the appointment of a guardian by the courts of unaccompanied foreigners if they are staying in the territory of the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, allowing applicants to enter into an employment relationship in certain circumstances, as specified in the amendment to the law.
The harmonisation of Slovak Republic law with EU law in the field of migration and asylum process was assessed in regular reports by the European Commission on preparedness for accession of the Slovak Republic to the EU.
In 2002, the report drew attention to the insufficient personnel capacity of the Ministry of Education, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. Asylum process
In the Czech Republic, since 1990, matters relating to refugees fall within the competence of the MV.
With effect from 1.1.1996, the MV established the organisational arm of the SUZ State. This was due to the separation of State Administration's enforcement of the asylum procedure, which is carried out through the MV Department of Asylum and Migration Policy, from the provision of services to asylum seekers.
The task of the SUZ is to provide accommodation, catering, health and other services to participants in asylum and asylum procedures.
In the Slovak Republic, they carry out decisive tasks in the field of the MA asylum process, in particular in terms of financial and material-technical security of the asylum process to the extent defined by specific regulations.
Priority tasks are issues related to the decision-making of aliens' applications for asylum in the I. the level of administrative management and the comprehensive operation of asylum facilities in the areas of accommodation, catering, health, financial and material security of asylum seekers.
In addition, it develops concepts for the migration policy of the state.
Cooperation and support from the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR) has significantly affected the results achieved in the area of asylum system development in the Slovak Republic in recent years.
His financial participation in the reconstruction of the asylum housing stock was of particular benefit.
The UNHCR also co-financed social, cultural and sporting activities for applicants.
4.1 Development of the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the chart.
A significant increase occurred in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis and in 2003 the number of refugees from Chechnya increased.
For an overview of the results of the asylum procedure in the Czech Republic, see Table 1.
A total of 394 cases were granted asylum in the audited period, including 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 in 2003.
A total of 22,731 cases were not granted asylum in the audited period and 22,636 cases were terminated.
The number of parties to the 1 January proceedings shall comprise both those to whom the decision has not yet been taken and those to whom the decision has not been transmitted.
It also includes persons who have been forgiven for missing the time limit for lodging an appeal, or who have been annulled and have not yet been issued with a new decision.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers is on a steadily growing trend.
If 96 applicants were registered in 1993, it was already 10,358 in 2003.
A significant increase in the number of applicants occurred in 2001, when 8,131 applicants were registered, an increase of 423% compared to 2000, in which 1,556 persons applied for asylum.
The results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic during the audited period are shown in Table 2.
A total of 49 asylums were granted in the audited period and did not exceed 0.22% of the registered number of applicants in each year.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
The asylum procedure was terminated in a total of 23,088 cases.
A large proportion of applicants, by staying outside the asylum facility without authorisation, voluntarily left the asylum procedure before closing.
In 2002, it accounted for more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants and by more than 94% in 2003.
The length of stay of one applicant in one of the asylum facilities, converted into an average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The MÚ's findings also show that most applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic are seeking better living conditions, i.e. economic migration, which is not supported by documents adopted by the international community, to which the Slovak Republic also applied.
In such cases, the asylum system is used for a purpose by the applicant.
An application for asylum based on economic reasons, such as seeking employment or better living conditions, is not grounds for granting asylum.
Such a request should be in accordance with the provisions of § 12 clause. 1 font. a) Act No 480/2002 Z. z., on asylum, assessed as manifestly unfounded and should be decided within 30 days.
Internationally recognised principles to identify economic migrants are not yet established to distinguish them from applicants persecuted in their country of origin and to speed up the asylum process.
In view of the above, it can be concluded that the Slovak Republic is a transit country from the point of view of international migration and the destination countries of migration are and remain Western European States.
After joining the EU, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic acceded to the Agreement designating the State responsible for examining asylum applications lodged in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents the submission of multiple special purpose asylum applications in several EU countries.
Applicants shall return to the country of first registration after positive identification in EURODAC.
The Slovak Republic is part of the EU's external borders, therefore the application of the Dublin Convention may result in an increase in the number of applicants who will need to establish conditions for residence in the Slovak Republic until a decision on granting or not granting asylum is taken.
4.2 Use of funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security to asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements and national legislative provisions based thereon.
The national budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the final decision granting asylum and their health status.
The increasing number of persons entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the increased use of statutory benefits for applicants, such as expenditure on food, pocket money, expenditure on basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
The amount of some selected doses is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic during the audited period the meals were 58 CZK per person per day, 12 CZK per person per day and 6 CZK per child under 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per day was on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
In addition to pocket money, asylum seekers staying in residential centres with separate cooking and applicants staying privately outside asylum facilities may be granted a contribution of up to a minimum of life.
Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, as amended, inter alia, grants the municipalities a right in Section 84 of the Municipality to pay the costs incurred in connection with the asylum facility in its territory.
The amount of the contribution was determined annually by government resolutions and during the audited period amounted to CZK 7 per person per stay day.
At the same time, municipalities are entitled to a contribution to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools attended by asylum seekers.
The amount of the allowance was CZK 120 per pupil per month in the audited period provided that in the given month the student attended the school for a minimum of 10 days.
In the Slovak Republic, in the controlled period, the meals were 70 Sk per person per day, the allowance was 12 Sk per person per day and 8 Sk per child under 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per stay day averaged 442 Sk in 2001, 447 Sk in 2002 and 445 Sk in 2003.
The municipalities in whose territory the asylum facility is located comply with Law No 480/2002 Z. from., on asylum, an allowance is granted for the partial reimbursement of expenditure incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and activities of the asylum facility.
The municipalities have so far only partially used the possibility to apply for a contribution of Sk 1,500 per bed and calendar year.
National legislation in both countries for issuing asylum decisions provides for a 90-day period from the start of the asylum procedure while allowing, where justified, an extension of that period.
The most common reason for the extension of the asylum procedure, which affects the amount of expenditure of the state budget, is the lodging of appeals against the decision not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days of the date of the asylum application (17.61%).
In total, 73% of asylum procedures opened in 2001-2003 were finally decided within one year of their initiation.
Within two years of the opening of the asylum procedure, 92% of asylum applications were finally decided.
In the Slovak Republic, according to MÚ data, up to 90% of applicants who have not been granted asylum use the statutory possibility of extending the time limit by bringing an appeal to court.
In some cases it was an extension of more than a year and at the time of the auditing the proceedings were not terminated in court.
A certain benefit in the shortening of asylum procedures is expected from the establishment of joint workplaces of the Ministry of Education and Labour of the Police Corps in reception centres in Adam-Gbeloch, Opatovský Nový Vsi and Liptovské Vlachoch, which was acceded to at the time of the inspection from the 1.10.2004.
This foresees simplifying procedures and shortening the time limits for proceedings between the two elements of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic established asylum facilities in which they gradually created appropriate conditions for the provision of services to participants in asylum proceedings.
Asylum facilities provide asylum seekers with accommodation, catering, healthcare, pocket and basic material equipment and hygiene supplies during their stay.
At the same time, leisure courses are organized and conditions for cultural and sporting activities are created for applicants.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
The SUZ manages and operates asylum facilities and is responsible for managing the state property in the reception centre of Vyšní Loti, the reception and residence centre of Červý Újchod, the residential centres of Bělá-Jezová, the Stop near Brno, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and in the buildings of integration
At the beginning of 2002, a reception centre was established in the transit area of Prague-Ruzyně Airport.
The SUZ also provides for the operation of asylum facilities in Strážž pod Ralskem, Seči, Bruntál, Zbyšov and Kasava, which are operated by a legal person pursuant to § 80 para. 3 Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of reception centres is 747 seats and the total accommodation capacity of the accommodation centres is 1,977 seats.
Reception centres are closed establishments that asylum seekers may not leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic reception operations referred to in Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum are carried out.
A breach of the obligation to reside in a reception centre shall be regarded as an offence.
Residential centres where asylum seekers arrive from reception centres shall be used to accommodate asylum seekers until a decision on their application for asylum has become legally effective.
Under certain conditions, asylum seekers have the option of leaving or staying in private residences.
Asylum seekers shall have the right to free accommodation, provision of meals, other services and allowances in the reception and residence centres in which they are declared to be resident, provided that they have endured the operations necessary to establish their financial and property circumstances, and such conditions are such that they cannot be fairly required to partially reimburse those services.
Integration centres shall be used for the temporary accommodation of persons granted asylum.
Clients are accommodated in the Centre on the basis of an accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months with the possibility of extension until they manage to provide adequate housing or secure it themselves under the state integration programme.
In the integration centre, clients pay for all accommodation costs and cater individually.
Persons with granted refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1 Costs of asylum facilities
To compare asylum facilities, it was chosen as the best indicator of the cost per physical stay day.
It is based on the actual number of people who have actually been provided with the services provided by the asylum facility every day.
In Table 3 and chart, the SUZ-operated facilities are identified as owned and operated by legal entities pursuant to Section 80 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum, as contractual.
The costs per stay day in the SUZ's own asylum facility are decreasing with the increasing full capacity of these facilities. The reason is that the fixed costs of running the premises are allocated to more asylum seekers.
The volume of total costs incurred to provide services for asylum seekers increases directly in proportion with the increasing number of asylum seekers.
In 2001 and 2003, applicants in crisis capacity were accommodated in their own asylum facilities.
In part of 2003, exceptional accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds in total) was used to address the capacity crisis of asylum facilities caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers of Chechen nationality from Poland.
This capacity was ensured by leasing 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
The expenditure per applicant per stay day was then lower in these years.
However, the long-term maintenance of high capacity of these facilities is not possible.
The risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and the need for more accommodation should be taken into account.
At the same time, it is not possible to perform some repairs, maintenance and investments in fully occupied accommodation capacity.
The form of asylum facilities operated on a contractual basis enables the adoption of operational solutions in the field of asylum facility capacities where necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centres and residence centres.
The Ministry of Education has reception centres Adamov-Gbely, Rohovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and a residence centre Brezová pod Bradlom.
The total capacity of reception centres is 470 seats and the residence centre is 100 seats.
An increasing number of asylum seekers were dealt with by the Ministry of Education by setting up a residence centre in Gabčíkov in the rented premises of the Bratislava Technical University with flexible available capacity from 250 to 940 seats.
According to the concluded contract, the leaseholder also ensures the provision of services related to the operation of the Centre.
In this way, the MEA addressed the lack of its own staff.
The residential centre was also temporarily established in 2002 and 2003 in leased premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 seats.
Reception centres had an average occupancy of between 57% and 62% during the audited period, with an average occupancy of between 33% and 50% in residential centres.
Occupancy varied according to the season and was highest in the last months of the year when he applied for asylum for many more applicants compared to other months of the year.
Further increase of accommodation capacity by about 450 seats will be possible after reconstruction of resorts in Opatovský Nový Vsi and Vlachoch.
Following the completion of the Humennom Centre in 2006, the number of seats will increase by another 550 people.
5.2.1 Costs of asylum facilities
Data on the cost of operating asylum facilities are given in Table 4.
Their analysis shows that the operation of an asylum facility by another body providing the premises and security of the facilities, including the related activities, is one way of securing at reasonable cost the tasks arising from the residence of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic.
6. Management of State funds and assets
6.1 Analysis of management
In the Czech Republic, the approved budget expenditure of the SUZ was increased by CZK 103,077 by thirteen budgetary measures in 2001.
Of which CZK 89,979 thousand (87.29%) were assigned funds. Most of it was intended to address the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (CZK 44,538 thousand) and to provide health care to asylum seekers (CZK 38,870 thousand).
In 2002, the SUZ's expenditure was increased by CZK 88,362 thousand by 20 budgetary measures.
Of which CZK 62,282 thousand (70.48%) were dedicated funds, most of which (CZK 53,200 thousand) were intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, the SUZ's expenditure was increased by CZK 88,078 thousand by 14 budgetary measures.
Of these, 82,000 thousand CZK (93.09%) were assigned funds released from the General Treasury Administration.
The amount of CZK 51,000 was intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers, CZK 24,000 to deal with the influx of Chechen refugees and CZK 7,000 for the program of humanitarian evacuations of disabled people in the Republic of Iraq.
For an overview of the use of selected SUZ expenditure during the audited period, see Table 5.
It is clear from the above overview that the highest part of the expenditure was spent on the provision of services.
The amount of expenditure incurred for the purchase of services ranged from 37,07% to 38,23% of total expenditure.
The aggravating expenditure under this heading was expenditure on accommodation and catering of applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, expenditure on medical care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service providing security at individual asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work and premiums (23.99% - 24.97%) contributed significantly to the SUZ's total expenditure.
Last but not least, material purchases (around 14%) contributed significantly to the SUZ's total expenditure, with food purchases (7.61%? 9,83% of total expenditure).
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the Ministry of Migration Policy and the asylum process was marked by more budgetary measures addressing legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
The draft and breakdown of the budget in the expenditure part was characterised, in particular, in 2001 and 2002, by an imbalance between the requirements of the Ministry of Education, which were based on the increase in the number of asylum seekers and the financing needs of their legal entitlements, and the resources provided, in particular, in the main category of current expenditure.
The administrator of the budget chapter addressed disproportions during the year with several budgetary measures increasing the current expenditure limit by 41.8% in 2001 and by up to 71.7% in 2002.
For an overview of the expenditure collected by the Ministry of Education during the audited period, see Table 6.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and premiums, ranging from 24.47% to 30.51%, and expenditure on materials and services, ranging from 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditure, contributed decisively to the absorption of current expenditure.
Over 10% were expenditure on security services and between 3.92% and 7.20% were expenditure on food purchases.
Another significant part was expenditure on accommodation and catering services, ranging from 10.82% to 26.96%.
A relatively low proportion, ranging from 1,03% to 6,25%, was capital expenditure.
6.2. Deficiencies identified
The results of the audits in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings that did not have a major impact on the management of state funds and assets.
These were weaknesses in particular in the following areas: (a) the use of State budget appropriations contrary to the purpose for which they were intended by the State Budget Act when current expenditure was covered by actions having the character of technical appreciation of long-term tangible assets; b) violation of the Accounting Act in the area of inventories and non-compliance with the indicative accounting curriculum.
In the Czech Republic, minor shortcomings were also identified in the handling of State property, when it was left for use to another person without an appropriate contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes to land registry data violated the Land Registry Act; the Waste Act has been violated by leaving the waste for disposal to a person who was not authorised to dispose of the waste.
In the Slovak Republic, shortcomings in the provision of disproportionately high reserves for the consumption of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in public procurement and the management of State property were also identified when its records were not adequately secured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not proven.
7. Internal control system
At 1 July 2002 the SUZ introduced an internal control system within the meaning of Act No. 320/2001 Coll., on financial control, determining the competences of individual employees responsible for carrying out preliminary, interim and subsequent checks.
At the same time, an internal audit system was introduced and an internal auditor of the SUZ appointed.
Each year, the SUZ is issued with a plan of financial, social and operational technical controls aimed at a comprehensive verification of the management of state funds and assets in individual asylum facilities managed by the SUZ.
42 management inspections were carried out in 2002 and 54 were carried out in 2003.
In the Slovak Republic, the direct exercise of control activities in the departments and organizations of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic in respect of compliance with generally binding legislation and internal regulations ensures the Ministry's controls.
Within the audited period, the tasks of the asylum policy section were not checked.
The internal control system of the Ministry of Education is primarily focused on the implementation of preliminary and ongoing financial control according to Act No. 502/2001 Z. z., about checking and auditing.
The performance of financial control is also governed by the internal rules of the Director of the Ministry of Education.
The substantive orientations of the control activities as part of the management of the various departments were set out in the annual plan of the Ministry of Education.
Directors of trade unions have been designated responsible for the exercise of control in this area.
According to the written documentation submitted, no deficiencies were identified.
Since the expiry of the Decree of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic No 28 of 23. 4. 2004, the Ministry is obliged to process and investigate complaints under the Complaints Act.
The organizational security of this task will need to be resolved in the near future.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Czech Audit Office.
Joint report on parallel checks on expenditure on construction of the Prague - Dresden motorway
Introductory word
Without the existence of trans-European transport networks, a modern, dynamic and, above all, united Europe would be difficult to imagine.
High-quality transport networks are a prerequisite for maintaining and raising the living standards of Europeans.
Creating conditions for fast, safe, reliable and cheap transport of people and costs is an important task for government.
This is a very demanding task both in organisational and technical terms and in financial terms.
European efforts at sustainable mobility often and hard to find compromises with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and human-friendly environment.
Construction of transport infrastructure, even with the necessary measures for the benefit of the environment, is financially demanding.
Considered procedures and government decisions in the preparation and acquisition of transport buildings can generate significant savings in public financial resources that can be used differently for the benefit of citizens.
One of the roles of the audit institutions is to actively look for shortcomings that have led to lower-than-achievable cost-effectiveness, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure on transport infrastructure construction.
Audit institutions should not only highlight the shortcomings identified, but recommend measures to improve the situation, for the benefit of citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short Summary
The two supreme audit institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SRN and the Czech Republic) of the Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as the "BRH") and the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO") carried out parallel checks in 2005 and 2006 on expenditure on the construction of the Prague-Dresden motorway (motorway D 8 v
Motorways are connected by a border bridge co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to the cooperation with the SAO, the BRH was able to carry out a thorough check on the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
On the basis of close cooperation with BRH, the SAO obtained for comparative purposes the necessary data on the amount of German costs of bridges and tunnels.
The Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany concluded a contract for the construction of a border bridge in 2000.
According to the construction process, the completion date was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
However, during the procurement process, the Directorate of Roads and Motorways of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "MSD") committed errors that led to the extension of the competition period and the shortening of the construction period.
The contract with the contractor was thus signed later than anticipated.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in a shorter time and ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, however, MSD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
As part of the joint control work, the prices of bridges on motorways D 8 and A 17 were compared based on the conversion per m2 of the bridge structure.
The statistical analysis of prices made it possible to identify bridges with high costs per m2 of area.
Analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in a group of large bridges over 100 meters long.
The price increase could also be attributed to the delay in the procurement procedure.
When analysing the cost of building the tunnels, the inspectors found that the prices of tunnels on the D 8 motorway were significantly higher than those of comparable tunnels in Germany.
The BRH and the SAO now have a database of bridge and tunnel prices that they will be able to rely on for future checks on the effectiveness of the funds used for transport infrastructure purposes.
For the construction of bridges, the two audit institutions recommend: the standardisation of bridge structures and the use of coupled steel-concrete and special structures only in cases where biased reinforced concrete bridges are not adequate.
Among the main features of the cooperation was its team spirit and informality.
During the parallel inspection, the auditors participated in their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report reports on the progress and results of parallel checks on funds spent on the construction of the motorway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The controls focused on the cost-effectiveness, efficiency and effectiveness of the expenditure incurred.
Parallel checks were carried out by the BRH in Germany and the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel checks took place in 2005 and 2006.
The SAO audited the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure amounting to approximately CZK 20 billion including VAT (approximately €690 million) on the border section of the D 8 motorway, which has the number 0807.
Of this amount, €64 million of European funds (ISPA) was planned to be used.
In addition to the parallel checks carried out jointly with the SAO, BRH inspected the preparation and construction of motorway A 17 in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of motorway A 17 amounted to approximately € 670 million, of which € 277 million will be co-financed by the European Funds (EFRE).
The motorway from Prague to Dresden is part of the trans-European transport corridor IV. Dresden - Central and Southern Eastern Europe - Istanbul.
Highway D 8 runs from Prague via Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
Motorway A 17 runs from the Czech Republic/Germany national border to Dresden.
Border sections of both motorways were under construction at the time of inspection.
These sections were put into operation on 21 December 2006.
On the German side, the motorway is finished up to Dresden, while on the Czech side the D 8 motorway is not finished, because section 0805, 16.4 km across the Czech Central Mountain between Řehlovice and Lovosice, is still in the preparatory phase.
According to the plan, section 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem is to pass through the protected landscape area of the Czech Central Mountains.
According to the forecasts carried out in the Czech Republic in 2001, the traffic intensity of 22,940 vehicles per day should be on the border section No. 0807 of highway D 8 in 2008.
According to German forecasts, in 2010 the traffic intensity at the Czech border will total about 25,000 vehicles per day.
In 2000, Germany and the Czech Republic concluded a Treaty between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic on the interconnection of the German motorway A 17 and the Czech highway D 8 at the common state border by building a border bridge.
Both States are involved in the construction of the bridge, so monitoring the construction of the bridge was an important aspect of the parallel checks carried out by the two audit institutions.
Cooperation between BRH and SAO
Since mid- 2005, the two highest audit institutions have discussed close cooperation in the control of the construction of the highway connecting Prague and Dresden.
Both parties had serious reasons for such cooperation:
1.
GERMANY contributes financially to the construction of the border bridge.
Its planning and construction is based on MSD.
Therefore, BRH itself did not have the opportunity to inspect this construction project.
2.
The SAO did not have at its disposal the comparative database needed to assess whether the funds were used economically in terms of the overall level of costs for bridges and tunnels on D 8.
3.
The SAO needed to ensure the effectiveness of expenditure, taking into account the main technical parameters of the motorway, in particular the arrangement of bridges and tunnels, which should allow the same quality of travel on both sides of the border.
Following preparatory negotiations, the Agreement on Coordinated Highway Control D 8/A 17 was signed by the Presidents of the two Supreme Audit Institutions on 4 January 2006.
Joint working meetings of the BRH and SAO auditors took place throughout 2006 at an interval of approximately six to eight weeks.
The negotiations dealt with current problems and tasks, in particular the preparation of a uniform methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels, the exchange of findings from border bridge inspections and the preparation of joint reports.
The ongoing exchange of information was an important feature of cooperation.
While BRH carried out most of the work on the comparison of technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and procurement procedures, the SAO largely prepared a methodology for monitoring the prices of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable regulatory standards for control in government differ in the way control actions are concluded in both countries.
For these reasons, the two Supreme Audit Institutions have drawn their own audit conclusions on their findings obtained during their checks.
This report reflects the results achieved during the parallel checks.
The cooperation will end with the signing of the final communiqué in the first half of 2007.
Construction of a border bridge
In the 2000 Treaty, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany agreed on a deadline for completion of the border bridge construction as far as possible in 2005.
The two parties then agreed to postpone this deadline until the end of 2006.
As an investor, MSD was active.
GERMANY contributes financially to the construction of the bridge from 42.13%.
In the period up to 1999, the MSD proposed that the border bridge should have a biased reinforced concrete structure.
In 1999, in agreement with its partners in Germany, MSD agreed to a related steel-concrete structure.
This Decision was justified by the reduction of the number of double pillars from seven to five and the subsequent ecological benefit of such a solution to the valley.
Moreover, the comparative calculations carried out by MSD indicated that the coupled steel-concrete construction should be a less expensive option.
But there was a mistake in the calculations.
They indicated that the new coupled steel-concrete structure would be only 397 m long.
It's actually 5% longer.
During the award of the border bridge contract, the MSD made serious errors.
It did not prepare the contract documentation to adequately describe the assessment criteria and sub-criteria for the benchmarking of tenders.
This error led to a subjective and problematic evaluation by the Bid Assessment and Evaluation Board and the Director-General.
The unsuccessful bidder contested the results of the procurement procedure.
A subsequent investigation by the Competition Authority resulted in the contract for the award of the construction contract being signed later than originally envisaged.
This meant that the 2004 summer construction season was wasted after the evaluation of the bids and that the construction period was reduced.
The construction company agreed to build the bridge in a shorter period of time, but at the cost of a substantial increase in costs.
The offered procedure included double mounting of the bridge superstructure, change in the construction of the pillars and establishment and equipment of the assembly premises.
In addition, the construction company was unable to obtain the originally designed type of steel at the necessary time.
The new type of steel - at a cost of roughly €4 million, which had to be fully reimbursed by MSD - made it possible to shorten the period for the implementation of anti-corrosion protection, which in turn made it possible to reduce the total period of construction of the border bridge.
Compared to the net price of €18.3 million offered in the tender, the total cost of building the border bridge will increase considerably as a result of the accelerated procedure and other financing adjustments.
The reduced period of time reserved for construction work led to an increase in the price of approximately €5.9 million.
The net cost is currently around €25.9 million, without taking into account automatic price increases (as at October 2006).
Comparison of bridge and tunnel prices
The two supreme audit institutions analysed the prices of bridges on motorways D 8 and A 17 in order to identify bridges whose price was too high and to compare the prices of bridges on the German and Czech sides.
The analysis was based on methods of mathematical statistics.
Furthermore, tunnels on D 8 were compared with similar tunnels on motorways in Germany (A 71, A 38 and A 4).
There are no similar tunnels on Highway A 17.
In preparing this part of the check, it was important to identify the relevant prices accurately.
The two supreme audit institutions set the following principles for comparing the prices of bridges: to be based on the actual price paid for the bridge without value added tax (VAT rates vary in the Czech Republic and SNR and are subject to changes); not to take into account prices for special bridge bases; convert prices in CZK to € according to the European Central Bank rate applicable to 30.12.2005 (CZK 29 = €1).
On D 8 i A 17 there are bridges of various structures (steel-concrete, biased reinforced concrete, coupled steel-concrete and steel) and various sizes.
In order to ensure homogeneity of the structures examined, bridges were divided into groups according to the type of construction.
Within these groups, the size of the bridge was also taken into account in the analyses.
By far the most common type of construction on both sides of the border were concrete bridges (20 bridges on D 8, 36 bridges on A 17).
The analysis focused primarily on this group of bridges, since the number of sets allowed the use of mathematical and statistical methods with a high degree of reliability of results.
Checks found that the prices per m of 2 concrete bridges on D 8 i A 17 depend on the size of the bridge (its length, area): the larger the bridge, the lower the price per m2 of bridge structure.
For German bridges, the price dependence was stronger than for Czech bridges (see graphs below).
Two concrete bridges were identified on A 17 and four on D 8, whose price is significantly higher.
To find these bridges, a method was used to detect atypical values in a set of numbers, and a regression analysis taking into account the dependence of the bridge's price on its size (for determining atypically expensive bridges, the standard distance from the regression curve is upwards).
However, information on the atypically high price of those bridges should only be considered as an indicator of which bridges need to be targeted.
In order to draw a generally applicable conclusion, the causes of the high price should be analysed in each identified case.
One such cause may be inefficient administrative measures or environmental protection requirements or other acceptable grounds.
Given that Czech concrete bridges are on average longer than German ones (see table below), the proven negative dependence of the bridge's price on its length could lead to the assumption that Czech bridges should be cheaper.
The hypothesis about lower prices of Czech concrete bridges is also supported by lower labour costs in the construction industry in the Czech Republic compared to the German Republic.
However, the results of the analysis show that the prices of concrete bridges on D 8 are higher than on A 17.
During the joint negotiations, two possible causes of this situation were identified:
1.
In Germany, most bridges are awarded as separate contracts.
Such an award allows small and medium-sized regional firms to participate in the contract contest.
In the Czech Republic many bridges are awarded as part of the contract for part of the motorway route, which is several kilometres long.
Small and medium-sized companies do not participate in such a competition because the contract is too big for them.
2.
In the Czech Republic there is more variability in bridge construction than in Germany.
In this context, the SAO found that the type of bridge construction is decided long before its construction.
The decision shall be taken at the time when the MSD translates the request for a territorial decision.
Although MSD selects types of bridges from several variants at this time, economics plays a smaller role in decision making.
The general conclusion on the prices of bridges in the Czech Republic and Germany could only be made on the basis of a thorough analysis of the construction market in both countries, which would however go beyond this control action.
The border bridge is the most expensive coupled steel concrete bridge on D 8 and A 17.
In the case of tunnels, the prices of tunnels on D 8 were found to be twice as high as those in Germany.
However, the comparison of the main construction and technical parameters of the tunnels on D 8 with the tunnels in Germany showed no significant difference.
Significant price differences could be attributed to the fact that there is no real competition in the Czech Republic in the field of tunnel construction.
However, a small number of tunnels did not make it possible to draw generally applicable conclusions.
Efficiency and efficiency of construction of the Dresden motorway - Prague
A separate Czech Republic was established in 1993.
The government approved the concept of the development of the motorway network in the same year.
The D 8 motorway should be gradually extended from Prague to the state border with Germany.
Section No. 0805 through the Czech Central Mountains should have been acquired earlier than the border section No. 0807.
The Czech Republic acquires motorway D 8 within the framework of programme funding.
The programme No. 327 220 "Construction of the motorway D 8 Prague - Ústí nad Labem - state border of the Czech Republic/Germany" set two objectives for the construction of the motorway D 8:
1.
improve the connection between Prague and Ústí nad Labem - a national objective;
2.
