In restricted procedures, the contracting authority shall first select potential suppliers to be asked to submit a tender.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU provisions allow a limit on the number of applicants in European restricted procedures.
However, a restricted procedure requires at least five tenderers to be invited to submit a tender and, in the case of a negotiated procedure for publication, at least three potential tenderers must be invited.
In any case, the number of candidates invited must be sufficiently wide to guarantee genuine competition.
The selection criteria shall be objective and non-discriminatory and shall be published in advance.
The selection of potential candidates to be invited is very susceptible to manipulation, e.g. preferences of some of them.
Reducing competition to a few candidates can ease their secret agreement.
This has a negative impact on the outcome of the proceedings.
Therefore, the contracting authority must take measures to prevent manipulation and ensure that it has effective control to ensure that the procedure is transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The provisions for the selection of candidates are similar in both countries.
In addition to the requirements of the European Directive, contracting authorities should change the tenderers which are invited to tender.
It is also not permissible to restrict competition from a regional perspective.
Contracting entities shall document and justify the selection of tenderers and the selection process.
Different provisions
In Germany, at least three candidates are required to be invited in the event of a restricted procedure and several suitable tenderers in the case of a negotiated procedure.
Except in two cases, the new Czech regulations do not allow to limit the number of candidates addressed in the case of restricted and negotiated procedures.
In Germany, when selecting candidates, the "four-eyes principle" must be respected.
While one worker proposes a list of these, another must substantially modify the proposal, for example by deleting the proposed tenderer or setting up another.
This is intended to prevent a situation in which an individual can definitively determine the range of candidates participating in the proceedings.
Where such a provision is not in place, a far-reaching unlawful agreement between participants is allowed.
The list of tenderers to be invited to submit a tender shall be confidential and shall not be disclosed.
This also obliges authorized independent experts.
In the Czech Republic there is no similar measure or measure for the confidential treatment of the list of applicants.
According to the German provisions, they may not designate candidates for an external company but may make proposals to the contracting authority.
There is no similar requirement in the Czech Republic.
Main control findings
BRH
Number of candidates
Apart from a few cases, the requirement to reach a minimum number of applicants has been met.
An analysis of almost 7,000 construction contracts with a value up to the national limit showed that in the case of restricted procedures, the contracting authorities invited an average of 6.6 potential tenderers and an average of 4.4 tenderers in the case of direct negotiated procedures.
Change of suppliers and regional constraints
In particular, the contracting authorities did not change the range of contacted tenderers in the area of building construction because they had good experience with those with whom they had cooperated so far.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
The contracting authorities argued that, in the case of a non-public procedure, they were to guarantee that they would reach out to tenderers whose suitability they had already ascertained in advance.
Although there was no evidence for illegal regional restrictions, the non-public tenderers included a larger proportion of regional tenderers than in the case of public proceedings.
The contracting authorities explained this by the low level of the contract compared to the public procedure and the high cost of travel for potential tenderers.
Cross-checking principle and proposals by self-employed professionals
Contracting authorities have generally ignored the obligation to amend the list of candidates proposed by self-employed professionals.
They argued in particular for staff shortages, time pressures or inadequate knowledge of the suitable candidate.
In many cases, the records did not show who had proposed the candidate who had been asked to participate in the proceedings.
The examination of some samples showed that the list of potential tenderers was established by self-employed experts and was accepted unchanged by the contracting authority.
The contracting authorities thus did not adequately protect themselves from potential manipulation.
Confidentiality of treatment of lists of potential tenderers
One contracting authority kept a list of tenderers for invitations to tender in a database to which all employees had access at any time.
This allowed for manipulation or unauthorised disclosure of the names of presumed or accepted applicants, who could then agree on a price.
Documentation
The dossier stated the reasons for the selection of tenderers in only a few cases.
SAO
Selection criteria for candidates
During the construction of the road circuit, interested parties did not have information on what their qualifications would be evaluated and how.
For the action related to the development and modernisation of waterways and ports in the contract notice, the criteria for limiting the number of tenderers have not been established.
All eight tenderers met the qualification requirements, but this exceeded the number to which the contracting authority restricted participation in the procurement procedure.
The Commission then selected the candidates by random selection method - by drawing lots, which was legal at the time.
This procedure should have been mentioned as a criterion already in the contract notice.
Summary
In view of the high risk of manipulation in the selection of the winning bidder in limited procurement procedures, both countries have introduced special measures to prevent illegal restrictions on competition.
German rules limit such opportunities for manipulation by cross-checking (four-eyes principle), by maintaining the confidential nature of the list of applicants and by prohibiting bidding on external companies.
The Czech rules aim to prevent potential restrictions with the aim of manipulation mainly by an unlimited number of applicants.
However, the audit found that part of the rules in question was not sufficiently applied and that the inadmissible restriction of the scope of the candidates was not prevented in some cases.
Contracting entities are obliged to completely eliminate these deficiencies.
Submission of tenders
The procurement phase in which potential tenderers may draw up tenders on the basis of the tender documents they have received begins with the publication of information on the procurement procedure and/or the invitation to tender.
Until the date of opening of the envelopes, any tenderers may submit their tenders to the contracting authority in order to bid for the award of the contract.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU law does not prescribe specific requirements at this stage of the procurement procedure.
The contracting authority must comply with the national rules governing this stage of the procedure and avoid potential manipulation.
Those provisions relate in particular to organisation and control.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The principle is that tender documents on the basis of which potential suppliers draw up their tenders must always be sent by the contracting authority.
Design offices interested in management should not perform this role.
The contracting authority shall ensure that all candidates have received the same information during this stage of the procurement procedure.
In the event of confusion in the procurement documents or where further questions arise, only the contracting authority may supply information to tenderers.
The design offices responsible for drawing up the procurement documents may not provide any information.
During this entire phase, any contact between the design office and the applicants must be avoided.
They must remain anonymous throughout the course because allowing contact with them can adversely affect the competition.
Tenders sent by post or submitted directly shall be submitted in a closed envelope.
Electronically submitted tenders shall be encoded.
Different provisions
In Germany, the contracting authority may mandate insured suppliers of external services to print and distribute documentation, while their employees must be obliged to observe confidentiality.
In Germany, tenders received must be marked with the date of receipt and transmitted directly and immediately in the original state (sealed) to the official responsible for their storage.
This worker must not be involved in the procurement procedure.
The menus received must be locked until the envelope opening date.
In the Czech Republic, the tenders received are marked with a serial number.
The contracting authority shall issue a report with information on the contest including the tender number and information on the preparation and receipt of the tender.
There are no specific provisions on the custody of offers.
Main control findings
BRH
BRH inspected the commissioning of the administrative building.
Sending of procurement documents
The audited contracting authorities sent the tender documents either directly or commissioned the external company to print and distribute them.
The self-employed did not send any documentation.
Information to tenderers
For the part of the procurement documents relating to questioning and obtaining information, the contracting authority has not acted under the separate planning rule from the procurement procedure.
Contrary to the relevant regulations, he often did not mention in the documentation the names of his contact staff, but rather the staff of the project management department.
Some tendering notices even included the names of firms or self-employed persons involved in the preparation of the procurement documents.
In rare cases, no identical information was received by tenderers who raised questions during the procurement procedure.
Menu Labeling
For contracting entities, all tenders received were marked with a stamp and a certificate of receipt.
However, in some cases in the negotiated procedure, offers were accepted by self-employed professionals, thereby violating the rule of one corruption prevention structure.
Custody of the tenders
Once marked, not all tenders were passed on directly and without delay to the official assigned to keep them in custody locked the tenders in a steel cabinet.
For one contracting authority, tenders were temporarily placed in the open compartment of the filing office to which all employees had access.
Another sponsor placed the mailbox in the hallway without permanent supervision, and part of the bids thrown into the mailbox stayed there overnight.
The opening of the box was wide and unsecured, so it was accessible not only to employees.
SAO
The SAO did not identify shortcomings in this area.
Summary
In both countries, rules are laid down to prevent contacts, in particular between interested companies and design offices that cooperate in the procurement procedure, throughout the process.
Equal treatment is ensured by sending the same information to all applicants.
Rules to prevent manipulation and corruption are appropriate for the receipt, safekeeping and confidentiality of offers.
In Germany, the requirements are somewhat more developed than in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the accumulated surveillance records showed breaches in some areas.
These irregularities can easily be corrected.
Opening envelopes
Opening envelopes
During the opening of envelopes, tenders that have been closed so far are opened, their contents are read and published.
The period during which the tenderer is bound by his tender shall begin at the moment of expiry of the deadline for the submission or opening of envelopes and shall end at the date specified by the contracting authority.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
The European legislation does not contain any specific provisions on opening envelopes.
However, national laws and regulations contain extensive requirements for the protection of tenders and competition during this sensitive phase of the entire procurement procedure.
The principles of "more eyes," transparency and credibility of the envelope opening process are intended to prevent manipulation and modification of tenders already submitted.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The opening of envelopes shall be carried out by several persons appointed by the contracting authority.
Compliance with the "more eyes" principle is intended to prevent individuals from secretly manipulating offers.
Candidates may be present when opening envelopes.
When opening, all envelopes must be placed before the Chairman of the Commission and opened one by one.
Offers received late may not be taken into account.
In order to ensure transparency when opening envelopes, this phase must be recorded in writing, including the conclusions (results). The record shall include, inter alia, the names of the tenderers and the prices offered.
The minutes must be read and signed by the group leader.
The registration may also be signed by the candidates present.
Different provisions
A commission is being set up in the Czech Republic to open envelopes.
The participation of independent experts shall be admitted.
The members of the Commission may also be entrusted with the deliberations in the subsequent stages of the procedure, i.e. the evaluation of tenders.
In Germany, the opening of envelopes takes place in the presence of the manager and recorder.
The manager shall be an employee of the contracting authority.
The manager and, in the case of civil engineering, the registrar shall not be participants in the preparatory phase (preparation of the procurement documents), may not decide on the award of the contract and may not be members in the subsequent processing (procedure) of the contract.
German regulations require that envelope opening entries include not only bid prices, but also all information on discounts and special (unusual) signs, such as damaged envelopes on receipt or late bids.
In the Czech Republic there must be an indication of the language of the tender and the signature of the tenderer in addition to the tenders.
German legislation requires all parts of the envelopes to be marked in order to avoid subsequent changes.
Tenders, typically marked as perforations indicating the date, must be kept confidential (secret) after opening the envelopes and may only be made available to persons processing them further.
Similar measures do not exist in the Czech Republic.
If a single offer is received in the Czech Republic, the envelope must not be opened and the tenderer must be notified immediately.
They do not have this adjustment in Germany and, if a single offer is accepted, it is opened and evaluated.
Main control findings
BRH
Cross-checking principle
During the opening of envelopes, the sponsors followed the principle of four eyes.
There was always a manager and a recorder who was not assigned another role.
However, in isolated cases, in small negotiated procedures, natural persons opened tenders sent to them without the participation of the contracting authority.
Envelope Opening Progress
envelope opening logs did not always document progress.
In some cases tenders submitted late were not marked and in some cases signatures were missing.
Labeling of incoming tenders
The contracting authorities indicated perforations with a date that complied with the requirements.
Some of them have been incorrect in the past, but have changed their practice after being warned by BRH.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
SAO
Time limit for receipt of tenders
During road repairs, the tenderer's bid was handed over to the contracting authority with a monthly delay, and he accepted it.
Summary
In both countries, substantial parts of the envelope opening provisions are identical with respect to the principle of "more eyes" and the principle of transparency, thus enabling the risk of corruption and manipulation to be substantially reduced.
The German rules are more comprehensive compared to the Czech Republic, especially the requirements for precise documentation of the procedure.
The marking, safe preservation and respect for the confidentiality of tenders substantially limit the possibility of subsequent changes to the tenders submitted.
Moreover, the staff responsible for opening envelopes shall not carry out any other activities related to the contract to be awarded.
Despite the detection of some irregularities, the findings confirm that the rules on opening envelopes are largely applied.
Assessment and evaluation of tenders
The contracting authority shall examine and evaluate tenders received within a specified time limit.
It must also award the contract to the tenderer who best meets the award criteria in the tender.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU law sets out the process for assessing and evaluating tenders in several steps:
The first step is to check the suitability of the applicants.
They must have a good economic and financial position and the required professional and technical knowledge and skills.
Tenderers who have sometimes been legally convicted of bribery or defrauding must always be excluded from procurement procedures.
Non-excluded tenderers must be evaluated in terms of numerical accuracy, technical suitability and value for money on the basis of previously published award criteria.
The contracting authority must identify the most economically favourable tender and in particular examine all significantly low price offers.
Review and evaluation is particularly sensitive and susceptible to manipulation.
For example, tenderers may be excluded for no legitimate reason, or tenders which do not meet the requirements may be left in competition.
The outcome of the evaluation may be improperly influenced by the preference or disadvantage of a tenderer, thereby preventing the selection of the most economically advantageous tender.
The contracting authority must therefore take special measures to select the persons involved in the process and ensure that they meet the requirements for integrity and technical expertise.
They also need to make sure that the process and the decisions taken are transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
In line with EU requirements, the relevant provisions in both countries require review and evaluation of tenders in step-by-step steps.
During the evaluation, the requirements for documenting the suitability of tenderers, the evaluation criteria and their weights as set out in the notice or tender documents shall not be amended.
The criteria laid down for assessing the suitability of tenderers cannot be further applied.
Further evaluation may only be carried out on the basis of evaluation criteria.
The tenders submitted must first be examined from a formal point of view as to whether they are complete or do not include suspicious elements which could encourage manipulation.
Where tenderers are excluded from further examination and evaluation of tenders submitted by them, they shall be informed thereof without delay.
Where the evaluation of tenders results in the finding of a disproportionately low bid price, the tenderer concerned must be given the opportunity to comment on the situation prior to the possible withdrawal of his bid.
The reasons for the decision must be transparently documented.
Different provisions
In Germany, candidates must remain confidential and only beneficiaries can participate in the evaluation of tenders.
Only the contracting authority may review the mathematical accuracy of tenders.
Only employees who are not included in the decision-making phase of the selection of the supplier or in the implementation phase of the project may be assigned to the evaluation.
There are no precise provisions on who can carry out further reviews and evaluations.
If external companies are entrusted with the examination and evaluation of tenders, they must be aware that the tenders are confidential and honestly respect this fact.
They may only make proposals to the contracting authority for a decision.
In the Czech Republic, tenders must be reviewed and evaluated by a commission appointed by the contracting authority to prepare a report on the draft conclusion of the contract.
However, in both countries the final decision depends on the contracting authority.
If in Germany the documents and declarations required in connection with the submission of tenders are incomplete, the tenderers concerned must subsequently submit the required documents within six days.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
If tenderers do not comply with this obligation, their tenders must be excluded.
In the Czech Republic, the contracting authority may decide whether to give the tenderer the opportunity to complete the missing documents.
If the candidate does not submit them, they must be expelled.
In Germany it is necessary to examine not only the total price but also the unit prices.
If the price structure of the offer shows that the prices for parts of the overall project have been estimated to be disproportionately high or low, the tenderers must be asked for an explanation.
Where they do not submit an explanation and where the contracting authority can demonstrate that the tender contains compensatory prices, such tenders shall be excluded.
This is intended to prevent bidders from submitting price calculations on the assumption that substantial quantitative changes will be made to each part of the overall project, which may lead to a significant increase in project costs.
In the Czech Republic the total price of the work is evaluated and the prices of the parts are not examined in detail.
Valuation compensation is not a reason for excluding the offer.
In Germany, a contract cannot be awarded to a tenderer who offers a price that is disproportionately high or low.
If one or more tenders differ in price by 10% or more from the price estimated by the contracting authority or from other tenders, tenderers must demonstrate that their tender has been credibly and convincingly calculated.
If they are unable to do so, the contracting authority should exclude them.
In the Czech Republic, the tender procedure may be cancelled after a price review if only tenders with disproportionately low prices have been received and tenderers have not justified these prices.
If the price of the tender is significantly higher than the estimate of the contracting authority, this does not justify the refusal to award the contract to the tenderer concerned (as opposed to German procurement law).
Where there is a suspicion of conduct in Germany to restrict competition, the contracting authority shall immediately report that fact to the competent superior authority.
It must decide on the way forward and if it is appropriate to inform the antitrust or law enforcement authorities.
It also has to approve (e.g. if the contract exceeds €50,000 and the contract has not been awarded to the lowest bidder) whether the contract will be awarded during the contract or whether the award procedure will be cancelled.
Czech rules do not regulate this area.
Main control findings
BRH
Verification of suitability and award criteria
Most of the procurement procedures examined complied with the relevant requirements.
In the case of certain recommendations of potential suppliers made by self-employed persons, contracting authorities themselves have not checked the suitability of tenderers.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
In some cases, procurement procedures have not provided sufficient documentation as to whether the contracting authority took into account all published evaluation criteria at the time of selection or whether the selection decision was based solely on the price criterion.
Selection of interested parties and confidentiality of offers
Some contracting entities used the services of unauthorised persons, such as self-employed workers or employees of building offices.
They were integrated into the planning or implementation process of construction projects, performing functions to be held solely by the contracting authority.
The contracting authorities sought to justify this fact with their insufficient human resources in the sector.
In some cases, they used self-employed professionals to review the service offerings of persons who were not formally bound to maintain the confidentiality of the offers and to carry out with due care the fulfilment of their obligations under the contract.
As far as contracting authorities are concerned, there was generally no conclusive record of whether tenders in the custody of self-employed professionals were only available to designated persons.
Review and mathematical control of tenders
Some contracting entities have forwarded open envelopes for further examination to self-employed professionals, without first conducting the prescribed examination of tenders and mathematical review and without documenting the results of those screenings.
In the event of any intention of manipulation, third parties could make changes to tenders which could not be identified by the contracting entity.
The examination of the documents revealed a number of cases where unusual elements in the tenders were not adequately labelled or where price and product data were missing.
Performance audits
A model check by one contracting authority revealed that in 75% of procurement cases the most advantageous tenders deviated by more than 10% from the predicted costs.
One of the 20 procurement procedures was cancelled due to inadequate tendering prices.
In many cases there was a lack of evidence or sufficient documentation on the examination of tenders or negotiations with tenderers for further clarification.
In many cases there was also a lack of detailed information on, for example, unit prices of the most important invoiced items.
Changes in market prices or increases in material costs were often cited as the reason for the deviations.
The contracting authorities have resisted the difficulty of identifying and demonstrating countervailing prices.
In the case of one invitation to tender made by an entity outside the scope of normal contracting authorities, a 66% lower price was offered compared to the initial cost estimate.
Data on closer cost verification or determination of reasons for derogations have not been recorded.
In clarifying this question, the contracting authority found no indication of price dumping for the tenderer to which the contract would potentially be awarded.
It was therefore not clarified whether the original cost estimate was excessive or whether the price offered was too low.
Later, the contracting authority rated this tenderer as a "low-cost company" which was unable to meet either qualitative requirements or deadlines.
In another procurement procedure, the contracting authority awarded the contract to a tenderer whose price was 35% higher than the initial cost estimate.
The contracting authority did not cancel the procurement procedure and made the unfounded argument that the tenderer concerned could be presumed not to have based its pricing on disproportionately high costs.
Suspected irregularities
Two cases of irregularities were found in one contracting entity and were reported to the firm responsible for technical supervision.
In one procurement procedure, two tenderers submitted tenders containing an identical price calculation, prompting the contracting authority to exclude both tenders.
The checks did not show any substantial shortcomings in the application of other provisions.
SAO
Verification of suitability
For many construction events, such as university buildings, roads and railways, contracting authorities did not exclude tenderers from participating in the procurement procedure, even if they did not comply with the requirements of the contracting authority specified in the procurement terms or did not demonstrate the qualifications to the extent required, or, conversely, one contracting authority was unable to substantiate or explain the reason for the withdrawal of the candidate who met the requirements.
Evaluation
For the construction of the wastewater treatment plant, individual evaluation criteria of the procurement procedure for the contractor of the construction were established, but the contracting authority did not respect them during the procedure.
For the railway infrastructure development action, the weighting of the award evaluation criteria was not established at the start of the evaluation.
For the road repair project, the evaluation of the "shortening of construction time" criterion was not performed correctly.
For candidates in second and third place, the evaluation incorrectly indicated a reduction in construction time than indicated in their tenders.
Documentation of the reasons for the selection of the tenderer
For the three actions linked to housing support, the contracting authority did not demonstrate on the basis of which criteria it assessed the tenders received and how it selected the most appropriate of them.
The correctness of the selection of suppliers of small-scale contracts linked to the construction of a road circuit with a projected price up to 500 thousand.
CZK could not be verified as the suppliers were selected only on the basis of telephone consultations about the price and date of delivery, but the documents about these negotiations were not prepared.
Summary
In both countries, the rules for verifying and evaluating tenders correspond to EU requirements.
However, they differ with regard to the specific steps of the procedure and the selection of individuals involved in the procedure.
Unlike the Czech Republic, in Germany these procurement process steps are governed by stricter and more detailed requirements, especially with regard to the application of the cross-principle and the protection of tenders.
The same applies to the rules for verifying the appropriateness of the prices offered.
In both countries, checks have been found in some cases that the essential steps of the process in verifying and evaluating tenders have not been documented at all and, if so, only partially.
The absence of control tools and transparency in decision-making during the review and evaluation of tenders enables manipulation.
The checks showed serious deficiencies, such as the submission of tenders to third parties without proper prior examination and documenting of tenders by the contracting authority.
Where contracting entities entrust a third party with the performance of the functions associated with the examination and evaluation of tenders, appropriate measures and enhanced control of the measures against the increased possibility of manipulation are necessary.
In all cases, the audited German contracting authorities did not use the complete set of available instruments and did not deal with their own price structure.
In the Czech Republic, weaknesses were identified in the evaluation of the suitability of tenders and the use of evaluation criteria.
Completion of the procurement procedure
Following the examination and evaluation of tenders, the procurement process shall be completed by the award of the contract or the cancellation of the procedure.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
In the case of a European procedure, all tenderers must be informed in advance of the award decision.
Suppliers shall have the opportunity to review the decision taken within a limited period of 10 or 15 days and to request a review where appropriate.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
The period of 10 days shall apply to electronic submissions and 15 days to other submissions.
The contract may not be concluded before the expiry of that period or before the decision of the examination procedure.
If the review body rejects the complaint and confirms the decision, candidates and tenderers must be given the opportunity to have the correctness of the application of the procurement law reviewed by an independent court.
This measure ensures that no contracting entity will be able to circumvent the legal protection of suppliers by swiftly implementing the procurement decision.
The contracting authority shall document the procedure accordingly.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have implemented information obligations for management.
In both countries, the final decision on the outcome of the procurement procedure rests with the contracting authority.
However, it cannot arbitrarily deviate from the results of a properly conducted review and evaluation.
The contracting authority shall conclude the contract within a specified period of time.
The reason is that the tenderer is not bound by his bid after the expiry of this deadline.
The contents of the contract shall not deviate from the winning bid.
The unsuccessful tenderers should be informed of the result in good time, stating why their bid was not accepted.
Cancellation of the procurement procedure is only permissible if certain conditions are met, e.g. if the prices in the tenders do not conform to the specifications.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the mandatory pre-contract waiting period of 10 or 15 days applies to both European and national proceedings.
In Germany, equivalent provisions apply only to European procedures.
In all other procedures in Germany, tenderers cannot be informed of the award of the contract before deciding on its EU provisions and the review award.
In the Czech Republic, the procurement procedure must be cancelled if a single tender has been received or only one tender meets the requirements for its consideration and evaluation.
In Germany, a contract must be awarded even if a single tender has been received, provided that the tender meets the conditions laid down in the procurement documents and is cost-effective.
Main control findings
BRH
Few irregularities were found in the completion of controlled procurement processes.
In some cases, European procedures have been granted to letter companies prior to the expiry of the notification period, which may invalidate the contract.
Also, in several open procedures, the authorising letters contained modifications incompatible with the contents of the tender, e.g. new time limits.
In some cases, contracting authorities have failed to meet the award deadlines.
In one open procedure, the contracting authority selected the second most advantageous tender because the tenderer offering a price more than 50% lower no longer wished to fulfil the contract at the price originally offered.
SAO
During the reconstruction and construction of the university, the contracting authority did not conclude a contract with the contractor in accordance with the draft contract contained in the tender of the selected tenderer.
For some road repair and maintenance operations, the construction of the motorway and the road circuit, contracts were concluded later than laid down by law.
In the case of construction modifications in former military injuries, the contracting authority has sent a notice of the selection of the most suitable tender to all tenderers only after the expiry of the legal period.
Summary
Both countries have implemented EU rules on the closure of procurement procedures.
Legal protection of unsuccessful candidates contributes to reducing corruption.
The Czech Public Procurement Act includes an institute of legal protection even in cases of contracts below EU limits.
In both countries, it was found that the limited contract time limit was exceeded.
This can cause adverse economic consequences and increase the risk of manipulation.
In the future, contracting authorities should eliminate such shortcomings when concluding the procurement procedure.
Documentation, notifications, information obligations
The procurement process with all its individual stages, relevant findings and decisions, including the relevant justifications, shall be documented in a transparent manner.
The completion of the procurement procedure at European level must be published.
Data on procurement procedures are summarised in EU statistics.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
The obligation to document the procurement procedure is in line with the basic requirement of the principle of transparency, applied at EU-wide level.
Only sound and timely documentation on decision-making and rationale guarantees transparency in the procurement process and, above all, guarantees effective legal protection of the interests of each tenderer in cases where the value of the contract exceeds European limits.
Proper documentation is also an essential part of anti-corruption measures, as the obligation to give detailed reasons for individual decisions and their justification significantly reduces the scope for manipulation.
In the case of European procurement procedures, the contracting authority must notify their completion to the EU Publications Office of Official Publications within 48 days of the award date.
The Office publishes the notification in the Official Journal of the EU and the transparency requirement is fulfilled.
The contracting authority must summarise the relevant information on its procurement procedures and communicate it to the European Commission through the relevant national ministries.
On this basis, the European Commission publishes annual statistics to provide an overview of the development of the single market in construction.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have fully transposed the provisions of the European Law on Documentation and Notification Obligations into their national legislation.
The provisions on documentation and notification for the purposes of European statistics are almost identical in both countries.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the obligation to notify a contract does not only apply to European procedures, but also to national procurement procedures.
The notification period is only 15 days from the conclusion of the contract.
In Germany, the obligation to notify procurement procedures, in addition to those compulsory under European law, applies only to restricted procedures exceeding the threshold of EUR 25 000 (CZK 625 000) and direct procedures exceeding the threshold of EUR 15 000 (CZK 375 000), including VAT.
Only parties shall be informed below this limit.
Main control findings
BRH
Documentation
A large number of entries have not been fully documented.
The notification did not contain all the necessary information, e.g. reasons for supply specifications and national rules.
In the case of one procedure, the contracting authority has not explained why it entered into a contract with a tenderer whose tender did not contain mandatory formalities.
In several cases, some of the required records were also missing.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the case of certain European procedures, the contracting authority erred in publishing the notice.
In the case of several entries, there was no evidence of publication of the notice.
Notification obligation
The scanned files included the minimum information required and were created and sent on time.
Pre-transparency
In most cases, the contracting authority published information on the outcome of the contract.
In the case of one contracting entity, contract information was not disclosed due to a communication error.
It took the procurer six months to notice the error.
Consequently, the outcome of the proceedings was not published during that period.
SAO
Documentation
For events related to the organisation of a major sporting event, considerable weaknesses were identified in the documentation of the procurement process, such as incorrect data on bid prices in the evaluation committee's meeting protocols.
In addition, some documents about opening envelopes have not been signed.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the preparation of road repair and maintenance, construction of the motorway and road circuit, contract notices were sent after the deadline or were not published.
Summary
The provisions on documentation and notification and notification obligations cover European requirements and are almost identical in both countries.
This generally ensures transparency of procurement procedures and final selection.
Czech reporting obligations are somewhat stricter compared to German ones.
The checks revealed deficiencies significantly reducing the value of documentation as a means of preventing corruption.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Contracting entities should continue to strengthen the transparency of their procurement procedures and fully comply with the notification and notification requirements.
Summary evaluation and recommendations
Parallel controls of the SAO and BRH focused on two areas that are essential for the procurement process in both the Czech Republic and Germany, namely the application of EU procurement law and the prevention of corruption.
EU legislation provides an opportunity for international competition within the EU to create a single European market.
Measures aimed at preventing corruption are not merely aimed at avoiding or at least reducing corruption, but at the same time at preventing financial damage and possible loss of confidence in government integrity.
The findings of the two audit institutions - the SAO and the BRH - with regard to the application of the procurement law of the two countries and the comparison of their respective provisions give an internal view of the common and different elements that can assist both countries in the further development and application of this law.
Application of EU procurement law
Both countries have transposed EU public procurement law into their national legislation.
In both countries there is thus an important common basis for public procurement and for meeting the essential requirements in the field of: competition; equal treatment of candidates; transparency of procurement procedures.
Contracting authorities reinforce these requirements partly through very extensive measures.
The Czech Republic has laid down provisions on public procurement requiring European procedures and procedures that are below the EU limits and is therefore governed by national legislation.
However, checks have shown that contracting entities are not always fully compliant with all relevant provisions of EU requirements.
German contracting authorities should continue to improve the quality of their procurement procedures in order to eliminate these irregularities taking into account the implementation of EU requirements.
In the Czech Republic, controls identified risks affecting the economy and achieving value for money.
It is in particular an incomplete definition of the subject matter of the contract, which resulted in additional work, which was often awarded in violation of the law, insufficient definition of the expected price and the required qualification assumptions narrowing the possible range of tenderers and thus reducing competition in particular in the field of transport construction.
Prevention of corruption
Joint controls were not intended to detect cases of corruption.
The reason was that both the BRH and the SAO did not have the tools to do so.
However, they can check whether the competent authorities of both countries are taking measures to reduce corruption and manipulation in public procurement and how these measures are applied.
As regards the prevention of corruption, the two countries focused on different aspects.
In particular, the German provisions provide for wide and unrestricted competition, transparency and control as a central element in preventing corruption.
In particular, Czech regulations aim to strengthen transparency of procurement procedures.
BRH
In Germany, general principles of corruption prevention apply to the entire federal administration.
These principles have also been included in public procurement requirements and have been adopted to meet the specific needs of such procurement.
The relevant provisions specify, occasionally and very precisely, ways of meeting the requirements for the prevention of corruption during the procurement procedure and of selecting the persons included therein.
In the view of the BRH, the principle of preference for open procurement procedures and calls for participation is a particularly appropriate tool for substantially reducing the risk of corruption in public procurement, while limiting competition increases the risk of manipulation.
Risk analysis and adequate controls (in particular the cross-checking principle), transparency requirements, procurement documentation and various organisational measures are also effective mechanisms to prevent corruption and manipulation.
Therefore, BRH does not feel the need to substantially amend the current provisions that public institutions must comply with when awarding public contracts.
Anti-corruption measures are widely applied in practice.
Irregularities found in some areas highlighted weaknesses in compliance with certain requirements.
Therefore, contracting entities should provide further training to their employees, thereby enriching them with anti-corruption requirements and further raising their awareness in this area.
A significant part of the identified weaknesses refers to activities delegated by the construction administration to private entrepreneurs.
However, the lack of adequate controls in delegating powers increases the risk of their abuse.
Therefore, activities susceptible to manipulation and corruption should only be transferred to third parties if the administration can guarantee a sufficient degree of protection against unauthorised interference.
SAO
In the Czech Republic, anti-corruption strategies have been adopted at government level, which significantly affect the field of public procurement.
Audits of the SAO took place during the period when one of the most important parts of this strategy was implemented, namely a significant change of the Act on Public Procurement and the adoption of successive implementing regulations.
The strategy adopted and the new legislation can be effective steps to improve the situation.
Under the new rules, for example, the contracting authority must justify the effectiveness of the contract, the determination of the estimated value of the contract, the adequacy of the qualification requirements, the establishment of the basic evaluation criteria and the method of evaluation of tenders, and properly document and publish everything.
Recommendations
Overall, both the SAO and the BRH have a favourable opinion on how to implement EU requirements.
Their broad application has confirmed in practice that EU competition, equal treatment and transparency requirements form an appropriate basis for EU public procurement.
The transnational model, introduced in the EU, can also serve as a basis for similar projects aimed at facilitating and promoting international competition.
Taking into account the large potential for material and intangible damage resulting from manipulation and corruption in connection with public procurement, both the BRH and the SAO insist that it is the obligation of the contracting authorities to continue measures against corruption and manipulation and to improve them where possible.
In particular, the organisational structures and procurement processes should be continuously monitored in terms of weaknesses and risks in order to identify and respond appropriately to the need for correction.
In comparison with the practice in Germany, it appeared that the share of open procurement procedures in the Czech Republic should be increased, giving room for competition and substantially reducing the possibility of corrupt behaviour.
In cases where this is permissible and appropriate for contracting entities, partial procurement may also have a positive impact on the price achieved. The higher number of applicants puts pressure on the price achieved.
The organisation of the procurement procedure is also affected.
In Germany, it is provided by special state organizations, whereas in the Czech Republic, with the exception of transport constructions, it is organized by central authorities themselves or through contractual organizations.
Both the SAO and the BRH wish to further develop knowledge in their work where appropriate and to address it with their parliament and government, beyond their joint project.
Moreover, they are convinced that the principles of procurement law and their implementation, as described in this report, will also be of interest at the level of the International Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions. (INTOSAI), because these principles and findings are of general importance for the effective fight against corruption and for the guarantee that public contracts are awarded in a regime of well-functioning and fair competition and that value for money is achieved.

JOINT FINAL REPORT ON THE RESULTS OF PARALLEL CONTROLS OF EXCISE ADMINISTRATION IN SR AND THE CZECH REPUBLIC
Joint final report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The submitted joint report informs on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the administration of excise duties in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the supreme audit institutions of both countries was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO SR and the SAO of the Czech Republic in the performance of parallel controls aimed at the administration of excise taxes, which was concluded in August 2015.
The theme of parallel controls was selected on the basis of the fact that the two EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to determine how it is applied at national level, how the system of excise tax administration is set up and how the systems in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic differ.
The greatest benefit of the control actions was the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the identification of good practice.
Finally, it was beneficial to find that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise tax management is very limited without the implementation of parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrík,
President
Chairman
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel inspections of SPD management in SR and CR
Summary and evaluation
The legislation of excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia and their administration is in accordance with EU law and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences were found between the excise tax treatment in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic. In the Czech Republic, the verification of the economic stability of applicants for authorisation and the compulsory marking and colouring of selected mineral oils and certain other oils contributes to the effective administration of excise taxes; In SR, the distribution of control stamps is easier than in the Czech Republic and less burdensome to the tax administration.
In the fight against excise evasion, supervision of the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials, implementation of the Institute of the Fuel Distributor and registration of retailers of consumer packaging of alcohol proved to be good practice in both countries.
Excise revenue in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's objectives of reducing labour taxation, introducing environmental austerity measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, including because there is no indexation of excise duty rates in both countries.
This has the effect of reducing the importance of excise duties on total tax revenues and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, of reducing the tax burden on excise duties in real terms.
The State has supported the implementation of environmental measures in the long term, but these measures have a negative impact on excise revenue, which will therefore need to be replaced in the future by other revenues or reductions in State expenditure.
Administrative expenditure incurred in the administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia has been increasing in the long term, mainly due to wage growth, and their efficiency is decreasing.
In SR, this efficiency is also negatively affected by expenditure on electronisation of excise tax administration (IT expenditure) and expenses incurred on the wages of employees carrying out permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
The electronisation of excise tax administration in SR did not materially reflect the reduction in the number of tax administrations.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR recommend that FŘ SR reconsider the merits of the exercise of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the effectiveness of administrative expenditure was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the audited period that would reduce the staffing requirements of excise tax administration.
The number of comparable administrative acts of the tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in individual years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax entities is about a third lower in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in the Slovak Republic perform administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical exercise of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic place emphasis on remote supervision and risk analysis.
The administration of excise taxes in the Slovak Republic is administratively more demanding than in the Czech Republic and, due to the ratio of the number of tax acts to the number of entities, more costly.
Electronisation of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the Slovak Republic, the administration of excise tax returns is fully electronized; in the Czech Republic, documents proving the taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are transmitted electronically.
Both methods of electronization support effective administration of excise taxes, which is why the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditure for the implementation of the EMCS could not be compared as FŘ SR provided expenditure data only for the upgrade of the system in 2011-2015, but the expenditure was also spent before that period.
Expenses incurred during that period only for the EMCS upgrade were approximately 20% higher in the Slovak Republic than those incurred in the Czech Republic for both the EMCS and the system upgrade over more than a decade.
Excise administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia did not achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when incurring comparable expenditure.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the Slovak Republic the management of excise duties is significantly more resource intensive.
The introduction of the Electronic System for Monitoring the Movement of Excise Products (EMCS) has made the administration of excise duties more efficient, but in the Slovak Republic to a lower extent, as significantly higher expenditure was incurred on the introduction and modernisation of the system than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
Cooperation between the two audit institutions was carried out on the basis of the Cooperation Treaty in the implementation of parallel controls aimed at the management of excise duties of 18.8.2015.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR agreed to carry out parallel checks, which will be primarily focused on the issue of excise tax administration and the results of which will allow analysis, comparison and evaluation of the findings.
Common audit issues were agreed on which parallel checks were based.
Characteristics of subject matter and objectives of parallel control:
The aim of the parallel controls was to compare the performance of excise administrators taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators and to identify weaknesses in the excise management process.
In particular, the following main audit questions should be answered:
Were excise administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia achieving comparable values of qualitative indicators when incurring comparable expenditure?
Has the introduction of the Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) system made excise duty management more efficient and has the implementation expenses efficiently incurred?
The parallel checks should have identified the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, especially in the area of legislation and in setting up the organisational structure.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Directorate-General of Customs (GŘC) and Financial Directorate of SR (FD SR) have joined the Joint Declaration on mutual cooperation between the Visegrad Four countries, the objectives of this declaration include, inter alia, combating fraud, exploring the possibility of harmonising legislation and seeking harmonised interpretations on the rules of selected problems, exploring the possibility of joint activities to increase efficiency in detecting fraud and sharing experience and best practice.
1 The EMCS is operated under Decision No 1152/2003/ES of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 establishing an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products.
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO of the Czech Republic
Control number: 15/33
Subject of inspection: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the inspection: The aim of the SAO of the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties, in particular when monitoring transport in the system of conditional exemption from excise duties and when securing tax (customs debts); verify that the excise management system is set up to ensure the efficiency of the collection of revenue of the state budget.
Audited period: 2012-2015 and, in the case of factual contexts, the period preceding and subsequent
Audited person: Directorate-General of Customs
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO SR
Control number: KA-023/2016/1050
Subject of inspection: Administration of excise duties
Objective of the inspection: The aim of the inspection was an independent and objective examination of whether the FŘ SR and the customs authorities (CA) operate economically, efficiently and effectively in the administration of excise duties in accordance with generally binding legislation.
Audited period: 2012-2015
Audited person: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation for excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Excise legislation is divided into EU legislation (see Annex 1) and national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118/ES, on the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EHS, defines excise duty and defines the basic rules for the administration and management of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This Directive allows for the imposition of consumption taxes on other products.
In particular, EU legislation provides for minimum conditions for: the level of tax rates for the different types of products selected, the production, storage, processing and holding of taxable products, the taxation, exemption and refund, supervision of transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and the keeping of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows control procedures and institutes to be implemented at national level, provided they do not distort competition.
Excise legislation in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, excise legislation is concentrated in the Excise Tax Act (Act No. 353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of mineral oil taxes, alcohol taxes, taxes on tobacco products, beer taxes, taxes on wine and intermediate products and taxes on raw tobacco.
This Act defines the forms of handling of excise products, taxpayers, authorisation procedures, conditions for the transport of products, tax returns and penalties for infringements.
The Act and subsequent Decrees further regulate certain other conditions for the management of mineral oils (branding of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils and storage of raw tobacco for purposes other than the manufacture of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in parts 45 to 47 of Act No. 261/2007 Coll., on the stabilization of public budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are contained in special legislation. Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation regulates the conditions for the sale, supply, distribution of fuel and the keeping of records of fuel put into free circulation.
Act No. 61/1997 Coll., on alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol.
Act No. 307/2013 Coll., on the compulsory labelling of alcohol, and the relevant implementing provisions provide for compulsory labelling of alcohol in consumer packaging, conditions for the handling of control tapes and conditions for the handling of alcohol (i.e. for the production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, taking over, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
Tax procedures not specified in special regulations are governed by Act No. 280/2009 Coll., Tax Code.
Penalties are imposed by procedures under Act No. 500/2004 Coll., Administrative Regulations.
The conditions for issuing a trade licence (concession) for the operation of the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuels" and "production, preparation and sale of yeast alcohol, spirit and spirits" are regulated by Act No. 455/1991 Coll., on the Business Enterprise (Trade Act).
The Czech Republic has used the authorization to introduce control procedures and institutes for controlling the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to supervise compliance with legislation in the handling of selected products for which no excise duty has been paid, as well as in the handling of selected products for which the tax has already been paid.
These include monitoring the handling of specific mineral oils and raw tobacco, labelling of certain other mineral oils, labelling of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic used the right to apply excise duty to other products and introduced excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes to legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the Czech Government's Resolution of 3 October 2012 No 735, the implementation of the "zero tolerance plan for the black market in spirits," in 2012-2015 in the Czech Republic there were major legislative adjustments which introduced a number of measures against tax fraud on alcohol excise duty.
During the same period, there were major changes in the legislation concerning the mineral oil tax, the tobacco tax and the criminality of preparing tax cuts.
Criminal protection of tax revenues
With effect from 1.7.2016, the criminality of the preparation of the offence of "tax reduction, fee and similar compulsory payments" is introduced. The modifications made should allow police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, such as the deployment of operational search resources.
General provisions for the administration of excise duties
The issue of authorisations for the treatment of excise products under the Excise Duty Act shall be subject to: reliability with effect from the 1.1.2015; indebtedness; economic stability; authorisations to operate a trade enabling the performance of an authorisation-related activity; situations where the appellant is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
The aim of the legislation was in particular to address the issue of the creation of tax arrears by reducing entities authorised to handle products subject to excise duty.
The economic stability condition newly allows the tax administrator to take account of the financial situation of tax entities both in the authorisation procedure and after the authorisation has been issued.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities with insufficient financial revenue to properly discharge their tax obligations from handling selected products.
To assess the economic stability of the proposer, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) have been established on the basis of which a financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, the administrative discretion of the tax administrator depends on the individual conditions of the procedure.
The Act stipulates the periodicity of the examination of the fulfilment of the economic stability condition due to the timeliness of the data - the examination takes place once a year following the deadline for submission of the income tax return.
The tax administrator has the possibility to set other conditions necessary for the administration of the tax.
If the holder of the authorisation does not fulfil the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the authorisation or cancel it with delay.
Of the 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of arrears if the tax liability exceeds the amount of the tax security (e.g. repeat recipient).
The authorisation was revoked by 10 entities, the other applicants increased the tax security, capitalised their contribution to the company or supported the current accounting data according to which they already fulfilled all the conditions for issuing the authorisation.
In addition to the appellant, the conditions of reliability and indebtedness must be met by a natural person who is a statutory body or a member, or by a natural person who is not a statutory body of the appellant or a member of the appellant, but carries on such activity (chain of legal persons in the position of statutory body or its member, so-called linked entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30 000 linked entities had been screened.
Records kept under the Excise Tax Act (Sections 37 to Section 40 and Section 60 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) include information on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, taken over, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment (contingent exemption scheme, importation, re-entry into the suspension scheme, export, free circulation, own consumption, loss);
the identifier (SEED ID) of the recipient or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of the event and the registration;
transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carriers, transport numbers);
the registration numbers of the related documents;
notification of the entry into free circulation of the alcohol in the consumer package marked with the control tape and of its distribution.
The record of take-over after transport must be made immediately after its termination.
In the case of a record maintained electronically, the record must be kept or allowed to be output in xls, xlsx, ods.
Alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures designed to provide a detailed overview of the activities of the entities (see Annex 3, diagram A) from the production of raw alcohol to the labelling of the control tape to its distribution to the final seller or authorised user of exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, both the customs authorities and the production facilities for the production of alcohol, which is not in operation, are subject to supervision.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of the processing of alcohol and the production of spirits and to identify people handling liquor in consumer packaging, to reduce the treatment of alcohol to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most important measures are: The records of the production, receipt, stocks and dispensation of alcohol contain information on the quantity of alcohol according to the various stages of production and processing of alcohol with the identification of the document numbers.
Restrictions on the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and on the number of packages with broken control tape at the place of final sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other packaging of a volume of max. one litre or three litres if it is a container made of glass.
Spirits in larger packaging are regarded as unmarked, which are forbidden to dispose of.
At the point of final sale to the natural person for his personal consumption may be max. one consumer package with broken control tape, or three, if fitted with a one-way valve.
Compulsory registration of a person who places alcohol in consumer packaging products with at least 15% vol. of alcohol in free circulation and is: an importer of alcohol, a producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or an operator of a tax warehouse under suspension, provided that personal and technical conditions are met.
Personal conditions - reliability, integrity and non-expression of prohibition - must be met by the applicant and the person in the position of statutory authority or responsible representative.
The applicant must grant bail of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approximately €3,700 to €185,000) depending on the estimated amount of control tapes collected.
Technical conditions for registration are an appropriate place for marking the alcohol and equipment of the marking or tax warehouse by a camera tracking device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administrator.
The registration marking of the control tape is introduced for the marking of spirits of more than 0,06 litres.
In the case of transport of control belts, the registration mark of the control belts shall appear on the transport documents or export declaration.
The control tape for the 30.11.2013 contained a 10-digit registration code which included a four-digit registration sampling number, the application code for assignment of the control tapes and the classification code according to the level of ethanol volume concentration.
The control tape from 1. 12. 2013 newly contains two types of identifiers and the amount of alcohol in the consumer package expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 ° C, rounded to the whole millilitres downwards.
The registration of control tapes for the marking of spirits contains daily records of the different methods of handling the control tapes according to the registration codes as well as documents on the basis of which the registration took place.
In the event of the destruction, loss or theft of specific control belts, their holder shall notify the tax administrator by electronic means of the registration code of the control belts concerned and their number the following working day after the operative event.
Introduction of a new substance of offences and adjustment of the level of penalties imposed for infringements in the handling of surveillance tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to or exceeding the excise duty (e.g. in the event of destruction or loss of control belts in the number exceeding 0.1% of the total quantity of the individual control tape order carried out, if the check tape is not returned within the statutory period).
Limitation of handling of control tapes only to registered holders who may not refer them to another person, except to provide them to a foreign supplier for the purpose of labelling spirits in consumer packaging produced outside the Czech Republic.
The control tapes exported must be placed on consumer packaging and re-imported no later than nine months after taking over from the tax administrator.
Compulsory registration of the distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging provided the fulfilment of personal conditions similar to that of the person obliged to mark the alcohol and with the obligation to deposit up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approximately €185,000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of alcohol in consumer packaging.
Beneficiaries are obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or final sellers, or to sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency administrator, the administrative body, the organisational units of the state or unregistered persons in the exercise of tax execution.
Notices of entry into free circulation of alcohol or sales in consumer packaging shall be sent by the holders and distributors of alcohol immediately on the following day following the operative event to the tax administrator through the information system led by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or following the content in xml format.
The notification shall include the number of control tapes used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the percentage by volume of alcohol, the European Goods Code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or the final seller as well as the name of the product and the batch of production.
Tax entities sent approximately 10.5 million in 2014 and 2015. notification.
Compulsory concession (specific form of trade licence) not only for the production and treatment of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging by the entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or to another legal or business natural person for his own internal use.
Licensed trades may be exercised only after a decision has been taken by the Trade Licensing Office, subject to professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed competence is required for the sale of alcohol.
The tax administrator benefits from an overview of sellers and their establishments and restrictions
trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, for the field of production, preparation of yeast alcohol, spirits, spirits and other alcoholic beverages, sales were registered in the year 2014 approx. 94 thousand and in the year 2015 about 104 thousand concessions.
During their activities outside the tax administrations, the following include: Trade authorities, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection Authority, the Czech Financial Administration, the Czech Trade Inspection Authority.
If it finds that there has been an infringement or breach of the prohibition, it shall immediately inform the excise administrator thereof.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has introduced a comprehensive system of supervision (see Annex 3, scheme B), to which mineral oils burdened by excise duty are subject, but also selected mineral oils unburdened by excise duties that have been used for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from production of mineral oil through storage, transport, marking and colouring of selected mineral oils, branding of certain other mineral oils to delivery to the final consumer or user and in some cases to consumption of mineral oils.
Customs supervision shall include the production and handling of markers for the labelling of mineral oils.
The marking and colouring of the selected mineral oils shall be subject to the mineral oils listed under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (other kerosene), 2710 19 29 (other not elsewhere specified medium oils) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49, unless their marking is prohibited.
For example, benzol, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion are subject to the labelling of certain other mineral oils.
The marking and colouring of selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils by branding is possible only under the permission of the tax administration.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion) whose kinematic viscosity at 40 ° C is less than 12 mm2 s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following: the flash point is less than 150 ° C, distilling at least 20 per cent of the volume including losses up to 350 ° C during the distillation test.
These mineral oils have been misused as an additive to finished fuels, in particular diesel fuel, or have been directly used or sold for motor propulsion because the physical characteristics are very similar.
Entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres shall register with the tax administrator.
The personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory authority and the responsible representative shall be fulfilled for the issue of the registration, which shall be valid throughout the period 2 Except for beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by burning.
3 Council Regulation (EEC) No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 Eg. when mineral oil is used as propellant (excluding water navigation, unless it is a private recreational vessel) or as an ingredient for the production of fuels, if the labelling is for a defect in their use.
registration.
As of 30 December 2016, the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations, at the suggestion of the marketing authorisation holder, four registrations were cancelled.
