The electronic record shall contain detailed information on the receipt, consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil, including document numbers, notification numbers of acquisition by the tax authorities, storage and consumption places, purpose of consumption, place of storage and consumption or, on sale, place of delivery and registration number of the customer.
The notification of any acquisition of special mineral oil shall be made to the tax administrator between 24 and 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of the trading partners, the name and nomenclature of the special mineral oil, the quantity, the purpose of consumption or the information on sale or transfer shall be notified.
Notifications of the estimated quantity in the relevant year of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the calendar year concerned.
Notices of use and marking, place of storage or consumption, identification details of the person to whom the special mineral oil is further sold or transferred shall be transmitted before any change.
Notifications shall be made electronically via intelligent forms or by a data box in the PDF format.
In 2015, persons handling special mineral oils submitted 630 notifications.
Securing and forfeiture of special mineral oils or means of transport, if applicable, must be declared by the tax administrator in cases where it detects the treatment of special mineral oils without registration or where the registered person fails to fulfil his notification obligation.
As in the case of non-compliance with obligations for the transport of excise products, these deficiencies cannot be remedied additionally.
Registration of the fuel distributor is mandatory for persons who sell or are entitled to sell fuel.
Only persons meeting the following criteria may be registered fuel distributors:
Compulsory concession of the Trade Licensing Office (specific form of trade licence).
The customs office examining whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory authority or the members of the statutory authority of the applicant - the legal person and the appointed responsible representative fulfil the condition of reliability - shall provide an opinion on the application for the concession or, where appropriate, on the appointment of the responsible representative.
Where such persons fulfil the condition of reliability, the customs office shall issue an agreed opinion.
A reliable person is a person of integrity, in terms of criminal property character, customs and tax law.
The issue of a concession shall be subject to professional competence.
Indebtedness of the same range of persons as in the case of reliability.
The debtor is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will fulfil his payment obligations to the State properly and in a timely manner, i.e. he does not have arrears to the State budget and to general health insurance.
A fuel distributor shall not be prohibited by a court or administrative authority from carrying out an activity that prevents it from performing its activities.
The fuel distributor shall not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
Deposit deposit (or bank guarantee) of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. approximately €740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 after three years of registration of the fuel distributor and fulfilment of other conditions (i.e. approximately €370,000).
The distributor shall submit the fuel distribution notification to the customs office within 20 days of the end of the calendar month.
Electronic notifications shall include information on individual purchases and sales of fuel.
The notified data are data on business partners, document numbers, selected product, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The entitlement to refund of the tax on mineral oils consumed in agricultural primary production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
Refunds of excise duty on mineral oils may be claimed only in respect of an activity which appears to be related to an activity carried out on land.
In 2015 there were approximately 64 thousand claims for refund totalling CZK 1 172 844 680 (i.e. €43,401,720).
Since 2017, the Government of the Czech Republic has also introduced the refund of excise duty on fuel to farmers with livestock production.
Farmers or breeders, such as cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats, will be newly able to apply this right.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of old-rate tobacco products
In response to the long-term lack of budget revenue from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic, with effect from 1 December 2014, introduced restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with an old tax rate in the event of a change in the tax rate.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid using tobacco stickers.
Using a tobacco sticker means placing it on a unit package (Section 116 of the Excise Tax Act).
For the application of the excise duty rate, the production of the tobacco product is decisive in a state intended for the final consumer, without having to be removed, delivered, dispatched or sold or sold to the final consumer.
The alphabet letter characterising the rate of excise duty is indicated on the tobacco sticker together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, and the sticker indicates the number of packages and the quantity of tobacco to be smoked in kilograms.
Tobacco sticker has no identifier.
The duration of the transitional period for the sale of unit packages of cigarettes intended for direct consumption and bearing a tobacco sticker bearing the previous (old) rate of taxation has been fixed until the end of the last day of the second calendar month following the entry into force of the new excise duty rate.
The development of tobacco sticker withdrawals in 2014 and the comparison with previous years show that tobacco product manufacturers have significantly frontloaded tobacco products with an "old" tax rate each year, thereby effectively shifting the effectiveness of the "new" tax rate by about one year.
Raw tobacco tax
As a result of the abuse of raw tobacco for the manufacture of tobacco products without the authorisation of the tax administration and the non-enforcement of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco has been introduced as a measure against tax fraud.
With effect from 1.7.2015, excise duty shall be subject to raw tobacco which has not been used or delivered for the manufacture of tobacco products, delivered to another Member State or third country or for which the origin, purpose or person to whom raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been established.
Restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco
Measures such as surveillance of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, labelling of unit packs with control tape and restrictions on sales at designated locations have been supplemented by restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
Production facilities for processing tobacco raw materials and manufacture of tobacco products shall not be subject to customs supervision.
Only registered persons may store raw tobacco for purposes other than the manufacture of tobacco, but such tobacco may not be further processed or modified.
Only a person fulfilling the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory authority and the responsible representative may be a registered person, which is valid throughout the registration period.
The conditions of registration are: (a) the authorisation to operate a trade enabling the activities of a person storing raw tobacco, (b) reliability, (c) indebtedness, (d) the fact that a person storing raw tobacco has not been prohibited from carrying out his activities, (e) the fact that the person storing the raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, (f) granting bail of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. approximately €740,000).
The electronic record shall include the date of receipt or dispatch of raw tobacco, the document number, identification of the trading partner, the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco shall be made to the tax administrator between 24 and 72 hours before receipt or dispatch.
The details of the trading partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the storage address, the purpose of use and the carrier data shall be reported.
Notifications of the quantity foreseen for the relevant year of raw tobacco accepted or dispatched shall be submitted by the body together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the calendar year concerned.
Notifications shall be submitted electronically by the data box in the format of The ERC.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the prescribed requirements.
Legislation of excise duties in SR
The legal framework regulating excise duties in the Slovak Republic is based on EU legislation and thus complements its single tax system.
The various types of excise duties are taxed by the Slovak legislation, which is similar to the legislation of the surrounding countries.
Definition of legislation in the SR
The excise legislation is provided by four laws according to the subject matter of the tax.
Harmonisation was achieved by adopting the following excise laws: Act No 98/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No 106/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No 530/2011 Z. z., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No 609/2007 C. z., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All excise laws are rules of substantive law and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No. 563/2009 Z. z., on the administration of taxes (tax code), is a rule of procedural law, regulates the administration of taxes, rights and obligations of tax entities and other persons.
This legal framework transposed the various provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/ES of 16 December 2008 on the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EHS and transposed the provisions of other directives and legislation of the European Community.
Structure of amendments to legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject matter of control in the SR
Since 2011, the legislation on the administration of excise duties has undergone several major changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In the EMCS, the transport monitoring of selected excise products under the suspension scheme was changed from a documentary administrative accompanying document to an exclusively electronic system where such transport is monitored in real time.
The EMCS electronic system introduced in 2015 an institute to suspend tax access to EMCS.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
The customs office has the possibility to suspend access precisely in the event of a justified fear of non-payment or undetermined tax on previous tax periods and its non-enforceability.
This relates to the maturity of the tax, since the transport of excise goods requires the composition of the collateral, which is released by termination of transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A major change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the possibility of using so-called red diesel was abolished.
The marked gas oil, also commonly called red naphtha, was one of the mineral oils.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific legal purposes, e.g. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The aim of the abolition of red diesel was to reduce the general government deficit, simplify the system of mineral oil taxation and reduce the administrative burden on the businesses concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel seller.
The purpose of this legal change was to introduce a record keeping obligation for all service stations.
Clarification of the movements of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to purchase petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
In 2014, new tax institutes were introduced, namely the fuel distributor and the fuel consumer.
This amendment contributed to eliminating tax evasion for petrol and diesel and made the movement of these fuels more transparent (see Annex 4, Diagram A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
However, in the SR, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to designate an indication substance.
Excise duty on tobacco products
In the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of tobacco raw materials, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Material Act was expanded and a new tax entity was introduced - the tobacco raw material trader.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, the obligation to register technological equipment for the manufacture of tobacco products has been introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for labelling consumer packages of tobacco products.
Cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco are labelled with a stamp.
Under the new system, the customer of the stamps must request the customs office to issue the stamps electronically by means of an information system for the collection of the stamps.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was set up - in Mincovna Kremnice.
The exercise of tax supervision over the printing of control stamps was also introduced.
The changes contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system of printing control stamps strengthens the system of inspection of goods, because a unique identification number is generated on the stamp, through which it is easy to verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1-2 place) shall be the checksum; the third place determines whether the code belongs to a check stamp or to a group of packages; the 4th place is the identifier of the series; 5.-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9-12 place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
The cigarette labelling mark shall also indicate the price of cigarettes, the indication for the excise duty rate, the number of cigarette units in the consumer package and the length of cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer because the original three rules of substantive law were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The Act was drafted primarily because of the need for a comprehensive solution to the issue of taxation of alcoholic beverages, solutions to their production, monitoring of movements, provision of taxes, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, streamline the performance of tax administration, reduce administrative burdens for small and medium-sized entrepreneurs.
A new way of addressing the taxation of different types of alcoholic beverages introduced the application of a uniform excise duty rate to alcoholic beverages, taking into account the volume percentage of the actual alcohol content.
For still wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the volume percentage of the actual alcoholic strength by volume of the finished product shall be taken into account.
The concentration of beer shall also be expressed in volume per cent of the actual alcoholic strength by volume of the finished product.
A category of small-scale producer of fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is to exempt from excise duty a natural person who produces sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household of no more than 1000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for labelling consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the customer of the stamps must request the customs office to issue the stamps electronically by means of an information system for the collection of the stamps.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was set up - in Mincovna Kremnice.
The exercise of tax supervision over the printing of control stamps was also introduced.
The changes contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, diagram B) and the elimination of control stamp falsification.
The new system of printing control stamps strengthens the system of inspection of goods, because a unique identification number is generated on the stamp, through which it is easy to verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1-2 place) shall be the checksum; the third place determines whether the code belongs to a check stamp or to a group of packages; the 4th place is the identifier of the series; 5.-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9-12 place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common law no. 353/2003 Coll.
Tax on solid fuels, tax on natural gas and certain other gases and electricity tax are part of Act No. 261/2007 Coll.
By contrast, in the SR, each excise duty is regulated by a special law, except the Excise Duty on Alcoholic Beverages Act, which contains a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic from 1 January 2015, the issuance of an excise product authorisation under the Excise Tax Act is conditional, inter alia, on the demonstration of the economic stability of applicants, which the customs authorities annually verify by conducting a financial analysis.
In SR, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding to waive or reduce the tax security.
FŘ SR exercises tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of control stamps for the labelling of alcohol and tobacco products, their liquidation in the printing works and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of stamps is provided by the state-owned Mint Kremnica.
The production of tobacco stickers and control tapes in the Czech Republic is not subject to customs supervision in the printing works.
Tobacco stickers and control tapes shall be taken from the printing works in charge of the territorial office of the customs office in Kutná Hora.
Tobacco stickers are taken over by their customers at this territorial workplace, check strips for alcohol marking are further distributed to the respective local tax administrations according to the place of marking.
The legislation of the Czech Republic does not define manufacturers of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
In SR there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the manufacture of tobacco products or part thereof, in the Czech Republic such an obligation is not introduced.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco sticker bears excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when tobacco stickers are taken from the mandated customs office.
By contrast, in the SR, the mark does not contain excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced in the audited period if used for agricultural plant primary production, so-called green diesel.
As of 2017, this refund was extended to livestock production.
Such support for farmers is not introduced in the SR (it existed in the 31.12.2010 as so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of 20 million was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic. CZK (i.e. €740 thousand).
The introduction of this measure reduced the number of fuel distributors from 1,891 entities in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1,717 tax entities).
In SR, a similar institute of fuel distributors is introduced, but without the deposit required to ensure excise duty on mineral oils.
303 distributors were registered in the SR in 2014 and 407 distributors were registered in 2015.
The Institute of Fuel Dealer and Fuel Consumer is established in the SR and is authorised by the local customs office.
There is no such institute in the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils as well as some other mineral oils are subject to marking; in the Slovak Republic, the labeling of mineral oils is not applied after the abolition of so-called red diesel oil.
In the Czech Republic, the alcohol marking control tape contains an eight-digit individual code to verify the origin of the alcohol and a 12-digit registration code indicating the spirituality of the spirit drink according to which the registration of the control tapes is kept.
The destruction, loss, and return of the control tape are recorded in the registry the following business day.
The tape holder is obliged to notify the use of the tape within the same period.
In SR, the check mark intended for labelling alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number which, if used once a month, is communicated to the tax authority and used to verify the authenticity of the stamp.
The register contains the number of stamps collected, used and claimed.
Both the Czech Republic and SR have introduced the Institute of compulsory registration or registration of the distributor of alcohol.
In the SR, the registration shall be conditional on the fulfilment of conditions linked inter alia to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer alcohol of at least €100,000 or paid-up capital of at least €100,000; a minimum of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining registration is conditional, among other things, on the deposit of CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) for the benefit of the tax administrator for the entire period of validity of registration.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
In the SR, in the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging, the tax administrator is required to be present on a permanent basis.
In the Czech Republic, the production of alcohol in consumer packaging requires a special form of registration of a person obliged to mark alcohol with the condition of deposit in favour of the tax administrator from CZK 100,000 (i.e. €3,700) up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) according to the amount of control tapes removed and installation of tracking equipment with continuous access of the tax administrator.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic goes well beyond the minimum requirements of the EU for the subject matter and administration of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as those identified in tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax administrations to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
Excise duty on raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials has been introduced in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in addition to EU legislation to combat tax evasion in the form of abuse of tobacco raw materials.
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw materials are not harmonized tobacco products, both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic monitor their movement.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR may recommend that the measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the examination of economic stability of applicants for the issue of permits under the Excise Tax Act has proven to be effective because it reduces the risks of arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend applying such screening also in the SR conditions.
The distribution of control stamps is more efficient in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden the customs authorities with costs related to transport between the printer and the customer of control belts and tobacco stickers.
The financial administration of SR has a better overview of the existence and location of technological equipment for the manufacture of tobacco products.
However, the collection of tax on tobacco products is more effective in the Czech Republic, because the order of tobacco sticker itself is a tax return with subsequent payment of tax.
Thanks to the introduction of "fuel seller" and "fuel consumer" institutes, the financial administration in SR has a better overview of the locations of sales of fuel.
The introduction of compulsory labelling of mineral oils in the Czech Republic makes it easier to control the misuse of mineral oils with reduced tax rates or exempt ones.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and Slovakia (2014), a new control tape or stamp containing the identification code was introduced.
The surveillance tape in the Czech Republic also contains the registration code, while in the Slovak Republic the new legislation waived its listing.
Impacts cannot yet be assessed due to the short effectiveness of legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol with a check mark or tape is an effective measure to combat tax evasion.
The SAO SR and the SAO of the Czech Republic may recommend the introduction of this control measure also in other Member States.
The SR's position on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterised by a pro-entity approach that does not block the financial resources of tax entities.
By contrast, the approach of the Czech Republic is rather restrictive because it introduces a bail-out that burdens the cash flow of tax entities, but reduces the risk of arrears.
Evolution of excise revenue
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the State in order to increase the revenue of the State budget and also to regulate the quantity of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered harmful to the individual and/or to the company (regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Communication from the Commission: EUROPE 2020 - A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3 March 2010 under the flagship initiative A less resource-intensive Europe is the intention of the European Commission to improve the framework for market-based use of instruments, including by revising energy taxation to reduce energy consumption and resources.
In order to fulfil the EC's intention, Member States should seek to shift tax burdens from the labour force, inter alia, to energy and environmental taxation, as part of a greater "greening" of tax systems.
Collection of tax revenues from excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia includes collection of excise duties on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and share of GDP is also monitored by the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
Both supreme audit institutions used the following selection criteria to query the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties linked to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP decreased slightly according to OECD data.
The exchange rate of the ECB European Central Bank was used to convert amounts in CZK to € at 31 December of the year concerned.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against € in 2013 weakened by 9.1% year on year against 2012 (from 25,140 to 27,425).
This was mainly due to the monetary policy decision of the CNB Board of 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of excise duty collection, excise duty rates and per capita income in € have decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant reduction in the proportion of excise duties in 2014 was due to a one-off shortfall in excise revenue from tobacco products due to the impact of the new legislation restricting the sale of tobacco products at the old tax rate.
The proportion of excise duties is also influenced by the growth in income tax collection, which has significantly increased due to the improved overall economic situation of the Czech Republic.
The excise duty on mineral oils (about 55.7% in 2015) is the biggest contributor to the overall collection of excise duties, but it has declined despite significant economic growth compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duties on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although the registration of fuel distributors was introduced as a measure against tax fraud in 2013.
The trend of eco-efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels are negatively reflected in the tax revenue.
A negligible share is the natural gas tax, the solid fuel tax and the electricity tax, which is due to a low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to the surrounding states.
If tariffs are not raised, their share will decline in the future in view of the ever-decreasing energy performance of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the reverberations of a large case of tax fraud involving the placing into circulation of untaxed alcohol, alcohol containing methanol or poorly denatured alcohol in the form of spirits.
In 2015, following the adoption of a series of measures against such conduct and the revival of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the 2012 direct debits by €4 million.
The proportion of tax on tobacco products has increased as a result of increasing rates.
The basic rates of excise duties varied between 2012 and 2015 for the tobacco tax, where the rate was increased mainly due to compliance with the Council Directive on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
As a result of the CNB's monetary intervention, the real excise duty rate fell significantly in €, excluding the tobacco tax. It has risen only slightly in tobacco products.
There is no indexation of excise duty rates in relation to price growth, GDP or living standards, so the function of excise duties in regulating socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With economic growth in the Czech Republic and rising living standards, real excise duty rates are decreasing.
7 Indexation - automatic adjustment of a certain economic variable by inflation, this adjustment occurs on the basis of a law or contract (for pensions paid by the State it is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties linked to macroeconomic indicators in SR
The current legislation on excise duties in SR does not address the indexation of excise duty rates on consumer price developments because they are fixed.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Of all the excise duties introduced in Slovakia, the excise duty on mineral oils has the largest share of the year-round tax revenues of the state budget, while it has not fallen below 52% throughout the audited period.
The second largest share is the excise duty on tobacco products.
On average, this tax accounts for around 32% of the total excise duty collection.
Between 2012 and 2015, excise duty collection per capita of SR increased.
This development is due to an increase in the rates of excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The increase in collection of excise duties per capita of SR is constant and corresponds to the development of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the reduction in income in € per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention in the exchange rate of the koruna against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which is approximately 2.7 and 2.8 times higher in the Czech Republic, but the collection for these selected products is only about 1/3 higher per person.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK versus € for foreign consumers.
The tax on mineral oils also causes greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of tobacco products tax, increasing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a significant impact.
Evaluation The real rate of excise duties in the Czech Republic decreased as a result of CNB interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in total tax revenues is not increasing and there is no departure from labour taxation to taxation of consumption of selected excise products, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the achieved values of the proportion of excise duties are consistently above the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is mainly influenced by the change in excise duty rates, the development of economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future drawdowns of excise duties due to environmental measures subsidised by the State in various forms will have to be compensated by other revenues or reductions in State expenditure.
Due to the lack of indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, their regulatory functions are reduced and the EU's objectives of less dependent on environmentally inexpensive sources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco are underpinned.
Higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic reflects higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and income related to excise tax administration, i.e. the amount of expenditure per 100 units of income (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The efficiency of the tax administrator in the administration of the tax affects the scope and organisational arrangements of the tax administration, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of electronisation of individual activities.
The calculation of the administrative costs of the tax administration using the conversion rate method is based on the number of employees involved in the management of excise duties in the liner-controlled structure.
In the Czech Republic, in addition to other activities, excise duties are administered by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate branch of the state and an accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax administration is provided by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities being the internal organisational unit, the costs and revenues are included collectively for the whole organisational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility of comparing the efficiency of excise tax administration to the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs, expenditure and revenue of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were included.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative tasks performed mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some sub-controls are carried out by other public authorities, but their importance is negligible.
In particular, the following departments shall administer excise duties:
Directorate-General of Customs
DEPARTMENT 23 TAX
Section 231 - Tax Methodologies monitors and proposes legislative measures, ensures interpretation of legislation, methodologically manages and coordinates: implementation of tax management agendas and related regulations, in particular tax proceedings and related control and surveillance activities, administration of transport of selected products;
Department 232 - ELO and Search conducts search and methodically controls transport of selected products and ensures international cooperation between ELO and EMCS;
Section 233 - Tax controls shall methodically manage and coordinate the implementation of the tax control agenda at customs offices;
Department 30 LEGAL
Section 301 - Legal activities in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative procedure, tax control process, registration procedure, finding procedure, payment of taxes, fines for late claims of tax, penalty payments and interest;
Section 302 - Administrative activities carry out decision-making activities in cases where the legislation provides for the competence of the DG, e.g. the decision on the delegation of the local jurisdiction of the entity to another relevant tax administrator, the decision on the attraction, i.e. the taking over of the matter by the tax administrator, the appeal against the decisions of the customs authorities and the examination of the instigation of inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Section 303 - Management of revenue and recovery methodologically manages, coordinates and performs tasks in the context of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the performance of insolvency management tasks;
Section 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION SUPPORT
Section 601 - Risk and Criminal Analysis ensures and carries out risk analyses and contributes to managing executive risks and planning control activities and control actions;
Section 604 - Financial analyses are carried out in the customs administration, in particular under the authorisation procedure.
Customs offices carry out agenda activities in different locations in the region and the agendas are dispersed in several locations:
Section 02 - Analysis and information support for risk analysis, risk profile management and collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Department 1 LEGAL
Section 11 - Legal and administrative activities which process supporting documents, opinions and submission reports for the appellate body, issue authorisation decisions in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the Act on compulsory labelling of alcohol and the Act on alcohol, decide on securing payment for a tax not yet in force or yet fixed;
Section 3 - TAX
Section 31 - Taxation, which carries out the agendas: tax supervision for tax entities, e.g. monitoring compliance with the conditions laid down in the authorisations issued, supervision of the functionality and regularity of the production facility for the production of alcohol and determination of quantities and concentrations for the alcohol produced, professional supervision for the denaturing of alcohol, physical control in the field of excise duty management; non-tax controls in the field of controls based on laws having an indirect relationship with excise duties, in particular, checking the compulsory labelling and colouring of selected mineral oils, checking the taxation of selected products, checking the labelling of tobacco products, checking that sellers or buyers do not violate the Price Act and other price regulations; perform acts in connection with the Fuel Act, perform acts in connection with the Act on Compulsory Labelling of Alcohol and the Act on Alcohol, carry out operations in connection with the fulfilment of the obligation of a minimum quantity of biofuels for free circulation for transport purposes; registration of tax operators, registration of persons obliged to label alcohol and liquor distributors and registration of fuel distributors; the administration of taxes, in particular the conduct of tax proceedings on the assessment and prescription, where appropriate the refund, the monitoring of the collateral and its application to the payment of tax, the conduct of searches;
Department 39 - Tobacco Stickers and Control Tapes - is the organizing unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemia Region and carries out activities in the field of ordering, manufacturing and distribution and disposal of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
For the disposal of returned/damaged tobacco stickers, representatives of the customs office as well as representatives of the GTC are present to supervise and record the winding-up process.
In the case of alcohol marking belts, the Director of Customs shall, by an internal management act, appoint a three-member committee to dispose of the discarded unrecovered/returned shredding controls.
After the physical shredding of the control belts, the Chairman of the Winding-up Committee shall ensure that the data on the destroyed surveillance tapes are recorded;
Department 5 - CONTROLS,
Section 52 - Tax controls are carried out by tax controls;
Department 6 - SUPERVISION
Unit 61 - Supervising entities supervises entities at sales points, e.g. control of sales of spirits and tobacco products;
Department 62 - Mobile Surveillance performs traffic control of selected products on the way.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in SR
Since 1 January 2012, the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a difficult transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The formation of FŘ SR was also reflected in the composition of employees of the newly formed departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In connection with the administration of excise duties, activities related to the administration of excise duties within the organisational structure of FŘ SR have been integrated into a number of different sections and related trade unions.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Section of Customs and Tax FŘ SR Department of Excise Duties (Customs):
excise separation - regulates and coordinates excise management activities; draw up expert opinions; submit proposals and comments on legislative amendments; issue a decision on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax entities; assign and delete registration sampling numbers;
Department of Tax Supervision - regulates and coordinates activities in the field of tax supervision and tax control; exercise tax supervision;
ELO and SPD Systems - regulates and coordinates the activities of mutual administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through SEED and MVS; ensure management and updates in SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
control stamp separation - regulates printing and stamp handling activities; carry out tax supervision of the disposition and disposal of printing sheets and stamps in the printing works.
Department of the Vice President of Financial Administration
Department of Excise and Customs Remedies (Customs):
excise remedies - review the decisions of the customs authorities on the basis of the ordinary and extraordinary remedies applied; the appeal procedure at the second stage of the decision-making process.
The Customs Section was established during 2012; each customs office (9 customs offices), which has territorial responsibilities determined by the higher territorial units, has been directly incorporated under it, with the exception of one customs office which has been established, inter alia, to carry out tasks in connection with the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
separation of excise duties - carrying out methodological activities in relation to branches of customs offices and customs stations; for selected entities, the tax administrator performs direct acts, namely the registration (tax warehouse, authorised recipient repurposed, registered consignor), the amount of collateral, determination and refund, tax supervision and tax control; decides to waive the composition of the security; decides to waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee in the tax warehouse for alcohol;
separation of laws - decision-making activities in respect of infringements of tax legislation; activities related to sound and exceptional remedies; tax enforcement proceedings;
Branch Office - decides on registration (except tax warehouse, authorised recipient for re-admission, registered consignor), amount of collateral; prescribe and refund the tax; exercise tax supervision and tax control; decide on security and on the forfeiture of goods;
customs office station - exercise of tax supervision over the holding and movement of excise goods; ensure the exercise of permanent tax supervision in the alcohol tax warehouse; decide on security and on the forfeiture of goods.
Expenditure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic on the administration of excise duties is constantly increasing, as investments in efficient tax administration and electronisation of financial administration increase with the exception of wage growth.
Although excise revenues have increased, IT adjustments related to UNITAS have increased more rapidly.
Wage expenditure is significantly affected by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol, which is not applied by the Czech Republic.
The expenditure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic on the administration of excise duties increased significantly in 2015 between 2012 and 2015, mainly due to the increase in wage expenditure and expenditure on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, excise revenue grew at about the same rate.
Wage expenditure in the Czech Republic is positively influenced by the wider competences of the customs administration, e.g. weighing trucks, controlling the fulfilment of obligations in connection with myth.
The efficiency of administrative costs in the SR shows a slightly deteriorating trend year on year.
The number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee increased.
The number of employees in the Czech Republic did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee compared to the Slovak Republic grew more slowly.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, wage growth is an important factor in the impaired efficiency of administrative expenditure, which can be assessed as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining considerable administrative burdens in the management of excise duties appears to be a negative factor, as confirmed by the non-decreasing number of employees in excise tax management.
However, in the Slovak Republic, the administration of excise duties with lower revenues is significantly more demanding on personnel capacities.
Performance indicators for excise duty management
Excise duty management is a set of activities aimed at correctly identifying, determining and securing the payment of the tax.
The main processes in the administration of excise duties are tax assessment, authorisation and registration for business, traffic supervision, control and search of tax entities.
The numbers of administrative operations and managed entities are indicators of the performance of the tax administration.
The correlation between the observed indicator and the number of tax administrations expresses the efficiency of the tax administration's activities and defines the cost of the specific activity.
Authorisations and marketing authorisations are essential for the handling and transport of selected products for commercial purposes under suspension.
The tax administrator is obliged to carry out continuous administration for entities authorised or registered with a focus on the supervision of compliance with the laws and conditions laid down by the tax administrator, to which adequate personnel resources must be allocated.
The reference indicator was the number of valid authorisations or registrations to operate at 31 December of each year.
The number of authorisations or registrations issued is not identical to the number of tax entities.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in the case.
The administrative activities monitored are the most significant acts of the tax administration (claims of tax, administration of transport in the EMCS), or activities that are a sequence of actions concluded by a report or decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Authorisation and registration to operate in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
It is possible to manufacture, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under the permission of the tax administration to operate a tax warehouse.
If the tax warehouse operator has multiple warehouses, a permit shall be issued for each individually, including tax collateral.
Tax protection is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administration (i.e. the physical presence of an official and the provision of equipment by the tax administrator's conclusions).
In the Czech Republic, permanent tax supervision is not applied.
The tax warehouse operator also registers for tax pursuant to Section 125 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.
The authorisation to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products conditionally exempted from the import point to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to an export point in another Member State or to a recipient in another Member State (replaces the status of registered consignor pursuant to Art. Article 4 (2) 10 of Council Directive 2008/118/EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include permits for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels without tax, which are analogies of tax warehouse permits.
The brewer produces alcohol with a reduced 50% tax rate (14,300 CZK/hl ethanol) - fruit distillates for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and the operating permit is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced rate of tax may be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per household of the grower intended for personal consumption for the production period (July-June).
The registration of the cultivation burning held by the operators of the batch and made available by the tax authorities shall include information on the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
The eligible recipient for the re-admission of the selected products and the authorised recipient for the one-off acceptance of the selected products shall be entitled, under the authorisation of the tax administrator and the conditions laid down, to accept or repeat the selected products under a conditional system transported from another Member State.
The beneficiary is not the operator of the tax warehouse and may not store or dispatch the selected products under suspension.
The user of selected exempt products is a legal or natural person who receives and uses, or according to Section 52a or Section 53 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll. sells to another user selected exempt products; users have the status of tax entities without the obligation to register for tax.
Exempt products may be accepted and used only on the basis of a final authorisation, and only from the supplier specified in the authorisation.
Under the authorisation, exempt mineral oils may be sold to another holder of a use permit or user authorised to use mineral oils without authorisation.
Mineral oils exempt from tax may be sold without authorisation in statutory cases such as:
waste oils of less than 10 000 litres per calendar year, if produced or produced by the user in its operation;
selected mineral oils exempt from tax in unit packs of not more than 20 litres intended for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production and at the same time intended for sale to the final consumer.
Exempt products may be transported with a proof of exemption.
The distributor of alcohol in the consumer package is entitled to sell or otherwise transfer the alcohol put into free circulation after compulsory registration with the tax administration.
The storekeeper of raw tobacco is entitled to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products on the basis of registration with the tax administrator and the conditions laid down.
The person handling the special mineral oils is entitled to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils, which are in bulk or placed in packs exceeding 220 litres, on the basis of registration with the tax administrator and the conditions laid down.
The fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel on the territory of the Czech Republic on the basis of the issued concession and registration of the tax administration under the specified conditions, except for the sale of fuel from the service station.
The transport of the PHM must be accompanied by a tax document, a sales document or a transport document, or a distribution plan and rollovers.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent before the start of transport to the tax authorities.
The petrol station operator owns the fuel sold at the service station.
Petrol stations are places where the sale or supply of PHM to a fuel tank is permitted under the permission of the building authority.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators broken down into: registered - normal sale or supply of PHM usually to fuel tanks of vehicles; with a defined approach - operating generally in different company premises (e.g. quarries, saws, agricultural farms, transport organisations, construction yards), the sale is made for the other party on the basis of specific contractual relations; non-public - fuel dispensing points for the own consumption of operators only.
A service station is not a construction or equipment in the form of an operating tank located in operation (e.g. on a chassis) if the fuel is issued only for own use.
Operating tanks are not subject to the authorisation of the tax administration and are not registered.
Natural and legal persons may purchase, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free circulation for resale under the permission of the tax administrator.
They shall be authorised even if they purchase or obtain liquefied petroleum gases for their own consumption exceeding 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative operations in the Czech Republic
Tax control is a set of actions. The subject of the tax control is the tax liability, the claim of the tax entity or other circumstances applicable to the correct detection and determination of the tax relating to one tax proceeding.
Tax control can be carried out jointly for multiple tax procedures of one tax entity.
A repeated tax check may be carried out only under the conditions and justification laid down by law when the check is initiated.
The tax control is carried out within a period of three years for the determination of the tax, the period being extended by one year under statutory conditions (e.g. submission of additional tax proceedings, initiation of criminal proceedings in connection with the tax in question) or is suspended (judicial proceedings, international cooperation).
The period for determining the tax ends no later than 10 years after the expiry of the deadline for submitting an ordinary tax claim.
The tax administrator is not required to carry out a tax check on each tax entity.
The start of the tax check sets the deadlines for filing additional tax returns or additional accounts by the tax entity (Section 141 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.) and restarts the deadline for determining the tax (Section 148 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
On the basis of its result, an official tax may be determined.
The local investigation is an individual time-limited act (one day) in which the tax administrator seeks evidence and examines premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and transport packaging for tax entities and other persons involved in the administration of taxes, on the spot outside the tax administration's premises (e.g. at the sales point, on the road).
The tax administrator is entitled to borrow documents and items, take samples or arrange them.
On the basis of the result of the local investigation, the tax cannot be assessed separately, but the tax entity may be invited to submit an additional tax return (Section 145 para. 2 of Act No. 280/2009 Coll.).
Checking traffic data in the EMCS is not a local investigation.
Only the registered person obliged to mark the alcohol may place the order of alcohol labelling belts at the local marking point and is carried out using intelligent forms that are automatically imported into the alcohol labelling register application.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the ordered quantity of control tapes and orders production.
They do not oversee the production of control belts.
The production is provided by the State Price Printing Company, a state-owned company.
The control tape customer receives the control tapes from the tax administrator of the locally applicable marking point.
The order of tobacco labels for cigarettes, cigarettes, cigars and tobacco for smoking is a tax return.
The value of the tobacco sticker corresponds to the amount of the tax liability and the purchaser of the tobacco stickers is obliged to pay their value within 60 days of their removal from the tax administration.
The customer is obliged to calculate in the order itself the value corresponding to the amount of tax obligation ordered tobacco stickers.
This period applies only if the value of tobacco stickers is secured.
The order of tobacco stickers is made on a form specified by the Ministry of Finance in writing or via a data box with the possibility of using smart forms.
The production of tobacco stickers is ensured by the State Price Printer, a state-owned company.
The authorised tax administrator, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemia Region (Kutná Hora Territorial Office), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax administrator, who further distributes them and further checks their transport, storage and use with the customers.
Tax claims include regular tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including tobacco sticker orders, filed by tax entities.
The declaration of tax under the customs procedure on the basis of customs declarations and the declaration of the claim for refund of tax on: mineral oils used for the production of heat, other petrol used in the course of business other than for the production of heat or engine propulsion, mineral oils used for agricultural primary production are not included.
The fines imposed include administrative proceedings to deal with infringements detected, which are a set of successive administrative acts. The International Exchange of Information on Tax Entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 shall take the form of: a request for administrative cooperation, replies to a request for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, event reports, inspection reports.
Transport under suspension between the Czech Republic and EU Member States - the Czech customs office is the tax administrator of the receiving or dispatching tax warehouse or authorised beneficiary.
Performance indicators in SR
Authorisation and registration to operate in SR
The administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic is provided primarily by the customs offices and the Excise Department of the Customs and Tax Section of FŘ SR, whose procedures for the administration of excise duties are governed by individual laws on excise taxes and the tax code.
These laws determine not only the scope of authorisations for the CA and FŘ SR in the administration of excise duties, but also the rights and obligations of tax entities in connection with the registration or payment of excise duties.
The largest year-on-year increase in tax entities (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, due to an increase in tax warehouse permits issued, an increase in the registration of the authorised recipient for re-admission and the registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation has clarified the transport of certain bulk mineral oils as well as the notification obligation, if transported freely or in packaging of more than 150 litres, or 230 litres, as well as an extension of the list of mineral oils subject to control and transport procedure, other goods, e.g. anti-tapping products, oxidative inhibitors, bituminous inhibitors, products to improve viscosity, anti-corrosive products.
A mandatory indication concerning the indication of their kinematic viscosity has been introduced for lubricating oils.
An approximation of the registration process for selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in SR is provided in the following sections of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Within the national legislation of SR, when registering the tax warehouse operator in the context of all excise duties, the person wishing to operate the tax warehouse must also apply simultaneously for the registration and issuing of permits for the operation of the tax warehouse.
The resulting decision in the registration process is the excise registration certificate, by which the tax warehouse operator acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CA grants permission to operate a tax warehouse, which entitles the tax warehouse operator in that tax warehouse to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under suspension.
If the tax warehouse operator has tax warehouses in multiple locations, the tax administrator will issue a separate permit for each tax warehouse to operate the tax warehouse.
The transport of an excise subject under suspension is monitored electronically via the EMCS.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport.
ARC code under which the said transport can be monitored online and therefore in real time.
Where the tax warehouse operator is also a person authorised to distribute alcohol, he shall notify the CA electronically of the commercial name of the consumer packaging of alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer packaging of alcohol and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer package which he places in free circulation, at the latest on the date of its introduction.
Registered sender
The registered consignor is a special type of tax entity which cannot be registered as a tax warehouse operator at the same time, even if it dispatches the excise duty subject under suspension after release for free circulation.
Under the national legislation of the SR, when registering a registered consignor under all excise duties, a person wishing to dispatch an excise duty subject under the suspension procedure after release for free circulation for the customs procedure must simultaneously apply to the CA for registration and issuing an authorisation to send the excise duty subject under that procedure.
The CA shall issue a certificate of registration for the excise duty concerned and at the same time issue an authorisation to dispatch the excise duty subject under the suspension procedure after its release for free circulation.
Growing brandy
The basic operation for the operation of the cultivated brandy is to obtain a permit for the production of alcohol in the distillery plant from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development SR.
However, the authorization itself from the Ministry does not entitle the holder of the permit to operate the cultivated brandy.
In order for a person to operate a cultivated brandy, he must submit an application to the CA for registration and certification of registration of the producer.
The CA shall issue a certificate of registration for the excise duty in question, which at the same time entitles the producer of the brandy to produce the alcohol in the growing fuel.
The purpose of the growing fuel is to provide services to growers.
Cultivation brandy cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislator allows for a reduced tax rate of 50% of the basic tax rate, i.e. €540/hl, to be applied to alcohol produced in the breeder's brandy.
The reduced rate of taxation shall apply to alcohol produced in the growing fuel in quantities not exceeding 43 l and. one grower and his household per production period in the tax territory.
The production period runs from 1 July of the current year to 30 June of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year and it is therefore possible to apply a reduced rate of tax to the alcohol produced more than once within one calendar year because the alcohol is produced in two production periods.
This involves the production of alcohol outside the suspension scheme, which in practice means that the alcohol produced is in free circulation.
The breeder shall pay not only the excise duty and value added tax for the alcohol produced, but also the price for the services provided.
The breeder's brandy shall issue to the farmer a removal certificate which serves not only as proof of origin and method of acquisition of the alcohol but also as proof of payment of excise duty.
The transport of alcohol thus produced is not subject to monitoring by the tax administrator.
Importer of consumer packaging
National legislation allows persons who intend to import consumer packaging of alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third State and put it into free tax circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CA for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
The importer of consumer packaging shall not register for the relevant excise duty, but the CA shall issue a certificate of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packaging.
That certificate entitles the importer to import consumer packaging of alcohol or consumer packaging of cigarettes from the territory of a third State.
At the same time, before issuing the stamps, they must lodge a tax guarantee equal to the amount of alcohol or cigarettes they wish to put into free circulation.
The importer of consumer packaging must put into free circulation only consumer packaging marked with a check mark.
They must therefore submit to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the control stamps exported to the territory of a third State.
On importation, the importer is required to certify by the customs office of import the number of stamps imported back from the territory of a third State.
When importing consumer packaging, the importer shall proceed within the meaning of customs legislation, where the amount of excise duty is also part of the customs debt.
In the event of the release of consumer packaging into free circulation, the tax guarantee lodged shall be repaid to the importer or may be used to pay the customs debt.
The importer of consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
Where the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol is also a person authorised to distribute alcohol, he shall notify the CA electronically of the commercial name of the consumer packaging of alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer packaging of alcohol and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer package which he places in free circulation, at the latest on the date of its introduction.
Retailer of consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free circulation and eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute for the retailer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a permit for sale must apply to the CA for a permit and comply with the statutory conditions (trade authorisation for commercial activity; integrity in relation to intentional economic offences; she has not been withdrawn from the sales permit for 10 years; is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As this is a consumer package of alcohol in free circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice containing also the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation is sufficient to demonstrate the method of acquisition of consumer packaging of alcohol.
The holder of the authorisation shall keep for each establishment, for a calendar month, a record of the number of consumer packages of alcohol accepted, the number of consumer packages of alcohol issued, the stock of alcohol in the consumer packaging of alcohol on the last day of the month and the registration of shortages or surpluses in the number of consumer packages of alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the authorisation shall only purchase or otherwise withdraw alcohol in consumer packaging from the person authorised to distribute in the course of the business.
Distributor of consumer alcohol packaging
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free circulation and eliminate tax evasion, the legislator introduced a new tax institute distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person who intends to hold a distribution permit must apply to the CA for a distribution authorisation.
The applicant must comply with the legal conditions (trade licence for commercial trade; storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer alcohol of at least €100,000 or paid-up capital of at least €100,000; a minimum of 10 employees; has no arrears towards the customs office; has no arrears on compulsory levies; integrity in relation to intentional economic offences; he has not been withdrawn from the sales permit for 10 years; is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As this is a consumer package of alcohol in free circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice containing also the number of the holder of the distribution authorisation is sufficient to demonstrate the method of acquisition of consumer packaging of alcohol.
For each establishment, the holder of the distribution authorisation shall keep a register for each calendar month of the number of consumer packages of alcohol accepted, the number of consumer packages of alcohol issued, the stocks of alcohol in consumer packaging on the last day of the month and the registration of shortages or surpluses in the number of consumer packages of alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the distribution authorisation shall only purchase alcohol in the consumer package from another person authorised to distribute.
The person authorised to distribute shall notify the data for each calendar month electronically by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel dealer
Due to the monitoring of fuels in free tax circulation as well as the elimination of tax evasion, a new type of tax entity has been introduced, namely the fuel seller.
There is no specific regulation governing service stations in the territory of SR.
Therefore, the petrol stations in the SR national legislation are incorporated as fuel sellers.
Person wishing to sell petrol in free circulation in the course of business activities in the tax territory, diesel or LPG for final consumption, is obliged to apply to the CA for an authorisation to sell before the sale begins and to provide proof of proof, that the storage facility is certified and equipped with an appropriate validated measuring device to measure the amount of mineral oil at intake and dispensing, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
If the propellant seller is a tax warehouse operator, authorised consignee or registered consignor, the CA shall also automatically issue an authorisation for the sale of propellants to registered persons.
The fuel dealer is obliged to keep records of purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG for a calendar month, among other legal obligations, and is also obliged to notify the CA of the new fuel supplier (distributor).
The fuel dealer is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise remove propellants only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
However, when delivering propellants through the autocistern, the distributor prints the so-called bottles from the measuring equipment built into the autocistern.
That document shall include, in addition to the information relating to the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate.
For example, an invoice containing the fuel distributor number allocated by the tax authority is sufficient to demonstrate the method of acquisition of propellants.
The tax administrator in the territory of SR records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods in the exercise of tax supervision of mineral oils.
This is primarily an attempt to avoid roadside checks during transport, which is why hauliers use secondary road roads, bypassing the toll selection system due to more difficult monitoring of actual traffic.
Transports of mineral oils in converted tanks with double bottom are also carried out.
Many times, illegal traffic is accompanied by a vehicle that reports possible mobile patrols to the carrier in order to change the route and avoid road control.
There is also mixing of propellants with light heating oils or waste oils.
Fuel distributor
Due to the monitoring of fuels in free tax circulation, as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity has been introduced, namely the fuel distributor.
A person who intends to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in the tax territory in the course of a business activity in free circulation of petrol, diesel or LPG shall, before the start of distribution, apply to the customs office for a distribution permit and provide proof that the storage facility is certified and equipped with appropriate verified measuring equipment, as well as a list of suppliers and customers
The fuel distributor is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep separate records of the purchased and sold petrol, diesel or LPG for each establishment per calendar month.
The fuel distributor is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise remove propellants only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
The fuel distributor may only sell to a fuel distributor, registered person or fuel consumer in the tax territory.
However, when delivering propellants via the autocistern, the distributor prints, when pumping fuel, the fuel dealers and the fuel consumers respectively, the so-called bottles from the measuring equipment built into the autocistern.
That document shall include, in addition to the information relating to the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate.
As these are fuels in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice containing the number of the distributor of propellants or registered persons allocated by the tax administrator is sufficient to demonstrate the method of acquisition of propellants.
Fuel consumer
The consumer of fuel has a special position in national legislation.
A person who purchases petrol, diesel or LPG in the tax territory in free circulation for his own consumption and stores such mineral oil in a storage facility of 15 000 litres or more shall notify the customs office of that fact at the latest before first being placed in storage.
Consumers of fuel shall be registered by the customs office.
In addition to the legal facts, he is obliged to indicate the location of the storage facility.
In practice, they are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
Storage equipment shall be verified and fitted with a measuring device enabling the quantity of propellants to be measured at the time of receipt and dispensing (static mark, measurement bar).
The tank shall comply with technical standards.
The fuel consumer must only purchase propellants from a fuel distributor or a registered person.
As they are fuels in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for transport.
However, when delivering the propellants via the autocistern, the distributor prints the so-called bottles from the measuring equipment incorporated in the autocistern when pumping the propellants to the consumer.
That document shall also include the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate, in addition to the quantity data.
For example, an invoice containing the fuel distributor number allocated by the tax authority is sufficient to demonstrate the method of acquisition of propellants.
The tax administrator in the territory of SR records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods in the exercise of tax supervision of mineral oils.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who produces beer within the business and meets the legal conditions.
If the conditions laid down by law are met, a small independent brewery may apply a reduced tax rate, i.e. €2,652 per hl/percent of the volume of the actual alcoholic strength.
Annual beer production is limited to up to 200 000 hl of beer.
Since beer is produced outside the suspension scheme, an accompanying document is not required for transport as it is in free circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, they are small family businesses that also operate restaurants or bars in which they offer beer of their own production for sale.
Administrative operations in the SR
This subheading approximates the exercise of excise tax administration tax supervision for selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in SR.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative operations (by 5.3%) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, which was due to the realisation of more transfers in the EMCS.
By contrast, the largest decrease was recorded in 2014, up to 4.3%, due to fewer tax checks completed and fewer tax returns filed.
The decrease concerned legislative changes.
Tax checks
By exercising tax control, the CA detects or verifies the facts determining the correct determination of the tax.
Employees of the CA shall be shown the tax inspection mandate, which includes, inter alia, the purpose and object of the audit and the extent of the tax periods audited.
In practice, this means that the audited tax period may be one month, but also more tax periods.
The scope of the controlled tax periods is determined by the CA.
