The tax check begins with the registration of the commencement of the tax check.
The CA will confirm the receipt of the documents.
The CA is obliged to return the leased documents within 30 days from the end of the tax check.
The CA employee shall draw up a protocol from tax control.
If the tax check identifies a difference in the sum to be paid, declared or claimed by the audited tax entity, the CA, together with the Protocol to the audited tax entity, shall also send an invitation to comment on the findings set out in the Protocol.
The tax check is terminated on the date of receipt of the protocol.
The period for carrying out the tax check shall be no more than one year from the date of its initiation.
The tax check for registered persons and selected registered persons shall be carried out as necessary, but at least once until the date of termination of the right to tax, which is 5 years.
FŘ SR issued an internal management act adjusting the above mentioned deadlines due to the single tax administration procedure in the territory of SR.
Local investigations
A local investigation is the activity of the tax administrator in which it searches for evidence, examines and identifies the facts that are needed for the purposes of tax administration.
The CA employee records the local investigation and submits the copy to the taxpayer.
In carrying out the local investigation, the CA employee has the right to unrestricted access to land, operating buildings, rooms and places, including means of transport, transport packaging and accounting documents.
The clearing of the quantities of alcohol produced shall be established in the form of a local investigation.
The facts established are the basis for the exercise of tax control.
In the course of the local investigation, the CA is entitled to take samples as well as to secure the matter.
The FR SR issued an internal management act regulating the exercise of tax supervision and local investigations for individual excise duties subjects in order to harmonise the procedures of the tax administration.
Permanent tax oversight in tax warehouses for alcohol
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1.5.2004, there was also a change in excise tax management.
The need for more efficient spending of the state budget in administering alcohol excise duty, improving the business environment in the area and introducing legislative instruments to more effectively suppress the grey economy in the area resulted in the adoption of new laws in 2004 in connection with the administration of excise duties.
One of the measures brought about by the new legislative change was not only the transfer of the tax administrator in the field of excise administration from the tax offices to the customs offices, but also the introduction of the need for a tax administrator in the tax warehouse to alcohol.
In the territory of SR, national legislation determines that it is only possible to receive, issue, produce or process alcohol in the tax warehouse in the presence of a CA employee.
This does not apply to a tax warehouse which receives, stores or dispatches alcohol only in the consumer packaging of alcohol.
At the same time, the CA is obliged to secure employees in the tax warehouse so that the income, supply, production or processing of alcohol is not restricted.
The tax warehouse operator is obliged to ensure the conditions of the working environment for CA employees.
Based on the contract concluded with FŘ SR, the CA pays the rental costs to the tax warehouse operator on a monthly basis.
In the tax warehouse for the production, processing or storage of alcohol, the production facility for the storage of alcohol shall be so adapted as to enable the quantity of alcohol produced, the alcohol processed, the alcohol stored, including the alcohol and alcohol contained therein to be ascertained at any time.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Where alcohol is not accepted, dispensed, produced or processed in a tax warehouse, the customs office may waive the obligation to ensure the presence of a customs office employee, which it is obliged to secure by closing the customs office.
However, this option is not used very often in practice because tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of a customs employee to their advantage.
Some tax warehouse operators use the legal option within the meaning of Act No 467/2002 Z. z., on the production and marketing of alcohol, and use the production facility for the production of alcohol at the distillery for the cultivation and also for the purpose of the distillery for distillates, which must be a tax warehouse.
Approximately 250 customs officers ensure the exercise of permanent tax supervision in alcohol storage.
Issue of vouchers for the collection of alcohol control stamps
The basic act for the collection of the stamps shall be to send a request to the customs office for the assignment of the registration sampling number and to issue a voucher for the collection of the check stamps for alcohol.
Alcoholic beverage, which is alcohol, means goods of Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength by volume exceeding 1,2% by volume.
The check mark is intended for labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Consumer packaging of alcohol shall be considered to be closed consumer packaging filled with alcohol intended for direct human consumption.
Consumer packaging of the Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 may be placed in free circulation in the tax territory only if it is marked with a check mark.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee and the importer of the consumer packaging, which will put it into free tax circulation, may mark consumer packaging with a check mark.
The check stamp contains, inter alia, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numeric character. The identification number shall include the registration sampling number (1-6 instead of the numerical character), the volume of alcohol (7-11 instead of the numerical character) and the volume concentration of alcohol in the consumer package (12-14 instead of the numerical character).
Original model of check mark for alcohol:
The registration number shall be assigned separately by the CA to each customer.
Only a check mark, the identification number of which corresponds to the volume of the consumer's packaging, the volume concentration of the alcohol in the consumer's packaging and the customer's control mark, may be used to indicate the consumer's packaging of alcohol.
At the end of 2014, national legislation introduced a new information system for stamps.
The aim of the new control stamp information system was to simplify and computerise the system of ordering, assessing, printing, distribution and use of labelling stamps for consumer alcohol packaging.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee, the importer of the consumer packaging and the consignee (s) of the alcohol may refer to the consumer's packaging.
The purchaser of the stamps wishing to withdraw the stamps under the "new system" must request the customs office to issue the stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the customer of the control stamps is obliged to request their issue, notify the data resulting from the national legislation of SR and keep the registration of the control stamps.
The number of control stamp items ordered shall not be less than or equal to 500 units.
The tax administrator also communicates with the customers of the stamps by means of an electronic system of stamps, in particular when notifying the number of stamps that the customer of the stamps may withdraw, or when determining the date of receipt of the stamps by the customer of the stamps at the printing works.
The customer of the control stamps is obliged to deposit on the account of the tax administrator the funds corresponding to the price of the control stamps which he may withdraw and the quantity of which shall be notified to him by the customs office.
The price of the check stamp takes into account the amount of refunds to the printer. However, it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The control stamps are entitled to print the state-owned company Mincovna Kremnice.
FŘ SR exercises tax supervision over the handling of control stamps and their liquidation in the printing works.
FŘ SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when handling control stamps.
FŘ SR ensures the sale of control stamps to the customer of control stamps in the printer.
Check stamps can only be withdrawn in the printing works from an employee of the Financial Directorate.
Issuing of vouchers for the collection of stamps for tobacco products
The customer of the check stamp must ask the CA to assign a registration sampling number and issue a voucher for the purchase of the check stamp.
Consumer packaging of cigarettes may be put into free circulation only if it is marked with a check mark.
It is only possible to mark consumer cigarette packaging with a stamp in a company that manufactures cigarettes.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee or the importer of tobacco products wishing to place tobacco products in free circulation in the tax territory may be the purchaser of the stamps.
For the labelling of consumer packages of cigarettes, only a check mark corresponding to the relevant price of cigarettes, the number of cigarettes packed, the length of cigarettes, the validity of the tax rate and the registration sampling number may be used.
Consumer cigarette packaging can only be sold for final consumption at the price indicated on the stamp.
At the end of 2014, national legislation introduced a new information system for stamps.
The new control stamp information system was aimed at simplifying and informatising the system of ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using stamps intended for labelling consumer packages of tobacco, cigars, cigaretarillos and cigarettes.
The purchaser of the stamps wishing to withdraw the stamps under the "new system" must request the customs office to issue the stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the customer of the control stamps is obliged to request their issue, notify the data resulting from the national legislation of SR and keep the registration of the control stamps.
The control stamps are entitled to print the state-owned company Mincovna Kremnice.
FŘ SR exercises tax supervision over the handling of control stamps and their liquidation in the printing works.
FŘ SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate in the printing works when handling control stamps.
FŘ SR ensures the sale of control stamps to the customer of control stamps in the printer.
Check stamps can only be withdrawn in the printing works from an employee of the Financial Directorate.
The operator of the tax warehouse or the importer of tobacco products may mark the consumer packaging of tobacco with a stamp.
The operator of the tax warehouse, the importer of tobacco products or the authorised consignee may mark the consumer packaging of cigars or cigarillos with a stamp.
The labelling of consumer packages of tobacco, cigars or cigarillos shall be used only by means of a check stamp bearing the indication for the validity of the excise duty rate.
It is only possible to mark consumer cigarette packaging with a stamp in the company that produced them.
The number of control stamp items ordered shall not be less than or equal to 500 units.
The CA shall electronically notify the customer of the control stamps within three working days at the latest of the number of control stamps which he may withdraw, the price of the control stamps and the account number of FŘ SR.
The CA may reduce the number of items of control stamps ordered if circumstances arise on the basis of which it can reasonably be assumed that there may be a breach of tax legislation.
FŘ SR will determine the date of receipt of the stamps by the customer of the stamps, but not later than 10 days.
By means of an electronic stamp system, FŘ SR shall notify the customer of the stamps.
Control marks shall be issued exclusively by the Financial Directorate in the printing works, but only after receipt of the funds corresponding to their price in the relevant account indicated in the electronic notification by the customs office.
The customer of the stamps is obliged to keep the registration of the stamps in the electronic stamp system separately for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012, the ELO and SPD systems department of the Excise Tax Department of FŘ SR is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information following a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the competent financial administration authorities.
These include in particular requests for screening of excise authorities, requests for information on excise duty management and requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of applications shall take place in electronic form within the EMCS.
The following actions are included in administrative cooperation between EU Member States: requests for administrative cooperation (request for screening, request for information on excise duty management, application for confirmation of registration in the SEED); response to the request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; an event report; inspection report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Authorisation and registration
In the Slovak Republic, tax warehouses are subject to permanent tax supervision. In the Czech Republic, this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by a monitoring device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are a tax warehouse, in SR they are only registered by the tax administrator.
The Institute of Registered Consignor is established in SR, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In the SR, 43 l may be fired at a reduced rate of excise duty on alcohol in the case of cultivation burning.
By contrast, in the Czech Republic, the reduced rate of alcohol tax can be applied only for 30 l and.
The cultivated brandy in SR must be authorised not only by the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development SR, but also by the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, only the Ministry of Agriculture authorizes the cultivation of branches.
In the SR, the import of consumer packaging of alcohol is carried out in addition to the tax warehouse operator by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol.
The authorisation of the importer shall be subject to registration of the applicant with the excise administrator.
In the Czech Republic, no special authorisation from the tax administrator is required to import consumer packaging of alcohol.
In SR, the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol is conditional on the issuing of a tax administration permit for the seller.
The retailer of consumer packaging of alcohol has a statutory obligation to keep records, inter alia, of the purchase and sale.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any authorization for the final seller of consumer packaging of alcohol; the final seller does not keep any special records.
In SR, the fuel dealer must be authorised by the tax administrator to sell them.
The national legislation in SR does not regulate any special regulation of the petrol station, all activities concerning petrol stations are regulated only in the Act on excise duty on mineral oils.
In the Czech Republic, the petrol station is regulated by a special law on fuel, but the tax administration does not issue any permit to sell fuel.
Petrol stations are registered and their list is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In SR, it is not technically possible to obtain a list of petrol stations from the financial management system.
In the SR there has been a significant increase in the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities since 2012.
This increase was due to a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits decreased significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of bail for fuel distributors.
Administrative operations
In the SR, substantive legislation provides for the exercise of tax control by selected tax entities.
This issue is specified in an internal management act issued by FŘ SR due to the application of the uniform procedure of tax administrations in the territory of SR.
In the Czech Republic, the substantive legislation does not regulate the obligation to carry out tax checks, the procedural law only provides for the possibility of carrying out checks no later than the deadline for charging the tax.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax checks carried out and local investigations carried out in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic is that the internal management act of FŘ SR determines in which cases and in what time the tax administration must carry out a tax check, whereas in the Czech Republic the correctness of the declared amount of excise duty or its refund is verified mainly by local investigations.
The number of comparable administrative operations in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 due to an increase in the number of transfers in the EMCS system and also due to an increase in the number of tax returns filed.
In the SR, the number of administrative operations between 2012 and 2015 had a slightly increasing trend, which was influenced by an increasing number of transactions in the EMCS system and a decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the number of comparable permits and the registration of tax entities showed different legislative arrangements.
The number of comparable administrative acts of the tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period.
In SR, the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds of the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for about the same amount of administrative transactions.
It can be noted from the above that SR is more focused on the implementation of administrative acts by tax administrations, e.g. the exercise of physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, the emphasis is more on remote surveillance, e.g. tracking devices, immediate sending of data via web interface and risk analysis.
Electronisation of administrative operations
Electronization of administrative operations in the Czech Republic
Tax returns can be filed through the data box.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has introduced interactive forms of tax returns, which can no longer be processed automated.
The data must also be transcribed into the personal tax account of the tax entity.
The benefit is to limit the error rate of filed tax returns (DAPs), which saves the tax administrator's actions related to the correction procedure erroneously filed by DAPs.
GŘC is working on a new application for electronic DAP processing.
In addition, through intelligent forms, it is possible to submit tax applications or business registration and notification of data changes, to apply refund claims, to comply with reporting obligations on the handling of specific mineral oils, the handling of raw tobacco and the fulfilment of biofuel obligations.
The handling of control tapes is recorded by tax entities in the information system ORO WebClient, which is available for registered entities for registration by the tax administrator of the specified data.
Transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under suspension of tax must be carried out in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality into the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
Transport of selected products in free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic can always be carried out with proof of their taxation, proof of excise duty exemption, decision of the customs office to release the selected products under customs procedure, simplified accompanying document or other decision on excise duty assessment.
The required content of the data is laid down by law.
The Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents to facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.).
It allows the documentary form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents, which are sent via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic to the data warehouse, where each such document is assigned a unique 12-digit identification code (JIK).
The JIK shall serve for the purposes of inspection by the customs authorities on the way and shall prevent repeated transport to the same document.
For the largest fuel warehouse operator in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of PHM into free tax circulation, CS CR has online access to an electronic registration system in which the entity automatically deposits the issued tax documents.
CS CR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for the registration and monitoring of selected products in free tax circulation.
This system should use 70% of the existing EMCS functional specification.
The advantage will be the user-known environment for declarants and customs officers.
It will also be connected to a system of global guarantees, a register of tax entities or a system of risk analysis.
The system should allow for an overview of transport in free circulation between Member States, which is still operating on the basis of written documents without registration and sharing of negotiating numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the current procedure for registering selected products in free circulation can be seen primarily in the abuse of a simplified accompanying document, repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronisation of administrative operations in SR
When administering excise duties, the Financial Administration of the SR uses electronic communication to monitor the movement of goods in the EMCS system under suspension of tax exemptions, control stamps, filing of tax returns and also when registering and registering tax entities.
One-way electronic communication of tax entities with the tax administrator was also introduced in 2014, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
In the framework of electronic communication, the tax entity has a personal Internet zone, the so-called electronic personal mailbox, which is intended for communication with the financial administration after entering the access data.
Within this zone, the tax entity has access to an electronic filing office through which it submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other excise tax administration documents.
However, electronic communication through the personal Internet zone does not apply to all tax entities.
National legislation defines tax entities that are obliged to communicate electronically with the tax administrator.
They are mainly taxpayers of value added tax, tax advisers representing the tax entity and lawyers representing the tax entity.
The SAO also addressed the question of the scope of electronisation of excise tax administration.
These were only fully electronic transactions, namely tax returns and electronic communications within ELO.
If one looks away from the EMCS, the electronisation of selected comparable administrative tasks has increased, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
A fully electronised processing of the tax return is already in place in the SR from its filing to the registration of the tax liability.
In the Czech Republic the electronic processing of tax returns is not set.
In the Czech Republic, it is possible for tax entities to insert compulsory documents for individual transport in free tax circulation on the website.
In the future, the announcement of transport in free tax circulation is being prepared in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system.
Evaluation
The system of reporting of transactions in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax surveillance, thus eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid in violation of legislation.
This can be recommended as a good practice.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Due to good practice in the area of electronization of tax returns, the SAO SR and the SAO of the Czech Republic recommend that the electronization of tax returns be completed in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organisational structure and staffing in excise duties
The organization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic have undergone major changes.
Organisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
The customs administration of the Czech Republic from 1. 1. 2013 consists of the Directorate-General of Customs and customs offices, which are the administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
GŘC is an entity for the entire customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out comprehensive excise tax administration since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
CS CR also performs:
a) check:
in the field of road transport (weighing of trucks, payment of road usage charges, fulfilment of the conditions for the transport of dangerous cargo, professional supervision of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and international passenger transport),
the management of waste and packaging material,
the safety of imported food;
in the field of consumer protection and intellectual property rights,
employing foreigners,
b) customs administration - it is a comprehensive application of customs legislation, trade policy measures and formalities for the import and export of goods,
c) the collection and recovery of monetary transactions imposed by other public authorities within the framework of the divided administration;
d) the activities of the police authority (mandated by the customs authorities) in proceedings concerning offences committed by violation of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax administrator.
Although the scope of competencies (concurrency of control activities) increases the total cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there are cost savings from the scale, as the public administration does not have to spend expenses on the status of control group for each subject of control separately.
At the same time, the administrative burden of re-checking is reduced.
10 From 1. 12. 2016, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic also exercises the competence to verify the performance of obligations in the registration of sales (§ 2 para. 2 of Act No. 112/2016 Coll., on the registration of sales) and from 1. 1. 2017 supervision of compliance with the Act and the conditions of the operation of gambling including the imposition of penalties (Section 116 of Act No. 186/2016 Coll., on gambling).
Within the framework of the project Modernisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-tiered structure to two-tiered one with effect from 1 January 2013, and the middle article of the procedure (customs directorates) was abolished.
GŘC spent approximately 51 million on the project. CZK (i.e. approx. € 2,031,000).
CS CR from 1. 1. 2013 consists of the GØC and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organizational units of the state.
Customs offices and their competence are provided for by law, the administration of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial departments.
Territorial workplaces are internal organisational units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is entitled to set up and abolish territorial workplaces and determine their substantive scope by decree.
The legislation does not provide for any competence for territorial workplaces; the territorial posts shall exercise the competence of the customs office on its behalf.
Organisational structure in the 31.12.2012
Organisational structure from 1.1.2013
The administration of excise duties until 31 December 2012 was carried out by the DGC, eight CDs and 58 departments of the CA (including branches), i.e. a total of 67 trade unions and departments.
As of 1 January 2016, the excise duties were administered by the DG and 51 departments at the CA and their territorial workplaces, as well as eight departments of the legal department of the DC and the departments of the CA providing mobile surveillance, i.e. about 60 posts.
The cost of the CS CR most significantly affects wage expenditure.
As a result of the reorganisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, there were no savings of personnel resources.
The performance of the main processes is ensured by customs officers in service under the Act on the Service of Members of the Security Corps.
The possibility to reduce the number of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, because according to the provisions of § 42 para. 1 of Act No. 361/2003 Coll., on the service of members of the Security Corps, can only be discharged from the service in cases which are strictly defined.
Reduction of posts as a result of organisational changes in the Security Corps is not the reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to ensure the assignment of members of the appropriate service posts within the Corps, or to secure posts with another Security Corps (e.g. Police of the Czech Republic, Prison Services of the Czech Republic), otherwise they will reassign them to the reserve for the temporarily unincorporated, in which members of the Security Corps belong according to the law 80% of the average service income.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Organization of excise tax administration in SR
The Government of the Slovak Republic has set itself as one of the priorities of completing tax administration reform through the UNITAS programme, which ensures additional budgetary resources by unifying tax collection, tariffs and levies and by suppressing tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, which resulted in the merger of the SR Tax Directorate and the SR Customs Directorate into the SR Financial Directorate and the creation of a financial administration.
FŘ SR was established for 1.1.2012 by Act No 333/2011 Z. z., on government authorities in the area of taxation, fees and customs, as amended, as a budgetary organisation which is located in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
FŘ SR, CA and Criminal Office of Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No. 199/2004 Z. z., the Customs Act and the amendment and supplementation of certain Acts, as amended, are customs authorities if they carry out duties under customs legislation.
Within the meaning of Law No 333/2011 Z. z., on government authorities in the area of taxation, fees and customs, as amended, together with the tax authorities, constitute the financial administration.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of SR, the Criminal Office of Financial Administration, the Competent Centre of Financial Operations, Tax Offices, Tax Office for Selected Tax Entities, Branches of Tax Offices, Contact Points of Tax Offices, Customs Offices, Customs Branch Branch
The main mission of FŘ SR is the effective collection and administration of taxes and duties, i.e. also excise duties, to fulfil the income part of the state budget and protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of FŘ SR is the President of the Financial Administration, appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The President of the Financial Administration is responsible for the activities of the entire financial administration and therefore for the activities of FŘ SR, which he manages and represents in full.
Organization structure of FŘ SR from 1. 1. 2012 in short form
In addition to branches of customs offices (38 branches) and stations of customs offices (18 stations), excise departments (9 departments) and legal departments (9 departments) provide activities and processes for the administration of excise duties in the territory of the SR.

IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
In 2015, 74 organizational departments with a total of 1,300 employees dealt with excise duties in the framework of the financial administration structure of SR, in addition to FŘ SR; these services are managed by almost 48,000 tax entities.
Within the organisational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, approximately 60 organizational departments with a total of 1,011 employees managed by approximately 114,000 tax entities were involved in excise tax administration in 2015.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of individual excise tax management activities is divided into several staff-independent departments.
Their mutual coordination and cooperation is addressed through middle- and top-level management.
In SR, the performance of individual activities (registration, tax returns, tax control) in the field of excise tax administration is divided between the excise department and the branch of the customs office, under which the same employees of the tax administration often deal with the agenda.
Evaluation
In SR there is approximately a third of the number of tax entities per total number of employees in excise tax administration compared to the state of the Czech Republic; the effect of more employees on the efficiency of excise duty management is not clear.
EMCS
According to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003/ES of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, establishing an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products, The aim is to establish an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products to enable real-time information on transport to be obtained and to carry out the required checks; simplify the movement of goods within the Community under suspension of excise duty.
When implementing the system, Member States should allow economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of that Decision allows the EP and the Council to include in the EMCS the national specifications, the national databases forming part of the system and the technical or programming equipment deemed necessary by the Member State to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionality of EMCS
In the Czech Republic, EMCS was preceded by the system of registration of selected products (EVV), which was operated from May 2004 to the end of March 2010.
The EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1.4.2010 and is continuously supplemented by European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
The so-called customs module and declarant module were introduced in the Czech Republic.
The customs module contains a number of national functions.
In addition to the Community system, the EMCS system in the Czech Republic monitors movements under suspension of taxes initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The system ensures the automatic dispatch of the information to the tax registry after approval of the notification of receipt of the consignment intended for the authorised consignee for one-off receipt, followed by the revocation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO, including sending responses with an attachment in any format and arranging translations.
It is also possible to receive a report on the manual cessation of exports in the ECS (only the assignment of automatically generated messages is implemented in the EU).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS shall not permit the approval of an e-AD or an acceptance notification without the response of the competent customs authority to the risk profile (risk profile cannot be ignored).
The declarant module is available for tax entities free of charge, it takes the form of a web application in which the user logs in by user name and password (coordinates), which are assigned to him after registration with the CS CR.
Any action against the EMCS customs module shall bear a valid electronic signature in the EMCS declaration module.
The Declarant Module allows tax entities to directly record data on commenced and terminated services under the suspension scheme, so that tax entities do not have to spend money on acquiring the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module allow data to be read and stored off-line (saving time for frequently used data), filling in beneficiary data on the basis of a SEED ID check and requiring mandatory completion of data that are optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows for real-time blocking of excise security of the corresponding amount of taxable supplies to every shipment sent from the Czech Republic until the end of transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by the EMCS.
Without sufficient security, the EMCS declaratory module does not allow the e-AD proposal to be sent for approval to the CA for dispatch.
Each warranty has a unique number and includes the ARC transport (including the amount of blocked collateral) for which it was used.
The tax entity can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS declaratory module, where it sees the current amount of the blocked and unlocked excise guarantee.
Expenditure on the deployment and use of the EMCS
The development of the EMCS was carried out on the basis of eight contracts with fulfilment from 2006 to 2017 totalling CZK 46,791,924,60 (i.e. € 1,761,412,56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. €1,640,401.10) excluding VAT from 2006 to the end of 2015.
During the audited period expenses totalling CZK 14,545,454 without VAT (i.e. € 547,438,99) were incurred for the EMCS system upgrade.
The amount spent on the EMCS upgrade in the audited period and converted into one transport transferred to the EMCS amounts to an average of CZK 16.49 (i.e. €0.62), excluding national funds, is CZK 24.40 (i.e. €0.92) per transport between the Czech Republic and EU Member States.
The EMCS technical support was implemented on the basis of four contracts with fulfilment from 2011 to 2017.
The total amount of technical support totalling CZK 7,499,675 (i.e. € 281,389,77) including value added tax was invoiced by the end of 2015.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 on one transport transferred to the EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (i.e. €0.23).
The invoices for development and technical support concerned the national solution and developed the EVV application, which was already operated by the GŘC before the EMCS system itself.
The invoices were covered by programme funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the delivery of services to other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under suspension.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document - SAD, which was used before the efficiency of this system, and thus ensured better control and management of the transport.
It has been introduced in the SR since 1.4.2010 and is continuously supplemented by requirements arising from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport.
ARC code under which the said traffic can be monitored online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionality of EMCS
The EMCS provides for the reception and dispatch of excise goods only by tax entities authorised to use the EMCS, thereby greatly reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The greatest development of functionalities occurred in 2011 when the EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the deployment and use of the EMCS
The introduction of the EMCS system was implemented as another module of SysNeD application equipment and therefore it is not possible to determine exactly the amount of costs of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The objective of the EMCS was to replace the system based on the administration of transport in paper form.
The EMCS benefits from a comprehensive overview of transport between Member States within the EU from the notification of the start of transport to the end of transport, while reducing administrative costs for tax administrations and tax entities for the processing, transfer and archiving of documents is important.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, national functionality was introduced into the EMCS system allowing monitoring of transport in a conditional system between two locations in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
In the Czech Republic, the automatic functionality of online monitoring and guarantee of excise duty is applied.
National functionality is also introduced, which monitors the riskiness of the taxpayer or transport, with the subsequent mandatory response of the tax administration.
The SR and the Czech Republic register a comparable number of exchanges within the EU in the EMCS system.
However, the expenditure incurred in the SR to upgrade this system was €744 310.01 higher than in the Czech Republic between 2012 and 2015.
The SAO SR obtained data from FŘ SR on the upgrade of the EMCS system only for the period from 2011, even though the system had been established and operated before.
Nevertheless, the expenses incurred to upgrade the EMCS system in SR were EUR 188,134,44 higher than the costs incurred to implement and upgrade the EMCS system in approximately ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
For the audited period, the amount of expenditure related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in SR per transport exceeds 2.3 times that of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation of the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO SR met the objectives.
Both audit institutions acquired a deeper knowledge of the excise tax management system in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in the two tax systems that affect the efficiency of excise tax administration.
Examples of good practice have been identified during parallel checks, which could contribute to the reduction of tax fraud, their importance as tax rates rise.
Procedures to reduce the cost of excise duty management have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons unless mutually coordinated due diligence is carried out with the tax administrator.
This makes the role of supreme audit institutions indispensable.
Report on the results of the parallel control of the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The 1977 Lima Declaration stresses that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financing operations.
The Declaration calls for tax revenues to be controlled to the greatest extent possible.
It considers the European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) to be one of the most important components of public tax revenue.
VI. the EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of public revenues carried out by the SAI.
An important step towards optimising the control activities of the SAI is the development of a specific strategy for auditing public revenues.
This concerns, in particular, taxes as the most subtle source of public revenue, which is most susceptible to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may, to a certain extent, be unable to carry out control activities without cooperation with another State's SAIs.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in the income of many countries.
To combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAIs carrying out checks in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation with each other.
Right on VI. the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn has developed the idea of controlling the administration of value added tax (VAT) and the VIES system in the framework of cooperation between the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
This was followed by careful preparation, where both parties first had to familiarize themselves with the legal environment and procedures for the administration of VAT in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
On the basis of an analysis of this information, a selection was made of the control topics included in the control programme.
Achieving effective and efficient VAT management is a long-term problem and individual countries (in particular the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We believe that the results of our control can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrators, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international exchange of information.
Report on the results of parallel checks on the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 - 2005 - 1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Administration of value added tax after the Czech Republic joins the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Control objective:
(CZ) The aim of the audit action in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of value added tax after the integration of the Czech Republic into the Single Internal Market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "the EU") linked to the free movement of goods and services and to verify the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the application of the right to value added tax exemption for intracommunitary supplies.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system of control of intra-Community value added tax with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the aforementioned regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
System of exchange of information on value added tax Audits were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (SAO) and the German Bundesrechnungshof (BRH) in mutual cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two audit institutions on 8 June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected business transactions between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic") and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), the use of information obtained through international cooperation between tax administrations and comparison of VAT management systems of both countries.
The joint final report on the results of the audit actions was prepared within the meaning of European Directive No 31 for the implementation of the audit standards of INTOSAI.
The controlled period was the period from 1.5.2004 to 31.12.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The parallel control in the field of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAIs.
Outside the main point - information exchanges based on Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 - control covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and summary reports, which are closely linked to the main point.
Moreover, the check included the legal situation in the area of international bus transport of passengers and the comparison of some statistical data.
A comparison of the VAT management systems of the two countries identified differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among other things) for registration is the exceedance of the limit laid down in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, only one tax identification number is allocated to payers, which they also use in intracommunity transactions.
In Germany a tax number is allocated to the payers at the time of registration for VAT, which is used only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intracommunitary transactions intend to take place, he must request the assignment of a special identification number, VAT ID.
As different marketing authorisations cause problems, conditions should be settled across the EU (see. 4.1).
2) International bus transport of persons.
In the Czech Republic, international bus transport of persons is exempt from VAT with a right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport carried out on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of the Council Directive on the common system of VAT (see. 4.2)
3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic the payers submit VAT returns only for individual tax periods (month or quarter), in Germany the payers are obliged to submit so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they have to submit an annual VAT tax return.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to submit preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to submit tax returns for VAT in the Czech Republic electronically would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see. 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic payers submit summary reports to the tax authorities, in Germany the payers submit summary reports to the Customs Office.
The tax authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have data from the summary reports immediately after their submission.
The information from the summary reports is only available to the German tax authorities after their processing into Customs.
Combating VAT fraud requires that updated information on intracommunity transactions be made available as soon as possible.
The monthly submission of summary reports would shorten the time shift between the date of the transaction and the update of the data in the VIES.
This would subsequently allow timely verification of taxation in the purchaser's Member State (see. 4.4).
This would, however, require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for the submission of a summary report.
5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech Customs Office monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for received requests for information.
The German Customs Office does not monitor the passage of time.
Consequently, the German tax administration handled a significantly lower percentage of the applications received within the time limit.
Because of these problems, BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a permanent alert (see. 4.6).
6) Risk management system.
Each Member State develops its own risk management system (RMS), which has both strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and the BRH point out that effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5th).
Within the cooperation, both SAIs examined selected cases of intracommunity transactions between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Thirty-one cases of commercial transactions where there were doubts as to their implementation or suspicion of VAT evasion were examined together with the Customs legislation.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained through international cooperation and charged the taxpayer with VAT.
In these cases, the payers either wrongly claimed the VAT exemption or did not grant the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used because of different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to reply to a request for information.
There were cases where payers erroneously reported business transactions in aggregate reports.
As a result, the data in VIES were incorrect and tax administrations had to examine these cases (see. 6.).

Summary reports.

The report on the results of parallel VAT administration checks between the Czech Republic and Germany was prepared at a workshop in July 2007.
4. Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payers who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
According to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Charges (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 337/1992 Coll."), the taxpayer, the taxpayer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person who is defined as a tax entity by law.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421 865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
At 1 December 2005 the number of tax entities registered for VAT increased to 457,590.
The taxable person who has his registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months, shall become the payer from the first day of the third month following the month in which he exceeded the registration limit (Section 94 (2)). 1 Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on value added tax; hereinafter referred to as "Act No 235/2004 Coll.").
This person is obliged to file an application within 15 days after the end of the month in which he exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow the taxable person to be registered retroactively in cases where the reason for registration is in excess of the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with a right of deduction may become a tax payer, even if the turnover does not exceed CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) if he fulfils any of the other conditions specified in Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not fulfil any of the conditions laid down by law may apply for registration for VAT on a voluntary basis.
The registration procedure under Act No. 337/1992 Coll.
The voluntary VAT payer shall also indicate the date on which he applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator shall verify the data communicated by the taxpayer, i.e. the completed registration application with all the annexes.
If it has doubts about the data, it shall invite the tax entity to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After the tax administrator has verified that the tax entity meets the conditions for registration, it shall issue a decision in the form of a certificate of registration and a tax identification number ("TIC").
The tax administrator shall indicate on the certificate the effective date of registration for VAT and the periodicity of the tax period for VAT.
The tax period is the calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year did not reach CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750).
If the payer's turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax period is the calendar month.
The payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year reached CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax period and will notify the tax administrator of this change.
IRING segmentISintent  EU blank
The allocation of the VAT in the registration certificate is always constitutive and the tax entity is obliged to indicate it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special act (e.g. Act No. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The TS contains the code "CZ" and the stem part which forms the generic identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is the birth number, or another general identifier, if so provided for by a special law, and for a legal person the identification number (provisions of § 33 para. 12 Act No. 337/1992 Coll.).
If the tax entity has not fulfilled its registration obligation even at the request of the tax administrator, the local tax administrator shall register it without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issue of a Certificate of Registration ex officio, which is served on the tax entity.
In the Czech Republic, the tax entity which has obtained a business authorisation is assigned a tax at the time of its first registration for any tax.
The same VAT is used by the tax entity even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., which is effective from 1.1. 2005, the tax administrator may, in the event of non-compliance with the VAT registration obligation, impose a refund of up to 10% on the total revenue or income for taxable transactions, which that person has wrongly effected free of tax, for the period from the date; to which she was legally to be a registered payer, until the date, to which, by decision of the tax administration, she became a registered payer (provisions of § 98 para. 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
Payment of the amount thus determined shall be regarded as payment of tax (§ 98 para. 3 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it is not a sanction.
Cancellation of registration of the VAT payer when fulfilling the statutory conditions is possible for two reasons:
1)
Cancellation of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover that does not reach the registration limit (§ 106 para. 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer shall be entitled to apply for cancellation at the earliest 1 year after the effective date indicated on the registration certificate.
2) Cancellation of registration "ex officio" (§ 106 para. 7 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), if: (a) the payer has not performed without notice the reason to the tax administrator for 12 consecutive months of performance, (b) the payer does not fulfil his obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Taxpayers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State, which has no registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person, which performs transactions with the place of supply in the country and is the person liable to declare and pay tax on such transactions pursuant to Section 108 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. (so-called "non-established payer"), becomes the payer on the date of the performance.
This person is obliged to file an application for registration with the Financial Office for Prague 1 at the latest by the date of implementation.
In the application for registration, it is obliged to indicate all the taxes allocated to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If the "non-established" payer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic, the Tax Office for Prague 1 will retroactively register it because of the Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax entity became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic.
In retroactive registration, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires proof from tax entities that the transaction has been carried out (invoices or explanatory letters).
If the "non-established" tax entity requests registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable transaction is made, then the Tax Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts for the performance to take place.
As of 31 December 2004, 473 "non-established" payers were registered at the Financial Office for Prague 1, of which 124 were from Germany, and as of 31 December 2005, 951 "non-established" payers were registered, including 233 from Germany.
According to the provisions of § 106 para. 9 Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the "non-established" payer on 31 January of the following calendar year, provided that the payer has not been obliged to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The audit of the SAO found that if a "non-established" payer lodges a tax return abroad for carriage of mail on 25 January, i.e. in accordance with the statutory regulation at the date for filing the tax return, the tax office often does not have it available on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant for the possibility of cancellation of registration to the tax office are known later than 31 January, in the Czech Republic it is not possible to cancel VAT registration in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
In view of the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (§ § 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter referred to as "AO"), anyone engaged in business activities is obliged to inform the municipal/municipal office or the relevant tax office.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the Municipal Tax Office.
If the tax office identifies an undertaking that has begun operations but has not registered, the competent tax authority may register the taxpayer under official authority - even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are tax resident and non-resident in Germany are legally obliged to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in Section 2 of the German VAT Act ("UStG").
This obligation does not depend on the turnover they realise.
There is no voluntary registration for VAT in Germany.
There are special tax authorities for entrepreneurs living permanently abroad.
For example, for those who have their registered office in the Czech Republic, the competent Financial Office is Chemnitz-Süd.
At 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Financial Office; as of 1 March 2006, a total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs had been registered.
BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register so-called semi-independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
Since the employment permits of employees from the 10 new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
These companies do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs set out in Section 2 of the UStG because they are usually dependent on a single employer to determine their working time and the manner in which they carry out their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire of the competent tax authority, in which he must provide information about the company and the activities it carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is handled either by special departments of the tax authorities or by general-interest departments responsible for assessing taxpayers.
This form is used to assess the risk of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues the tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the competent tax office, the next three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the tax office, the next five (or four) are for differentiation of payers, the last being always the control digit.
If an entrepreneur intends to participate in intracommunity trade, he needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an intracommunity supply exempt.
Customs shall assign VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and has a VAT tax number.
Customs assigns VAT ID to entrepreneurs automatically when the payer indicates intracommunity delivery in his VAT return.
The VAT ID structure is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
Registration of an entrepreneur may be cancelled: 1 at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business activities), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all marketing years) and 2 when the tax administration realises that he no longer engages in business activities.
The validity of the VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of the VAT tax number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform Customs about the abolition of the tax number so that the Customs Code can expire for VAT purposes.
According to the German VAT Act (§ 19 (1) UStG), tax residents in Germany are not obliged to pay VAT in the event that the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and the following year the latter is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000.
So-called small entrepreneurs ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice VAT to other entrepreneurs and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not obliged to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that there will be no provision of § 19 para. 1 UStG apply.
This confession is binding on him for the next five years.
The entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For tax non-residents there is the possibility to appoint tax representatives (Section 22a UStG).
The prerequisite is that they carry out exclusively exempt business operations and are not entitled to an entry tax deduction.
The function of the tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign businessman who does not have to register for VAT.
Invoices shall include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among other things) for registration is the exceedance of the limit laid down in the VAT Act.
If the tax entity in the Czech Republic does not exceed the set limit, it has the possibility to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration process is standardized in Germany, but different organisational models in the federal states may result in differences.
In the Czech Republic, the payer is assigned a tax at the time of his first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he uses the same VAT in intracommunity transactions.
In Germany, a tax number is allocated to the taxpayer when registering for VAT, which is used only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intracommunitary transactions intend to take place, he must request the assignment of a special identification number, VAT ID.
As the SAO and the BRH have established, Germany's two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, as in the Czech Republic, which assigns a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intracommunity transactions.
On the other hand, a two-tier system allows retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the competent tax authority of their business.
This retroactive registration allows the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax period, in particular an accurate estimate of VAT liability.
As different marketing authorisations cause problems, conditions should be settled across the EU.
The German Parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as the Tax Credit Card).
The Federal Taxation Office will allocate the VAT at birth of the natural person.
This VAT will be valid throughout the life of the natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the competent tax authority shall apply for an economic tax credit card to be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of the VAT ID.
Work on introducing an IT device to manage the TID has not yet been completed.
International bus transport of passengers
Legislation in the Czech Republic
According to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. with effect from 1. 5. 2004, the transport of persons between Member States and between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with a right of deduction.
This transport is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by businesses registered for tax in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
Return transport shall be regarded as a separate transport.
If "non-established" tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out other economic activities besides international bus services, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International transport of persons was exempt from VAT in the Czech Republic on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V of the Council. Article 5 (5) 1 font. b) where:
"For the purposes of Art. Article 28 (2) 3 fonts. b) Directive 77/388/EHS the Czech Republic may continue to exempt from value added tax from international passenger transport in accordance with point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Art. Article 28 (2) This Regulation shall enter into force on the twentieth day following that of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Union.
Description of the legislation in Germany
Pursuant to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/ES of 28 November 2006, implemented under Section 3b (1) of the Treaty. 1 of the German VAT Act is the place where the carriage of passengers (i.e. transport services) takes place (i.e. where the carriage takes place).
The German tax system therefore does not distinguish between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only the part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable provision of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also does not distinguish between tax residents and non-residents.
If the tax non-resident carries passengers through Germany, the part of the route which takes place in Germany also constitutes a taxable provision of transport.
The tax non-resident must notify the competent tax office of his intention to provide passenger transport before carrying out his services in Germany.
The tax office shall register this non-resident for tax (cf. 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach specified in the taxpayer's notification.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare his taxable supply of transport in the German VAT return.
On 1 March 2006, the Tax Office of Chemnitz-Süd registered 741 Czech payers who carried passengers.
If passenger transport is provided to a tax resident who is a person liable for VAT, the tax non-resident does not have to pay VAT to the tax office itself.
Instead, the entity obliged to pay VAT to the tax office and the invoiced net amount to the tax non-resident is the tax resident who is the recipient of the services; this process is known as "reverse charge" and complies with Article 196 of the 2006/112/ES Council Directive.
In addition to the notification of the tax non-resident and his VAT return, the German tax administration has several means of assessing the accuracy of the taxable provision of passengers.
The mobile control groups of the customs office carry out audits of certificates of buses licensed for foreign transport, which are used for the carriage of passengers via Germany.
After each audit, mobile control groups shall send a control report to the competent financial authority.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group shall be entitled to request VAT from the bus driver before continuing the next transport.
A non-resident may deduct the VAT thus paid on the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may notify the intention to carry out an audit to be carried out in the office of the tax office or it may use the administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if a tax non-resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT charged in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under the Council Directive.
In order to review the VAT return or the fulfilment of the obligations of a non-resident, the BRH considers all such administrative cooperation to be too labour intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for the taxable provision of passenger transport.
In particular, the audit of the accounting of the tax non-resident incurs disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration must audit foreign accounting, which means not only the need for foreign language knowledge, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
The audit of this type is also likely to require more time than the audit of a tax resident, but this audit is limited to the provision of passenger services carried out in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident may not only accept the right to carry out checks which are the responsibility of his national tax administration, but also the right to carry out audits by other Member States in which he carries passengers.
Moreover, in any Member State in which only one provision of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all tax obligations applicable to it in those Member States, in all languages and in all tax forms of those Member States.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore incurs disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in both countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, the transport of persons between individual EU Member States or between Member States and third countries is exempt from VAT on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic with a right of deduction.
In Germany, the part of the transport carried out in the German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
Where such carriage is provided by a non-established payer in Germany for the first time, he shall notify the competent tax authority in advance of the provision of the carriage.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to declare in Germany the taxable supply of part of the shipment in the tax return.
Implementation of the law is very time consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered with the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office carry passengers.
Compared to the effort, the tax return, if realised, is rather low.
Member States collecting VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT are burdened with time consuming obligations without a financially sensitive result.
In order to avoid disproportionate VAT costs, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in only one Member State.
This could be the state where the transport starts or where the provider resides.
Such taxation would require adaptation of the Council Directive.
VAT returns
Submission and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to file a VAT return on a form prescribed by the Ministry of Finance within 25 days after the end of the tax period, even if he has not been taxed unless the law provides otherwise.
The actual tax liability is payable within the time limit for filing the VAT return, except for the tax charged in connection with the import of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., for which the maturity of the tax is determined by customs regulations.
If the overcompensation results in a refundable overpayment, the payer shall return without request within 30 days of the overcompensation.
The deadline is not applied in cases where the tax administrator launches a tax procedure concerning the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of § 73 para. 11 Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the right of deduction may be claimed in an ordinary VAT return at the latest for the last tax period of the calendar year in which the right of deduction may have been claimed.
After the expiry of this period, the right to deduct may be further claimed within 3 years of the end of the tax period in which the right to deduct may have been claimed at the earliest.
However, this is only possible by filing an additional VAT return.
Amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1.1.2005, it is only possible to submit an additional VAT return for the period during which the right to deduct could be claimed for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return if (a) the totality of the corrections increases the tax liability, (b) the correction is carried out where the last known tax liability does not change, but only the data previously claimed by the taxpayer, (c) the correction of the rate and amount of the tax pursuant to Section 49 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
