The payer may submit an additional VAT return if it reduces the tax liability by aggregating the corrections.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The submission of the VAT return in electronic form can be made through the Internet or on a technical data medium.
Submission via the Internet may be made as a submission with a data message bearing a guaranteed electronic signature or as a submission with a data message not backed by a guaranteed electronic signature.
In the case of submissions with a data message not covered by a guaranteed electronic signature, submission is still required in writing, i.e. delivery of the computer report to the tax administrator (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines concerning the values of intracommunity supplies/acquisitions of goods.
Acquisition of services is recorded on special lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of initial automated control within the ADIS system.
The value of supplies of goods to other Member States to taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with the data provided in the summary reports filed by Czech payers.
The values of the acquisition of goods from other Member States from taxable persons in other Member States shall be compared with those obtained through the VIES system from the aggregate reports of payers from other EU Member States.
At the tax office, the ADIS system tests the credibility of VAT returns.
This test takes place automatically, as VAT returns cannot be measured without performing the test.
The credibility test includes the calculation of the credibility criteria and the evaluation of the risk types of VAT returns.
According to the provisions of § 37 para. 1 Act No. 337/1992 Coll. the tax office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on the person who fails to comply with the obligation of a non-monetary nature under this or special tax law or by decision under this Act.
Automated tax information system used by the FA for technical support of tax administration.
The audit of the SAO found that the tax authorities generally did not take advantage of the possibility to impose a fine on the payers for not filing a VAT return.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between the preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and the annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit provisional VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not obliged to pay VAT must file an annual tax return.
In general, taxpayers are obliged to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which the VAT is incurred (Section 18, par. 2 UStG).
However, if the VAT requirement exceeds EUR 6 136 in the previous calendar year or if it is a newly established undertaking, the relevant entrepreneur is obliged to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to submit a monthly VAT return if a refund exceeded EUR 6,136 in the last year (§ 18 para. 2a UStG).
VAT returns need not be lodged if the amount of annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT liability must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax period in which the VAT was incurred.
The refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FA.
There are no time limits (according to the law) for the processing of tax returns and the refund of excessive VAT deduction.
In order to recover the tax in good time, it is possible to offer collateral for the amount to be recovered.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and refund the tax quickly.
The German VAT law provides for the possibility of extending this period (§ 18 para. 6 UStG).
Such an extension should be requested separately.
It allows you to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT duty a month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of a monthly return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT charge.
Whenever an error is detected, the entrepreneur must file a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered with the tax office, the entrepreneur cannot correct the erroneous advance tax return, but only the annual VAT return.
Correction of the annual VAT return for the benefit or disadvantage of the payer is possible during the following 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
The payers are obliged to submit preliminary VAT returns electronically.
The tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule in order to avoid undue hardship.
Submission of an annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the Internet, either with or without certification.
If it is made without certification, the payer must submit the return once more on paper with personal signatures.
If the payer does not submit a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In case of late filing, a penalty payment may be imposed on the payer (up to a maximum of 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000).
During the previous inspection, BRH found that tax authorities often did not measure this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was calculated inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard fine therefore fails to meet its objective of reducing the average delay, especially when submitting the annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to intracommunity delivery/acquisition of goods.
Acquisition of services is recorded on special lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on the separate line of the tax return/VAT.
In the case of VAT returns which are submitted in paper form, a copy must be made either via a scanner or by staff specially authorised to do so.
Data from VAT returns submitted electronically shall be immediately available to the tax office officer.
Once all the data has been entered into the system, RMS staff will go through it and select cases that meet certain criteria.
The selected VAT returns must be reviewed by a tax office official on the basis of a control report drawn up by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration must roughly estimate the amount of VAT that the taxpayer must pay, the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers submit VAT returns within 25 days after the end of the tax period.
Depending on the amount of the payer's turnover, the tax period shall be either the calendar quarter or the calendar month.
In Germany, the payers submit advance VAT returns, depending on the previous year's tax liability, either within 10 days of the end of the calendar quarter or months.
By 31 May of the following year, payers are obliged to file an annual tax return.
The obligation to submit an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly provisional) tax returns by filing a single annual VAT return;
- if the payer corrects the admitted intracommunity transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period for which the summary report is made;
- the Federal States do not normally compare VIES data on intracommunity acquisitions of German payers before processing the annual VAT return.
In accordance with the registration (see. 4.1.3) German payers are obliged to submit an annual VAT return irrespective of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German financial authority to examine the maximum turnover limit for small entrepreneurs.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare annual VAT returns with direct tax returns and final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only on the tax returns filed.
Unlike the Czech Republic, tax payers in Germany are obliged to submit tax returns for VAT in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to submit tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
According to Section 102 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. a payer who has delivered goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State.
Data on the value of the goods supplied are always given in the Czech currency broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their VAT ID, under which they are registered in their country.
Data on the services provided shall not be entered in SH.
SH shall be filed by the payer with a monthly and quarterly tax period for each calendar quarter within 25 days of its closure to the locally competent tax office.
Correction of incorrect data is performed in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the date of detection of errors.
Erroneous data referred to in the SH shall always be replaced by those specified in the subsequent SH.
Like tax returns, SH can be filed electronically by the payer.
If the payer does not submit SH or subsequent SH and had it according to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. submit, invite the tax administrator to submit it and inform the tax administrator of the consequences in the event of non-filing of SH or SH, i.e. that the tax administrator is in accordance with Section 37 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll. entitled to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for failure to comply with non-monetary obligations.
The audit of the SAO found that the tax authorities generally did not take advantage of the possibility of imposing a fine on the payers for failing to comply with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of SH submissions, tax entities are not sufficiently motivated to fulfil their obligations because the non-submission of SH does not affect the VAT liability.
The tax administrator is obliged under Section 102 para. 5 Act No. 235/2004 Coll. to examine the data in the SH or subsequent SH, where appropriate, to remove any ambiguities and use the data to determine the tax liability.
In case of inconsistency of data in the SH and data in the relevant (payer with monthly tax period) or the relevant (payer with quarterly tax period) VAT return, the tax administration should verify the accuracy of the tax liability declared in the VAT return.
Incorrect data in SH will be removed by the tax entity by filing a subsequent SH itself, or it may be called upon to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct data on the delivery of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
- the payer fails to demonstrate the particulars given in the SH (or subsequent SH), correcting them by submitting a subsequent SH,
- the tax administrator has demonstrated that the information provided by the payer in the SH or subsequent SH is not true.
The tax administrator, by inserting a correction without filing a subsequent SH by the payer, does not replace the filing of the tax entity, only adjusts the data in the VIES database to be up-to-date, complete and accurate.
SH data shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
They may only be dispatched and received by the national financial administration for cooperation with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is Customs (in the Czech Republic performs this function of the MF, Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (Customs).
is the automatic message that Customs receives from other Member States.
Contains all incorrect VAT IDs specified in sent lines of SH.
If an incorrect VAT ID is used in one of the conveyed common lines of SH or subsequent SH, an entry is made in the table of incorrect VAT IDs.
The table contains the so-called "VAT ID Doubts Notice."
The tax administrator checks the data and records the verification result in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer shall declare VAT and indicate the value of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT return.
The selected cases of irregularities in the value of the goods acquired declared by the Czech taxpayer in his VAT return and in the value of the goods delivered, as stated by the payers from other Member States in their SH, are sent from Customs to the tax office for examination.
Tax administrators are obliged to investigate irregularities.
There may be three situations:
a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant VAT return lines is lower than the value declared by EU payers.
In this case, the tax administrator will verify the accuracy of the data.
b) The difference amount is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects its SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself submits an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administrator whether, despite this fact, it will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States indicated by the Czech taxpayer in the respective lines of the VAT return is higher than the value of the delivered goods declared by EU payers.
It is also at the discretion of the controller to verify the accuracy of the data.
After examining the difference and clarifying the causes of its occurrence, the tax administrator shall enter the result of the verification into ADIS.
The results of the screening are transmitted back to the CLO.
The number of cases sent from Customs to the tax authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005 is shown in Chart 1 (source: MF).
Chart 1 above shows that the number of cases transmitted from Customs to the tax authorities for each quarter of 2005 decreased.
A significant decrease in numbers occurred in the 4 2005 quarter. Customs has increased the minimum threshold, including with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between VAT return data and EU data may not always be due to an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error arising from the fact that certain types of transactions may be introduced into the SH in a different way in each EU Member State.
The most common reasons for irregularities in reported transaction values found at audited financial offices are set out in Table 1.
Administration and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs making intracommunity deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or participating in triangular transactions are obliged to submit SH every quarter of the year in which intracommunity supplies are indicated by beneficiaries (§ 18a para. 1 UStG).
SH must be filed by the 10th day of the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If an extension of this period is allowed in the case of provisional VAT returns, this also applies to SH.
SH must be supplied to the Customs.
They must be submitted electronically from 1 January 2007.
Exemptions may be allowed by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers realise that incorrect data are given in SH, they are obliged to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not submit an SH, Customs will initiate proceedings to enforce the submission of that report.
Part of this procedure is: - the first reminder - the second reminder associated with the threat of a fine/penalty payment and - penalty payment.
Although the German Tax Code allows a fine of up to EUR 25 000 (Section 329 AO), the Customs Code measures fines in three steps, in amounts of EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, § 26a para. UStG 1 No 5 stipulates that payers act illegally if they deliberately or negligently fail to properly submit an SH, file it incomplete, submit it in a timely manner or if they do not correct or correct it late.
This offence can be punished with a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intracommunity supplies cannot be entered into VIES by the tax office because the processing of SH is the sole task of Customs.
SH data are stored only in the CLO system.
Therefore, the SH data are visually available only after processing into customs.
The deadlines for processing SH are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
SH data shall be stored within three months following the relevant calendar quarter.
Where incorrect VAT IDs are included in the SH of German payers, Customs shall receive the O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
Customs contacts a specific entrepreneur and asks for the correct information.
If the Customs Authority fails to obtain correct information, the case shall be referred to the competent tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
During the inspection, BRH found that most entrepreneurs corrected VAT ID at the request of Customs.
However, in cases where a payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud, the challenge, threat and assessment of three additional fines take too much time.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the competent tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The tax office rejected the exemption of declared intracommunity supplies in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax office asked him to file a corrected SH against the Customs Authority because the tax authorities could not correct the data in the VIES themselves.
BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor Customs inspected the submission of the corrected SH, so the payers often failed to comply with the request.
In view of the fact that the Customs Office does not have access to VAT return data, a comparison of the data on the supply of goods declared in the VAT return and SH will not take place before the submission of these data to the Customs of the other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied in the preparation of VAT checks.
Data obtained from other Member States shall be processed into Customs.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and subsequently submitted to the Member States concerned.
This data shall be used for the purpose of checking acquisitions carried out by the tax authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, the CLO checks them on the basis of a comparison with the data from the previous calendar quarters.
If they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is generated and sent to the competent financial authorities.
This procedure is applied permanently, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created later and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the purpose of the assessment procedure subsequently checks these data with intracommunity acquisitions data.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who are not fully entitled to VAT deduction.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have delivered goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State submit an SH within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter to the locally competent tax office.
The tax authorities shall process the SH and transmit the data to the Customs Authority.
The value of the delivery of goods to another Member State, indicated by the payer in the SH, is compared at the tax offices with the value of the supply of goods to another Member State indicated by those payers in the VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the measurement procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made intracommunity deliveries are obliged to submit SH quarterly by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers are submitted to the CLO, from 1.1.2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities only have information from SH after processing it into Customs.
Payers from both the Czech Republic and Germany indicate only the supply of goods in the SH. The provision of services is not mentioned in the SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are unable to correct erroneous lines filed by SH themselves.
As a result of this limited access to German VIES data, the incorrect VAT ID has not been corrected, even though the payer provided the correct VAT ID to the FA.
The German Tax Administration does not compare the information on intracommunity supplies contained in the VAT return of the German payer and its SH.
The differences between the data of these two statements are not normally detected before the German Customs Office provides data from VIES to other Member States.
In view of the findings of the BRH, it is clear that the comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in the VIES.
Data on the delivery of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT returns.
The comparison shall be carried out by Customs separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are transmitted to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in payers' tax returns.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intracommunity acquisitions.
Such a general check is only processed for payers who are not fully entitled to VAT deduction.
Moreover, the German tax administration controls the taxation of intracommunity acquisitions of other payers only if RMS produces a control notice or if the payer is intended for inspection anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities of the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, VAT fraud detection depends on the quality of the RMS.
Combating carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intracommunity acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides financial authorities with information that may be up to six months old.
This delay may be reduced by up to four months if the payer administers SH per month.
The monthly submission would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, since most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are obliged to submit tax returns on a monthly basis - and SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, SH's submission may be linked to the filing of a VAT return.
However, the obligation to submit SH on a monthly basis would cause more time mismatches between the reporting of intracommunity supply and intracommunity acquisition and could increase the flow of data between Customs.
In 2006, the German Federal Government considered the general provisions of monthly SHs.
Its implementation failed due to the doubts of the federal states.
These feared that the monthly submission of VIES data to the Customs of other Member States could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the monthly SH and monthly data transmission obligations were to be effective, a monthly update of the VIES would require a European monthly SH standard.
Statistics on delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
In the context of foreign trade, Germany represents the most important trading partner for the Czech Republic.
The total volumes of intracommunity transactions in goods carried out between the Czech Republic and Germany are shown in Table 2.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of incorrect tax credits or VAT IDs contained in the reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to the different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL reports.
While Czech Customs refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, German Customs refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
International exchange of level 3 information
Implementation of international information exchange in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax administrations to obtain information from other Member States concerning intra-community commercial transactions and the payers who have carried out such transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, namely the exchange of information on request and the exchange of information without prior request.
International exchange of information on request takes the form of so-called information requests (hereinafter referred to as "JHA"), using standardised SCAC forms.
The tax administrators from the Czech Republic send their JORs, or responses to the received JORs through the Financial Directorate to the CLO, which ensures translation of the information provided on the standardized SCAC forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
The CLO also ensures the income of JOI from other Member States and the responses to sent to JOI, their translation into Czech and distribution to local tax administrations for processing.
In Art. 8 Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 provides for a maximum period of 3 months from receipt of an application for the processing of the JHA.
The SAO was audited by all SAO, handed over during the audited period between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Of the 94 RU admitted in the Czech Republic from Germany, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) were settled within a specified three-month period, another 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were settled after that deadline and the remaining 1 case was not sent to Germany until the SAO was checked.
More detailed information on the deadlines within which replies to the JHA received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic contains chart 2.
Of the 335 JHA shipped from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) reply received within the three-month deadline, another 179 (i.e. 53,4%) of requests were answered after this deadline and on 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) no response was received from Germany until the SAO was checked. (in the remaining 1 cases, it was not possible to determine from the data transmitted when the response from Germany was received).
More detailed information on the time limits within which the replies to the JHA sent to the Czech Republic were delivered to the Czech Republic is given in Chart 3.
The percentage of intracommunity transaction values reported in the JHA passed between the Czech Republic and Germany contains Chart 4.
As can be seen from the above chart, the value of commercial transactions examined through the JHA was most frequently in the range above EUR 60 000.
International exchange of information without prior request takes the form of either automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax administrations from other Member States are often forwarded, without prior request, information that may be relevant to them in the management of VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected on Customs.
Information is transmitted electronically between Member States.
"Automatic exchange" means, pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States without prior request and at predetermined regular intervals.
"Structured automatic exchange" means systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport by automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax administrator from the New Means of Transport Delivery Report form pursuant to Section 19 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. and a copy of the tax document issued.
The tax administrator shall complete the necessary data in a specially created template when processing the aforementioned form and forward it to the contact officer at the Financial Directorate, where the data are collected and within a specified date, i.e. no later than two months from the end of the quarter in which the information was made available, to the Customs Office for subsequent processing and transfer to other Member States.
In addition, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on consignment sales that are exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU operations that appear to be unauthorized and information on potential "missing traders."
That information is sent to other Member States by means of a spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of the international exchange of information in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and spontaneous information are initiated by the local tax authority.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form directly to the German Customs, which transmits the SCAC forms to foreign customs.
The tax authorities were instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information controlled by BRH were sent in order to ensure the taxation of intracommunity acquisitions in another Member State and, where appropriate, to demonstrate the exemption of intracommunity supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German Customs Office receives a request for information from another Member State, it shall check the value of the supply of the goods or services referred to in the application for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
In the absence of a reasonable reason for such a request, the German Customs Office shall reject any application containing an amount below that limit.
In addition, the German Customs Office shall translate free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are not in German or English.
In order to respond to a request for information, the Customs Office shall send the request to the Competent Tax Office with a reference to the three-month period.
There are no further deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of tax administration.
Although the German Customs Authority has technical conditions for monitoring past time limits, it lacks sufficient personnel capacity to alert the tax authorities to reply to outstanding requests for information.
The tax authorities shall obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two distinct types of audits: a special VAT audit covering any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which may cover only one recent commercial operation.
This short and ﬂexibilní type of audit does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has demonstrated its utility in investigating individual taxable business operations.
In the context of automatic exchange without prior request, the CFN provides other Member States with information - on VAT IDs allocated to payers resident in other Member States - on the refund of input tax to payers resident in other Member States.
Moreover, the CFN has undertaken to provide other Member States with the following information through structured automatic exchange:
a. Delivery of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without using their VAT ID, b. shipping or catalogue sales in other Member States which are not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intracommunity acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. intracommunitary supply of goods which the German payer did not declare in SH because he treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. potential "missing trader" who made intracommunitary transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who delivered goods to potential "missing traders" or those recipients who misused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The dispatch of JOI or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and in Germany by the local tax authorities that send the completed SCAC form to Customs.
While Czech Customs uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech - English) and translates the sent information into English or German, German tax authorities follow the instruction to write JOI or spontaneous information only in German on a single-language form.
German Customs does not ensure the translation of German texts.
During the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 between the Czech Republic and the CFN, the SAO found that the Czech tax administration handled 74,5% of the submitted applications within a specified period of three months.
Although the German Customs Authority draws the attention of the tax authorities to the three-month deadline, it does not monitor past time limits.
The result of missing notifications is a large number of delayed responses to JOI.
Due to these problems, the BRH recommended regular warnings to Customs.
The situation has improved.
According to the latest information, the German Customs Authority is now alerting the tax authorities to answer unfinished responses to the JHA.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, several departments at various organisational levels of tax administration deal with the management of VAT risks.
Within the MF, the following departments deal with risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
The VAT Methodology and Performance Department and the VAT Risk Management Report, which, among other things, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates trends of these risks at the domestic and community level.
Nationally, it coordinates the functioning of the role of Credibility of VAT tax returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intracommunity transactions.
Based on data from the trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risk commodities, processes conceptually VAT risk management and cooperates with relevant EU institutions and other Member States in this area.
The Department of International Cooperation in the Management of VAT, which, inter alia, ensures the exchange of VAT information, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, ensures public awareness and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of incorrect tax credits or VAT IDs contained in the reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
These differences may be due to the different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL reports.
While Czech Customs refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, German Customs refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
The Department of Tax Control and Search Methodology, which, inter alia, carries out risk analysis within the framework of methodological tax control management and sets out the priorities for the targeting of tax controls in the Financial Directorate plans, prepares risk analyses in the context of tax evasion reduction, including the collection of lessons learned from tax administration and other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
Search departments are set up in the Financial Directorates, which carry out, inter alia, searches for tax entities and areas that are risky from the point of view of the occurrence of tax fraud. (e.g. online shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), search of unregistered tax entities for risks of tax evasion (E.G. internet services, job brokering, radio and print services, etc.), analysis of chain fraud links and transmission of information to territorial financial authorities.
At the selected 12 financial offices, specialised control departments are set up.
They have regional jurisdiction, tax controls outside the territorial scope of the tax authorities are carried out on the basis of mandate.
The need to set up a specialised tax control unit has arisen on the basis of increasing findings of new and better forms of tax evasion, which occur primarily among entities linked to chains.
These departments focus on controlling tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities and multinationals and tax entities with a large range of activities in terms of turnover size.
The following mechanisms to reduce VAT risks have been integrated into ADIS: - the role of the credibility of VAT returns used to evaluate the risk of tax returns filed, - the role of the Selection of tax entities to check, allowing the collection of payers to check on the basis of selected criteria, - the role of VIES through which tax administrations have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES allows, inter alia: - to verify the validity of VAT ID of payers from other Member States, - obtain from other Member States the value of the goods delivered to the Czech payer, declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States, - generate a set of non-SH payers - carry out a formal data check, which payers from the Czech Republic have indicated in the SH, before such data is sent to other Member States, - generate a set of payers for whom the information on the supply of goods to other Member States referred to in the VAT declarations does not match the data in the SH, - generate a set of payers for whom the value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States referred to in VAT declarations does not match that declared in the SH by all its suppliers from other Member States.
Within the framework of activities to reduce the risks of tax evasion, tax administrations have access to registers of government bodies such as the Commercial Register, Land Registry, Motor Vehicle Register, Business Register, etc.
More detailed information can be found in section 4.4.1 Administration and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Given the federal (federal) structure of Germany, the federal tax administration (in particular Customs) and the tax administrations of 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of RMS.
Although there are joint working groups on development, neither Customs nor federal tax administrations share a fully consistent database.
At Customs level, ST I 2 ("KUSS" - Special VAT Audits and Tax Investigations Coordination) collects the findings of the tax fraud check in a specific database called the AACC.
KUSS, in cooperation with the tax authorities, introduced a new database called ZAUBER for the transfer of the names of tax fraudsters "missing traders."
KUSS coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
KUSS experience is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, several other CLO and MF departments are entrusted with RMS-related responsibilities and powers.
A formal check of the composition of VAT ID of other Member States in SH filed by German payers is introduced at customs level.
This formal check is carried out prior to the provision of SH data to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
The validity of VAT IDs specified in the SH is verified on the basis of the O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the procedure for correcting invalid VAT IDs, see. also 4.4.2).
In addition, the RMS on CUSTOMS is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and creates several types of control reports based on several characteristics that typically feature in so-called carousel trading operations in order to identify potential "missing traders."
The tax authorities of the Federal States are instructed to prepare these control reports and, in some cases, to report on the results of their findings to the Customs Authority.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics if the existence of a tax fraud case (instead of solely targeting the company's turnover) is to be sufficiently likely.
The BRH therefore proposed that the MF should take account of different characteristics in the preparation of the reports.
The RMS should also cover other factors, such as the taxpayer's payment behaviour (morale), branch (economic activities) or shareholder structure.
The second level of RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the Federal States and focuses on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, RMS generates a list of those payers who have reported intracommunity supplies in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the Customs to monitor the full administration of SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intracommunity acquisitions reported in the payer's annual VAT return with VIES data.
The tax administrations of the Länder seek to avoid comparing quarterly data, since such comparisons would reveal too much non-conforming data attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
- the different duration of the intracommunity transaction, in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand, and of the beneficiary on the other;
- different accounting for sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different reporting on tax returns.
In addition to comparing VAT return and VIES data, many Federal States have introduced elements of RMS based on VAT return data and certain other facts (such as the structure of the company name, the age of the shareholders, the number of employees and the taxpayer's payment behaviour/morality).
Bavaria has introduced a RMS based on rules that allow a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter referred to as risk managers) to programme their own rules for the allocation of potential perpetrators of tax fraud.
This RMS is applied when tax authorities process monthly VAT returns.
The competent tax authority therefore receives the recommendation created by the RMS before the VAT is fixed.
As this RMS is unable to reflect current findings in its activities, risk managers must adjust the relevant rules on the basis of feedback from the tax authorities.
The Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania Administrative District has programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with tax file data in which the inspection revealed tax evasion.
On the basis of these data, the RMS is able to determine the characteristics of tax evasion.
The RMS produces once a month a list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The competent tax authorities shall use this list as a basis for decisions on the audit of the proposed taxpayers.
After carrying out the audit, auditors must report their findings in order for the results of the list to be reflected in the RMS.
The North Rhine-Westphalia Administrative Area uses an adaptive artificial neural network, which is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on the large number of data assessed for VAT returns and some other facts, this neural-fuzzy system or system of collecting potentially useful information (the data-mining system) calculates the probability that a particular taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential perpetrators of fraud.
The local tax authorities shall use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers for inspection and shall notify the findings of the inspection to the data processing centre.
The implementation of one of the three RMS in the other Länder is ongoing.
Given that none of the three RMS is based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful for tackling tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although the specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and the BRH have found that each Member State has developed its own RMS.
As well as different approaches in the three federal states of Germany, the RMS of each EU country has its strengths and weaknesses.
The tax authorities of the EU Member States are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud - especially carousel fraud - is not a national but rather a European problem.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State but in more than one State.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
The loss of VAT caused by fraud in the EU may not affect the Member State of the initiator of the fraud.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
There should therefore be a European exchange and debate on RMS.
Selected control findings when verifying business transactions
The SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected business transactions, which were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
In addition, the two audit institutions jointly examined the execution of several commercial transactions for which there were doubts about their implementation or irregularities in the way the payers from both countries reported these transactions in their VAT and SH tax returns.
At the request of BRH, the SAO examined a total of 8 cases involving commercial transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
In 43 cases, the SAO examined the values of intracommunity transactions with Germany, which Czech payers reported in their tax returns and SH, on the basis of BRH warnings.
At the request of the SAO, BRH examined 23 cases involving commercial transactions between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with the Customs.
The examination of the selected cases revealed, inter alia, that different marketing authorisation methods in EU Member States lead to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to data in VIES, the Czech payer was to be acquired in III. quarter 2004 from a German payer of goods worth EUR 60 500.
As the Czech taxpayer declared the acquisition of goods only equivalent to EUR 29,869, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to examine the value of the goods delivered.
In reply to the JHA received from Germany, the German party stated that in the II. in 2004, the German payer supplied the Czech payer with goods worth EUR 27 381, in III. quarters of EUR 31,997 and IV. EUR 10 276 in the 2004 quarter.
The reply also showed that the VAT ID of the German payer was valid only from 28 September 2004, but the German Customs Office retroactively issued a VAT ID certificate of validity from 1 May 2004, following an additional application by the German payer for a VAT ID certificate.
The German payer carried out the repair of SH.
On the basis of this information, the Czech payer was involved in the acquisition of goods.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech taxpayer, following an investigation by the tax administrator, filed additional VAT returns for individual tax periods in 2004, in which he increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States while claiming the deduction of VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT returns, the Czech tax administrator could not clearly determine whether the values of supplies from the aforementioned German supplier were included.
As requested by the SAO, BRH found that the German supplier was registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, because he did not apply for VAT ID when registering, he was only assigned an identification number for transactions within the CFN.
Although in Germany it is usually not possible to assign VAT ID to the payer retroactively, in this case the German tax officer retroactively assigned VAT ID to the aforementioned German payer in 2006 at 1.5.2004.
The German Customs Office assigns VAT ID retroactively if the German businessman has not caused a delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay caused Customs after the payer's request for VAT ID.
In this case, Customs assigns VAT ID retroactively because the entrepreneur does not need his own valid VAT ID for intracommunity supply under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the contrary, the German beneficiary does not need a valid VAT ID of its supplier to report intracommunity acquisitions.
Due to these different practices between Member States, the German Customs Office has retroactively allocated VAT ID in this particular case.
2.
As part of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator requested that the German taxpayer register for VAT be examined.
The VIES indicated the date of registration of the 5.3.2005, stating on the registration certificate of the German payer issued locally by the competent German financial authority the date of the 1.10.2004.
In the reply received from Germany, the German party stated that the German taxpayer had been registered since 1.10.2004, but VAT ID had been provided to it in Germany for organisational reasons up to 16.2.2005.
By enquiry with the local tax administrator, the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator performed a VAT check on the Czech payer for tax period III. quarters 2004 to II. quarter 2005.
This audit revealed that the Czech payer included CZK 9,897 (EUR 314) in the VAT return provided to the German payer prior to his VAT registration (i.e. before 1.10.2004).
For tax period III. In the quarter of 2004, the Tax Office charged the taxpayer a VAT of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
On the basis of the SAO's request, BRH found out that the German payer had not received VAT ID until 16.2.2005 when it informed the tax office of its business, which it had started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office retrospectively registered it for VAT on 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return the payer reported intracommunity acquisitions from the Czech Republic totalling EUR 160 (approximately CZK 5,000).
3. The Czech taxpayer reported in the VAT return for September 2004 and SH for III. quarter 2004 delivery of goods worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) to the German payer.
The Czech tax administrator found, when verifying the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, that his registration was valid from 11. 11. 2004, i.e. after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer filed an additional VAT DAP, in which he reported a domestic tax base of CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) and VAT of CZK 21,777 (EUR 692).
The SAO inquired with the local tax office in the Czech Republic that the Czech taxpayer subsequently submitted an application for the renewal of the procedure in respect of the additional VAT return and provided a confirmation from the German tax administration that the German payer had been tax-led since 1.1.2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer in the international exchange of information.
The reply received from Germany indicated that the VAT ID had been allocated to the German payer only 11.11.2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the request for retrial.
BRH found that in this case it was not an intracommunity acquisition of goods because the German payer acquired VAT ID up to 11.11.2004.
However, the German beneficiary declared the acquisition as an intracommunity acquisition and declared VAT on the acquisition when it claimed the refund of the input tax in the same amount.
However, since there would be no change in the value of VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the tax administrator in Germany did not correct the data in its VAT return.
In addition, BRH found that the name of the German payer, mentioned in the JHA, had been changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in confusion between two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of goods by a Czech payer in I. the quarter 2005 EUR 22,686 from the German payer.
By enquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that this administrator had carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, verifying that the delivery of the goods had taken place and that the Czech payer had billed and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not acknowledge the acquisition of goods in the VAT return because the German supplier did not indicate his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer was registered for VAT for intracommunitary transactions from 21.4.2005, i.e. to the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the certificate of registration to the German payer so that he could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech Tax Office assessed the transaction as an acquisition of goods from a non-payer in Germany. The Czech taxpayer did not receive any additional tax from the transaction.
BRH found that, under German law, a payer supplying goods to other Member States may not have VAT ID allocated in order to exempt intracommunity supplies from VAT.
The supplier must only have at his disposal the VAT ID of the purchaser from another Member State and be able to demonstrate the transport of the goods to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act it was therefore an intracommunitary transaction and VAT should be charged in the Czech Republic.
In any case, it is important that the Czech tax administrator noticed this transaction, because the delivery of the machine at that value was not the basic business of the German supplier.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German Customs refuses to reply to Ryanair concerning intracommunity transactions worth less than EUR 15,000: 5.
Czech payer according to data from VIES in III. acquire EUR 12 561 worth of goods from the German payer in 2004 quarter.
The Czech tax administrator performed a tax check on the tax entity for this tax period.
In the context of international administrative cooperation, he requested the German tax administration to verify the delivery of these goods through the SCAC form.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of the goods, claimed that he never traded with the said German company and his accounts did not include the acquisition of these goods.
The German tax administration rejected the requirement to provide evidence - contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents - on the grounds that turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no other explanatory justification was given.
As the Czech tax administrator did not obtain the means of proof for determining the tax on acquired goods, it terminated the tax check without finding and the tax liability remained in the original amount.
As requested by the SAO, BRH found that the German payer acted as a "fiscal representative" (Section 22 a - e UStG).
The German payer reported these deliveries in his annual VAT return and in SH.
He was recognised as entitled to the exemption of supply.
Based on the BRH notice, the German Tax Office will send to the Czech Republic the supporting documents required for determining the tax on goods acquired in the Czech Republic.
As mentioned in chapter 4.6.1, the responses to the JHA sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the three-month period more often than the replies from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO examined the fact that the Czech tax administration sent a request for information to Germany on 5.10.2005 concerning the verification of the value of the goods delivered for the 4 quarter. 2004
The German payer reported in SH for this period of delivery of goods to the Czech payer worth EUR 86 307, but the Czech payer stated in the same period in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only corresponding to EUR 35 314.
In reply to the JHA, delivered to the Czech Republic on 9. 5. 2006, i.e. after the expiry of the deadline for processing, provided for in Art. 8 Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German Party stated that the application could not be processed as the German firm ceased operations at the end of 2005.
The Czech tax administration did not have the necessary documentation for the tax proceedings in the Czech Republic.
7. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator applied to the German taxpayer via the SCAC form for a review of the delivery of cars worth EUR 1,265,554 made in III. and IV. the 2004 quarter, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that no reply was received from the SRN until the time of the inspection.
The SAO also found out by enquiry with the local tax administrator that the Czech payer did not include in the VAT return the supply of new means of transport for the German payer worth CZK 11,816,103 (EUR 375,472).
The Czech tax administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity filed a subsequent SH.
On the basis of the SAO's request, BRH found that the German CCP had not, for technical reasons, forwarded the abovementioned RU to the locally competent financial authority for examination.
Following the warning of BRH, a check was carried out in Germany by a German purchaser which found that the acquisition of all cars was properly taxed and that the relevant cars were sold to another payer in Germany.
8. According to data from VIES, the Czech payer was to acquire in IV. quarter 2004 from a German passenger car payer worth EUR 48,500.
The Czech payer did not admit the acquisition of these goods.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
Tax returns were not filed by the Czech taxpayer even after the tax administration's calls. The tax office charged VAT of CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004.
On 2.6.2005, CLO drew attention to the abovementioned delivery from the German payer.
As the Czech taxpayer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, the tax administrator sent the JOI to Germany concerning the above delivery.
As the reply to the SAO was not delivered to the Czech Republic until 7 February 2007, it was not known how the Czech tax administrator used the information obtained by international exchange until the end of the audit.
The Tax Office cancelled VAT registration to the Czech payer on the date of 23.8.2005 due to non-compliance with the VAT Act.
In some cases, only a partial response was sent to the RU because the audits carried out by the tax authorities on payers were not completed at the time of the SAO and BRH control:
9.
In 2005, the Czech tax administrator applied to the German taxpayer via the SCAC form for verification of the delivery of a car worth EUR 16,991, made in III. the 2004 quarter showing signs of carousel fraud.
In reply to the JHA, the German tax administrator stated that it had only an invoice issued by the Czech payer for delivery worth EUR 16 335.
On the basis of the SAO's request, BRH found that the check carried out by the German Financial Office on the purchaser from Germany had not yet been completed.
The German purchaser declared the acquisition of goods worth EUR 16 335 twice in the tax returns for the months of August and September 2004.
10. In 2005 the Czech tax administrator requested a review of the delivery of cars to a German payer totalling EUR 198 167 made in IV. quarters 2004 and I. the 2005 quarter showing the hallmarks of carousel fraud.
The German tax administration sent a partial reply to ŽOI to the Czech Republic in which it confirmed the acquisition of certain cars by a German payer and further stated that the investigation in Germany had not been completed.

The SAO found that the Czech supplier had carried out several local inquiries in order to verify the excess VAT deductions, in which it did not identify their unauthorised drawdown.
BRH found that the German payer had declared the acquisition of goods from other Member States totalling EUR 579 114 in that period in his VAT returns and that the check carried out by the German Financial Office on the purchaser from Germany had not yet been completed.
Chapter 4.4.1 describes the reasons for the differences between the intracommunity value of the goods indicated by the recipient in the tax return and the values indicated by the supplier in his SH.
The audited cases showed that the most common reasons for the differences were not the time shift or the indication of the incorrect value of intracommunity delivery of goods in SH:
11.
Czech payer had in I. According to VIES data, the 2005 quarter was acquired from a German payer with a value of EUR 35,716, but the Czech payer did not acknowledge the acquisition.
Since the Czech taxpayer did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not operate at the company's headquarters, the Czech tax administrator asked the international information exchange to verify how the German payer communicated with the Czech payer.
According to the German tax administration, the reply received from Germany indicated that the Czech taxpayer was unknown at the notified address and that the goods were taken over by the contracted carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer only delivered goods worth EUR 21 659.
The Czech payer sent the German payer a false receipt of payment of EUR 155 153 in favour of the German payer.
After discovering the fraudulent conduct by the Czech purchaser, the German payer managed to recover the supplied material with the help of other Czech customers, except for one item worth EUR 7,916.
By enquiry with the local tax office in the Czech Republic, the SAO found out that the tax administrator provided the Czech taxpayer with VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States amounting to CZK 388,522 (EUR 13,044).

According to the German legal situation, the German payer reported the corrected value of the goods and the reduction of the taxable amount in the quarter in which the correction took place.

12.
In the context of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator requested by means of the SCAC form to verify the supply of goods and services carried out in III. quarter 2005.
According to this ŽOI, the Czech payer was to deliver to the German payer a total value of EUR 396 126 and provide services worth EUR 11 885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation to verify this delivery with the Czech payer.
In reply to the JHA, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech payer supplied the German payer with a production line including assembly.
Individual parts of the production line were delivered by the Czech payer before the Czech Republic entered the EU and after 1. 5. 2004 the line was assembled on the basis of the order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed to have defects.
In III. In 2005, the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer took the invoices but did not recognise them and did not pay.
The SAO also found that all invoices are properly registered in the Czech payer's accounts by enquiry with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
In VAT returns for III. The 2005 quarter shows only the amounts documented by the Czech payer which relate to post- 1.5.2004 invoicing.
BRH found that on the basis of a reply from the Czech tax administration, the local tax authority in Germany concluded that the transaction concerned the delivery of goods from the Czech payer to the German payer, including assembly services.
In this particular case, the place of work is where the production line was installed.
According to the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the supplied service is obliged to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient may claim a VAT deduction from the same amount.
As there would be no change in the value of VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax office.
13. According to data from VIES, Czech payer A had acquired a machine worth EUR 58 000 from the German payer C in February 2005.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to examine this delivery.
In reply to the JHA, the German party stated that already in 2004 the German payer C supplied the Czech payer B, which was to return the machine to the German payer C in October 2004.
According to the information of the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but transported to the organizational branch of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Further, the reply to the request for information showed that the German payer C sold the machine to Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organizational arm of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
As the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intracommunitary delivery of goods.
By enquiry with the tax administrator of the local payer B, the SAO found that according to VIES data, the German payer C delivered in III. quarter 2004 to Czech payer B goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027.
Payer B denied the acquisition of the goods. The local Czech tax administrator sent the Company to Germany.
According to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
A further investigation by Payer B revealed that the Czech tax administrator did not find a machine worth EUR 88 027 in Payer B's accounting and that it could be a machine of the same type as was supplied by the organizational component of the German Payer C to Czech Payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax administrator of the local payer A carried out a local investigation with this payer.
The tax administrator had at its disposal the invoice of the German payer C of 7.2.2005, on which payer A was listed as the customer of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that payer A does not have this invoice included in the accounts.
Payer A had a leasing contract with another Czech company, where the subject of leasing was a machine of the same type.
The transfer of the machine from the leasing company took place 9.2.2005, the transport of the machine was provided by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech Tax Office to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found that the German payer C did not deliver a machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intracommunitary supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax administrator did not grant exemption from VAT to the German taxpayer C and corrected the data in its tax return.
German payer D supplied the machine to Czech payer B.
According to German law, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, BRH found that the German payer C indicated in its SH for I. quarter 2005 delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000 to Czech payer A.
This supply was not examined during the tax check carried out by the German Financial Office.
The following diagram shows the relationships between participants in the above commercial transactions.
14.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administration received a request for information from the German tax administrator requesting verification of intracommunity supplies from the German payer worth EUR 879 680 625 to the Czech taxpayer.
According to the German tax administrator, there was a suspicion that this was a pretentious intracommunity supply of goods.
It was further stated in the JHA that the German payer had not undertaken any active business since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer.
According to the Czech Company Executive, the above case appeared to be a German payer's claim against the German tax administration, which was applied by the Czech payer as a partner of a German company with the German Tax Office.
According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administrator does not currently have any information that the German tax administration would address the issue related to the Czech taxpayer.
According to the available information it was not the delivery of goods, yet the stated value is still included in the VIES system as an intracommunitary delivery of goods to the Czech payer from Germany.
The main reason for the following irregularities was that the beneficiaries did not show intracommunity acquisitions of goods in their tax returns (see also section 4.4.1):
15. According to VIES data, the German payer supplied in III. quarters 2004 to I. quarter 2005 to the Czech payer of goods totalling EUR 33 205. The Czech payer did not admit this acquisition.

As part of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator requested verification of the delivery of goods from Germany.
In response to this request, the German tax administration stated that the German payer sent part of the goods to the Czech payer's address, the remaining goods were collected personally by the Czech payer.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech taxpayer filed additional VAT returns for these periods before receiving a reply to the JHA.
Despite this submission, differences in acquisition values were not resolved, so the Czech tax administrator recommended that a tax check be carried out on the Czech payer.
The check has not yet been carried out.

For the same period, the Czech payer granted intracommunity acquisitions only equivalent to EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator requested verification as part of the international exchange of information on the value of deliveries.

An additional VAT return has not yet been filed.
The Czech tax administrator told the SAO that it would continue to proceed in such a way as to comply with the deadlines for any additional VAT assessment for the relevant tax period.
17.
German payer had in IV. supply the Czech payer with goods worth EUR 11,600 in 2004.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator requested confirmation of whether the Czech payer actually existed because the alleged partner of the German payer had set up more fictitious companies in Germany.
The Czech payer confirmed the acquisition of goods to the Tax Office.
According to the Czech payer, however, the goods were not transported from Germany to the Czech Republic and were further sold during 2005 in Germany.
The Czech payer submitted documents on the sale of goods for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany, he did not grant or pay tax on the sale of the goods in the Czech Republic or in Germany.
All these facts indicated tax evasion in the territory of Germany and the Czech tax administrator communicated them to the German tax administration in reply to the JHA.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech taxpayer submitted an additional VAT return for IV based on the investigations carried out. the 2004 quarter, in which he included the value of the acquisition of goods, inter alia, from the German payer, while claiming the right of deduction for the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
VAT on the sale of goods in Germany did not appear in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return after the local investigation without change.
According to the Czech legislation, in this case it was not the acquisition of goods from other Member States because the goods were not dispatched or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator therefore carried out an incorrect conclusion of the local investigation.
BRH found that the German tax administrator corrected the tax return of the German taxpayer immediately after accepting the reply to the JHA stating that the goods had not left Germany and claimed VAT of EUR 1 600.
In addition, the competent tax authority has sent a notice to the tax office of the actual consignee to ensure that the resale of these goods is correctly taxed.

18.
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech taxpayer acquired a passenger car worth EUR 47,400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
The application was accompanied by a copy of the certificate of registration of the Czech taxpayer for VAT.
A copy of the passport of the person who was said to have carried out the transport of that car was also included.
An investigation by the Czech tax administrator found that the passport was stolen, the person in it did not bring any vehicle to the Czech Republic and denied any contacts with the German tax entity.
The Czech tax administrator never issued a VAT registration certificate, a copy of which was sent by the German party.
This information was provided by the Czech tax administrator in reply to the JOI together with the information that it could not confirm the acquisition of the goods - the car in question.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer did not reside at the address listed in the Commercial Register and the company executive was non-contact.
The Czech tax administrator charged the Czech taxpayer a tax liability of CZK 0 for the February 2005 tax period.
Further investigation, the Czech tax administrator found that the car in question was sold to another Czech entity, which bought it through an advertisement on the Internet.
BRH found that the local German tax administrator, on the basis of the Czech reply to the JHA, would not recognise the German payer as entitled to exemption from VAT.
19. During the inspection, the German tax office was unable to clarify the difference of EUR 3000 between the value of the goods acquired declared in the payer's tax return and the value provided from another Member State.
It was said that the Czech payer should deliver during IV. quarters 2004 to I. the 2005 quarter to the German payer of goods worth EUR 89 424.
Since the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the data in VIES, the German tax administrator requested verification of the supplies and their reimbursement in the context of the international exchange of information.
The Czech tax administrator stated in reply to ŽOI that the only executive of the Czech company was removed from the Commercial Register on 8. 7. 2005 and the new executive was not registered.
The German recipient of the goods appears to have been related to a partner of the Czech company.
The Czech payer filed both VAT and SH tax returns, which were signed by an unauthorized person - the company's partner - after the executive was deleted from the Commercial Register.
The accountant of the Czech taxpayer confirmed to the tax administrator that the partner of the company paid the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR was deposited into the company's account.
Cash receipts were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic discovered by inquiry with the local tax office that the tax administrator recognised the Czech taxpayer as IV. the quarter 2004 entitled to VAT exemption on delivery of goods to another Member State worth CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) and for I. quarter 2005 of CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47,548).
BRH found that the tax administrator in Germany did not correct the tax return of the German purchaser because the German judge confirmed the insolvency of the German payer.
Since the earlier check did not reveal any signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to recover the tax liability.
20. According to data in VIES, a German payer acquired EUR 4,251,196 of goods from the Czech Republic in 2005 after acquiring EUR 43,274 in the previous year.
Neither in the 2004 tax return nor in the 2005 tax return did the German payer declare intracommunity acquisitions.
Moreover, it did not declare adequate deliveries.
As a result of these differences, the German tax office dispatched the JORs concerning the fourth quarter of 2005 and the first quarter of 2006.
For these two quarters, the Czech supplier reported intracommunity deliveries to the German payer totalling CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5,615,299).
On 6.9.2006, the Company received a request from the German Party to verify whether the Czech payer had received the declared intracommunity supplies.
In reply to this JOI, the Czech tax administration stated that the German party's request could not be met because the Czech payer had no executive.
According to materials provided by the SAO to the competent tax administrator, on 30 March 2006 a protocol was drawn up with the Czech payer's manager to initiate VAT control for IV. quarter 2004 and January to December 2005.
The taxpayer was also invited by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above mentioned periods, but did not submit any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the sole executive of the Czech payer was terminated as of 16.5.2006. The new executive was not appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech taxpayer has stopped filing VAT returns.
As part of the audit of the SAO in cooperation with the BRH, he also examined several cases of intracommunity supplies between the Czech Republic and Germany, which were not the subject of prior exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the cases examined was transmitted by the two supreme audit institutions through the Customs of both countries.
21. The Czech company (eCR), which is not a resident in Germany, has informed the competent tax authority (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to make a taxable transaction in Germany.
