As a result of this information, the company has been registered since June 2005 but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) has accepted an order from a Danish businessman (eDK) for the production of several wind farms and for the supply of these wind farms by name, on the risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to lack of own capacities, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relationship and mode of transport of wind farms:
According to the German legal situation, the location of these transactions must be determined according to the following:
- A Danish businessman (eDK) sent wind farms for assembly under his name, to his own risk and his account in Austria.
Since the assembly of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
- Since the carrier was instructed by a Danish businessman (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his risk and on his own account, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport started - in Germany.
Although wind farms were dispatched to another Member State and the payee is a registered payer from another Member State, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) could not obtain an exemption because another Member State of destination is different from another Member State of the registered office of the Czech company.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted the input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of transport.
Transport of some wind farms started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
- The supply of wind power plants that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
- The supply of other wind farms which are produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intracommunity delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intracommunity delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not declare any intracommunity acquisition or submit SH to German Customs in its tax return in Germany.
Thus, it is possible that the Czech company reported all intracommunitary deliveries uniformly as intracommunitary deliveries from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that (eCR) did not declare any intracommunity supply to Austria, but intracommunity delivery to Denmark.
A review of the taxation of intracommunity acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), even though this case shows no indication of tax fraud or evasion.
Furthermore, the SAO and the BRH examined the transactions in order to highlight the differences between tax returns and VIES data caused by different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that changes in legislation need time for the application of new legislation by both payers and tax authorities:
22. SH for II. up to IV. In 2004 quarter, the Czech payer reported intracommunitary delivery to the German payer totalling CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25,197,885).
During the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported intracommunity delivery to another German payer totalling CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970).
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers reported the abovementioned deliveries in SH in accordance with Act No. 235/2004 Coll., valid in 2004.
Further examination of the above-mentioned transactions, the SAO auditing group found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the legal arrangements for the supply and acquisition of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers reported electricity supply in accordance with Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as an intracommunitary supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legislation in force in 2004 it was not an intracommunitary acquisition, but a taxable transaction with the place of execution in the territory of Germany.
The difference in statutory regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., amending certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1. 1. 2005.
23. During the examination of selected intracommunity transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was also found that the Czech payer reported intracommunity deliveries to the German payer totalling CZK 240 411 163 in SH for Q1-4 2005. (EUR 8,071,823) and another Czech payer reported intracommunity delivery to the German payer totalling CZK 263,470,776 (EUR 8,846,050) in SH over the same period.
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1.1.2005 in the case of electricity supply, the place of supply is the place where the purchaser has his registered office, place of business or has an establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have reported the supply of electricity to SH in 2005.
As both payers reported intracommunitary electricity supply in SH, the VIES data was distorted by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
Cooperation met the objectives of BRH and SAO.
Both SAIs acquired a deeper knowledge of VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed differences between the two systems and showed that VAT governance legislation differs.
Suspicious cases of intracommunity transactions were detected during parallel checks.
It makes sense to examine some of them afterwards.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs produced recommendations on the administration of VAT.
Monitoring of these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
New experience and knowledge gained through cooperation between the two audit institutions is the basis for the successful implementation of subsequent VAT administration checks.
Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, the Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise control between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The submitted joint report informs on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel inspections carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Czech Audit Office of the Republic aimed at the administration of excise duties in the period following the entry of both countries into the European Union.
The cooperation was carried out on the basis of a contract for cooperation in control activities concluded in February 2006.
The theme of parallel controls was selected in view of the fundamental change in the system of excise duty collection which took place in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union from 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow the circulation of non-taxed goods until the date of delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows for the movement of goods under tax supervision under suspension.
The system places great demands on tax administrations and envisages close synergies between Member States' competent administrations in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise controls for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Control number: (Czech Republic) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject: (Czech Republic) Administration of Excise Duties (SR) Procedure of Columns
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (SAO-CR) and the Czech Audit Office of the Republic (SAO SR) concluded the "Surveillance Cooperation Agreement" on 8 February 2006.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel inspections of the "Excise Tax Administration," included in the SAO-Czech Audit Plan for 2005 under No. 05/34, and "Control of the Columns Procedure for Collective Taxes," included in the SAO SR Control Plan for 2006 under No. 48/11.
Parallel checks were coordinated.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information that could not be obtained by the Contracting Parties when controlling the administration of excise duties in the territory of their State and of producing a joint final report on the outcome of the checks within the meaning of the European Implementing Directives for the implementation of the INTOSAI audit standards - Directive No 31.
In the Czech Republic, the control (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic") was carried out by groups controlling from the state budget department and from the territorial unions of central Bohemia, southern Bohemia, western Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia between 7 February and 2 June 2006.
27 controllers were involved in the inspection.
The audited persons were the Directorate-General of Customs (hereinafter referred to as the "GRC") and 11 financial offices.
Within the GŘC 12 selected customs offices were checked out of a total of 54.
The inspection in the Slovak Republic (hereinafter "SR") was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with exposures of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 in the period from 13 February to 2 June 2006.
8 controllers were involved in the inspection.
The aim of the parallel checks was to examine customs procedures for the administration of excise duties and compliance with relevant legislation in both countries and in the European Union.
International cooperation was focused on the practice of tax administrators in supervising the transport of excise goods, in particular on the registration of initiated and terminated transactions under suspension of tax, and on the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between excise administrators of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
2. Administration of excise duties
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by the financial authorities until 31 December 2003.
As of 1 January 2004, this agenda had been taken over by the customs authorities, which had so far only levied excise duty on imports.
Mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty in the Czech Republic.
The income of the state budget from excise duties in the Czech Republic totalled CZK 82.8 billion in 2004 and excise taxes accounted for 19.5% of the state budget revenue from taxes and charges amounting to CZK 424.7 billion.
In 2005, the income of the state budget from excise duties amounted to CZK 103.6 billion and the share of the state budget revenue from taxes and charges amounting to CZK 460.4 billion was 22.5%.
In 2004, the income from excise duty on mineral oils to the State budget amounted to 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it amounted to 90.9%.
The difference to 100% of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the income of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in the SR shall be carried out by the customs authorities from 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise duty on mineral oil, the administration of which they have been administering since 1 January 2002.
In the meantime, tax authorities administered excise duties.
Excise duty in SR is subject to mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
The state budget revenue from excise duties in Slovakia totalled SK 43.4 billion in 2004 and excise taxes accounted for 209.5 billion in total tax revenues.
In 2005, the revenue of the state budget from excise duties was Sk 50 billion and the total tax revenue of Sk 222,6 billion was Sk 22,5%.
Chart 1 - Comparison of Czech state budget revenues from taxes and taxes and tax revenues of SR state budget with excise revenue
The legislation in both countries relies on European Union rules governing this area, in particular: - Council Directive 92/12/EHS on the general arrangements, possession, movement and monitoring of excise products ("Directive 92/12/EEC"), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 2073/2004"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the transport of excise products under suspension of excise duty ("Regulation No 2719/92"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 3649/92 on a simplified accompanying document for the movement within the Community of excise products released for domestic consumption in the Member State of dispatch ("Regulation No 3649/92").
The basic legislation regulating excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No. 353/2003 Coll., on excise taxes, as amended, (hereinafter "Act No. 353/2003 Coll.") effective from 1 January 2004.
In the administration of excise duties in SR, the customs authorities are, inter alia, bound by the following generally binding legislation: - Act No 98/2004 Z. z. on the minimum tax applicable to mineraloleja as last amended (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 98/2004 of the European Parliament and of the Council"). z. "), - Law No 104/2004 Z. z. on the maximum tax on wine as last amended (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 104/2004 Z. z. "), - Law No 105/2004 Z. z. on the definitive tax on lieh as amended (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 105/2004 Z. z. "), - Law No 106/2004 Z. z. on the abovementioned tobacco tax as amended (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 106/2004 Z. z. "), - Act No 107/2004 Z. z. on the first-rate tax on beer as last amended (hereinafter referred to as "Law No 107/2004 Z. z. ").
2.1 Movement of excise goods under suspension between Member States of the European Union
The conditions for the movement of excise goods under suspension are governed by Directive 92/12/EHS in Title III - Movement of goods Art. 15 to 20.
According to those provisions, transport of such goods may be carried out only by an authorised warehousekeeper, which means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to produce, process, store, receive and dispatch excise products.
The beneficiary in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or economic operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper, but who may not store or dispatch such products under suspension.
The authorised warehousekeeper is a tax warehouse operator in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic; the economic operator is an authorised beneficiary for repeated or one-off receipt of excise products.
Under the Directive, the movement of excise products under suspension is only possible with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be drawn up by the consignor in four copies before the start of transport unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch require further copies.
2.2 Procedure for the initiation and termination of transport of goods under suspension between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for the start of transport is governed by Section 25 (1). 3 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll., including:
"The tax warehouse operator shall inform the local customs office responsible for the tax warehouse from which the transport is to commence prior to the start of transport of the selected products;
transport of the selected products may only commence with the agreement of this customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the transport of the selected products without delay after the condition for securing the tax is fulfilled... "
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start the transport of all types of excise products only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of transport only if security is provided for the amount of the tax attributable to the products transported.
The consignor is obliged to draw up the accompanying document in five copies before the start of transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document the consent to the start of transport.
Copy 1 shall be retained by the consignor, copy 2, 3, and 4 by the consignor to the carrier and copy 5 shall be retained by the office authorising the transport.
According to Slovak legislation, the beneficiary in the SR retains copy No 2 of the accompanying document. Copies No 3 and 4 shall confirm the receipt of the products and shall submit both copies to the competent customs office locally.
Copy No 3 certified by the customs office shall be sent to the consignor not later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which it accepted the products.
Copy 4 shall be retained by the consignee's customs office.
Transport is terminated by receipt of products by the recipient.
The customs office in the Czech Republic which authorised the start of the transport will decide on the release of the security within 5 working days after the presentation of copy No. 3 of the accompanying document, which is confirmed by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.
Chart No. 2 - Movement document for transport started in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic
Transport from SR
Until 31 December 2005, the procedure for the transport of alcohol and tobacco products from the SR to another Member State of the European Union was adapted as follows:
According to the provisions of section 26 para. 4 of Law No 105/2004 Z. z.
"From the tax warehouse to the tax warehouse to the beneficiary of the tax warehouse, the sender" (the supplier ") shall be obliged to send an electronic fax machine to the competent authority in order to send a copy of the relevant document electronically to Colní split Poprad; it is compulsory to send to the columnist within three days from the date of the commencement. "
According to the provisions of Section 22 para. 4 of Law No 106/2004 Z. z.
"In the case of tobacco products from the tax warehouse to the tax warehouse to the beneficiary, in another case the sender" (supplier ") shall be obliged to send electronically the faxom to the Czech Republic. it shall be obligatory to send to the customs authority within three days from the date of the commencement. "
In the case of the transport of other excise products (mineral oil, wine and beer) between 1 May 2004 and 31 December 2005 ("the audited period"), the tax entity was not obliged to notify the Poprad Customs Office or the competent Customs Office of the start of transport under suspension.
The tax administrator did not learn about the transport of these products until a local investigation or a tax check on the accompanying documents and accounting documents of the tax entity.
The sender in the SR is obliged to draw up the accompanying document in four copies before the start of transport.
Copy No 1 shall be retained by the consignor (in the case of transport of alcohol and tobacco products, send a copy of copy No 1 electronically or by fax to Poprad Customs and the competent customs office).
Copy No 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods transported.
According to the Czech legislation, the recipient in the Czech Republic retains copy No. 2 of the accompanying document issued by the sender in SR and confirms the acceptance of the products in copies No. 3 and 4.
Certified copies No. 3 and 4 shall be sent to the local customs office in the Czech Republic no later than the first working day after the end of transport.
The customs office shall retain copy No 4 and copy No 3 on which it shall verify the accuracy and validity of the copy returned to the consignee.
The consignee shall send certified copy No 3 no later than the following working day after receipt to the sender in the SR.
Transport in SR shall be deemed to have ended on the date of receipt of the products by the consignee.
The sender proves the end of the transport by submitting copy No. 3 of the accompanying document certified by the recipient and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Chart 3 - Transport movement document (alcohol and tobacco products) started in SR and terminated in the Czech Republic
In 2006, the Slovak Republic gradually adopted amendments to all laws on excise duties according to which the consignor of goods under suspension of tax is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the local consignor before the start of transport.
The document proving the termination of transport of alcohol and tobacco products shall be copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the recipient and his competent tax administrator.
Document proving the termination of transport of mineral oils, wine and beer is copy No 3 confirmed by the consignee.
Confirmation by the tax administrator of the other Member State of receipt by the consignee of those goods shall be required if the latter is obliged under the legislation of the Member State concerned to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Records of initiated and terminated debts held by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
A single electronic system is not set up to monitor the transport of goods under suspension between Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/ES of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 establishing an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products requires the Member States and the European Commission to establish an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) from 1 July 2009 to enable excise administrators in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents which are currently used only in paper form and will contribute to simplifying the movement of goods under suspension and to ensuring a more efficient control of the movement of untaxed products across all Member States.
Member States' national databases will be part of this system.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transport commenced and terminated in the territory of the Czech Republic in the module Register of selected products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have online access to the system.
In the case of transfers carried out only in the territory of the Czech Republic, tax administrations may obtain information about the start or termination of transport immediately after registration of the accompanying document by the customs office into the EVV.
The customs office shall release the VAT on the transported products provided by the consignor at the time of registration by the customs office of the relevant recipient.
Customs offices in the SR use a database based on SysNed application software, which ensures automation of their activities in the administration of excise duties and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised recipient in SysNed application software, this information is automatically transferred to the "System for Exchange of Excise Data" (SEED) database.
3. Preparation and conduct of cooperation
The first coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO-Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO SR, which discussed the concrete process of cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties, took place in January 2006.
The two parties became acquainted with the excise legislation and the organisation of excise tax administration in both countries.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in authorizing, or starting and ending the transport of excise products under suspension and exchange of information between excise administrators of both countries.
At the meeting it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak parties: - compile overall data on the quantity of excise products transported from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic and vice versa, the transport of which started during the audited period, - compare data on mineral oil transport - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and alcohol - code of the Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 under the suspension procedure initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in SR and vice versa in November 2004 and September 2005.
During the checks, the screened periods were extended to include the months October and November 2005 and, during those months, the transport of tobacco products under suspension was subject to inspection.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of excise products transported under suspension between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the audited period.
4. Comparison of records of goods under suspension
The SAO-CR transmitted to the Slovak side a database of debits completed in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5,876 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 5,738 were mineral oils, 134 items of alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
The SAO SR forwarded to the Czech side a database of transfers completed in SR which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 696 items concerned mineral oil, 2,066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The SAO-CR compared the data on transport listed in the records initiated in the Czech Republic with data on terminated transport registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are shown in Table 3.
The SAO-CR compared transport data in November 2004 and September 2005 with a database of the Slovak customs administration, which the SAO SR transmitted to it at the beginning of the inspection.
The database did not contain data enabling reliable reconciliation of individual transport, and therefore only 63% of initiated operations were allocated.
Each transport was assigned according to multiple data, e.g. sender, consignee, date of transport, quantity of shipped products.
In October and November 2005, the SAO-CR compared the transport services started in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which included all data according to the accompanying documents on the basis of which 93% of the initiated transactions were unequivocally allocated.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the amount of mineral oils were given in litres or tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
The quantity of alcohol was in most cases indicated in litres but could be converted into litres of absolute alcohol on the basis of the database of that percentage of alcohol.
The quantity of tobacco products was indicated in pieces, in thousands and kilograms by type of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, where the termination could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or where the number of products transported did not match, the accompanying documents were checked.
Documents accompanying 487 transports of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were inspected.
The examination of these documents was carried out at the customs offices at which the SAO-Czech Republic carried out the inspection.
For the cases authorised by the other customs authorities, the accompanying documents were requested by the DG.
The Czech party asked the Slovak party to verify the implementation of 141 transfers, to which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic did not provide confirmed copies No. 3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products listed on the accompanying document did not agree with the quantity of products listed in the database.
In addition, data on transport registered in the Slovak database were transmitted to the Slovak party, which was not contained in the Czech Customs database.
The SAO SR searched 95 million in the database of the Slovak Customs Administration.
He requested that the remaining 46 months be verified by the local competent customs authorities, which demonstrated their termination by copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak party forwarded to the Czech side copies of accompanying documents on the basis of which transport was identified in the Czech database, except for those carried out by two Czech tax entities which were not found in the Czech database.
The following cases were examined:
- 11 spirits were registered in the Slovak database in a total quantity of 276,7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax body in 2004 and 20 million spirits in a total quantity of 404,66 litres of alcohol implemented in 2005.
The SAO-CR found that these were transports of taxed products, for which the sender does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The sender informed the tax administrator in writing about the start of transport. Transport was carried out on the basis of accompanying documents for the transport of products under suspension;
- a total of 94 million mineral oils were registered in the Slovak database, combined nomenclature code 2710 11 21, totalling 173 000 litres realised by the Czech taxpayer between September 2004 and December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that between May 2004 and June 2005 the tax entity carried out the transport of 102 thousand litres of untaxed mineral oils without proper authorisation.
The tax entity held a special authorisation to receive and use exempt products on the basis of which it could supply non-taxable products only to the holder of the same authorisation.
He did not notify the customs office in the Czech Republic of the initiation of the procedure and did not provide a tax security of CZK 1,207,680 for the transported products.
In the period July 2005 to December 2005, the tax entity transported 71 thousand litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of SR. Even in these cases, it failed to comply with the legal obligation by not notifying the customs office of initiation of the procedure.
The consignor in the Czech Republic may initiate the transport of products for free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State without the consent of the customs office, but is obliged to inform the customs office in writing prior to the start of transport.
A tax entity taking products into free circulation in another Member State is obliged to report the quantities and ensure the tax before withdrawing them.
Products may only be transported with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are governed by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also permits the use of an accompanying document for transport under suspension, but it must be clearly indicated that it is a "simplified accompanying document for the purposes of tax control (excise products)."
The same legislation on transport and admission to free circulation of products in another Member State applies in the SR.
In these cases, the tax entities transported the products put into free circulation with an accompanying document for transport under the suspension scheme, the 3rd and 4th of which the recipient submitted to the tax administration in SR for verification.
The customs authorities in the SR registered these transport operations in the database under the suspension procedure, since the accompanying documents did not indicate that they were a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the database of the Czech customs administration with the database of the Slovak customs administration and found:
- in the databases, the quantities of products transported were presented inconsistently, e.g. mineral oil in litres, hectolitres or kilograms; the alcohol is presented in litres or litres of alcohol making it more difficult to compare the quantities of goods transported,
- the quantity of spirit transported in the invoices did not match the quantity recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices were included in the databases,
- in the database of the Slovak customs administration, two transport of alcohol from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic was registered in November 2004 in a total volume of 47,237 litres of alcohol, which were not found in the database of the Czech customs administration.
The Slovak side submitted copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Until 30 June 2005, the conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the management of excise duties were regulated by Council Directive 77/799/EHS on mutual assistance between the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxes, certain excise duties and insurance premiums.
Regulation No 2073/2004, laying down rules and procedures allowing the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties, entered into force on 1 July 2005.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office to ensure contacts with other Member States in the field of excise duty management and shall be responsible for exchanging information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the report "Excise Liaison Office" (hereinafter referred to as "ELO CR") was set up at the GŘC to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise taxes between Member States of the European Union.
With effect from 1 May 2004, the ELO Office at Poprad carried out security tasks related to the management of systems for controlling the movement of excise goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the SR.
With effect from 1 July 2005, ELO's tasks shall be carried out by the Department of ELO (headquartered in Poprada) of the Department of Excise Duties of the Customs Directorate of SR (hereinafter referred to as "ELO SR").
In accordance with the provisions of Article 3 (1) of the Treaty. 3 Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office shall be responsible, in particular, for - the exchange of data kept in the SEED electronic register, - the Early Warning System Excise (EWSE), - requests for verification of movements of excise goods dispatched to other Member States or received from them by the Movement Verification System (
The content, scope and functionality of the SEED, EWSE and MVS systems are modified in Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - a system for the exchange of information on tax entities trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national excise tax registers and allows tax administrations in the territory of the European Union to determine whether excise products are traded by a person entitled to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States only for excise purposes.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information stored in that database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Law No 98/2004 Z. z., with Section 39 of Act No. 104/2004 Z. z., with Section 46 of Act No. 105/2004 Z. z., with Section 40 of Act No. 106/2004 Z. z. and with Section 39 of Act No 107/2004 Z. z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, authorised beneficiaries and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in SR contribute to the SEED database by registering a tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised recipient in SysNed application software, which is automatically connected to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, authorised beneficiary or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the associated data are automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Slovak Customs Administration and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic was usually carried out once a month, exceptionally more than once a month during the audited period.
SR Customs received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
The data are transferred to the SEED database in the Czech Republic from the national register, in which all persons entitled to dispose of excise products and issued authorisations to dispose of such products are registered.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Requests from customs authorities to provide information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through the ELO of the Czech Republic.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods through which the transport of risky shipments is announced.
The transport of certain excise products in quantities exceeding the limits set by the European Commission Regulation and the transport assessed as risky by the tax administration are considered to be a risk consignment.
The exchange of information is carried out in two forms:
- information - sent when the limits set are exceeded,
- warning message - sent if the transport of goods is assessed as risky.
When assessing the degree of risk of a consignment, ELO SR shall use the SEED database for sending the warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
If the data in the SEED database does not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee of the goods or the registered office of the consignee does not match), ELO SR shall draw up a warning message to the ELO of the Member State of receipt of the goods.
When drawing up the reports, ELO shall be governed by the regulations of the Tax and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457, which shall, inter alia, determine the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measure for the preparation of information and warning reports.
In the audited period ELO SR sent one warning message to ELO CR.
In the Czech Republic, information on initiated transport of products in quantities exceeding specified limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving transport.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic assesses the shipment as risky on the basis of its own analysis, it will prepare a so-called warning message, which it will send to the relevant Member State via the ELO of the Czech Republic.
In 2005 ELO CR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
The MVS - the system for controlling the movement of goods - enables the MVS, through requests, to control the individual transport of excise products as well as the control of the specified route of transport between the entities listed in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information shall take place on the basis of a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system shall be used in particular in cases where the consignor takes possession of a certified copy No 3 of the accompanying document and requests, for example, a refund of excise duty and where the particulars contained in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
In the audited period, ELO SR sent 33 requests to the Czech Republic.
ELO CR sent ELO SR 25 requests to MVS.
The customs authorities in the Czech Republic most frequently examined the particulars contained in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantities of products received or dispatched, or whether the consignor of the products mentioned in the accompanying document is entitled to dispose of excise products, unless this fact could be verified in the international SEED database.
Received by the MVS in both countries, they were referred to the customs offices locally responsible for the recipients or consignors of excise products.
The customs authorities examined the requested data and notified the outcome of the investigation via ELO to the other Member State.
6. Summary
The cooperation between the SAO-Czech Republic and the SAO SR allowed to compare the basic legislation governing excise duties in both countries, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the initiation and termination of the transport of products under suspension between the two countries, the registration of such transactions and further to compare the exchange of information between customs authorities in the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 By comparing the legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, differences were found:
a) in the procedure of tax entities and tax administrations when starting the transport of products under suspension.
Transport of products under suspension of tax may be initiated by the tax entity in the Czech Republic only with the approval of the tax administrator, which authorizes the start of transport on condition that the products transported have been provided with a guarantee of the amount of tax attributable to them.
The start of the transport of products under suspension in SR is not subject to the authorisation of the tax administration.
During the audited period, the taxpayer was obliged to notify the tax administrator of the start of transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
He could start shipping mineral oils, beer and wine without informing the tax administrator.
In 2006, the Slovak Republic gradually adopted amendments to all excise laws under which the consignor of goods under suspension of tax is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office which is locally responsible for the consignor before the start of transport;
(b) within the time limits for dispatch of copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The recipient in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copy No. 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification at the latest the following working day after the end of the transport.
Certified copy No 3 shall be sent to the consignor no later than the following business day after receipt from the tax administrator.
The consignee in the SR is obliged to send to the consignor of the products copy No 3 certified by the tax administrator and the recipient of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
Customs authorities in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of products under suspension.
The content and method of keeping this record is not regulated by legislation in the Czech Republic or Slovakia.
The customs authorities in both countries shall enter in the register all data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which transport is carried out.
There is currently no single electronic system for monitoring the transport of goods under suspension between Member States of the European Union, enabling excise administrators in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods.
According to Decision of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of excise products is foreseen from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of a contract for cooperation in control activities, the Czech Party has forwarded to the Slovak party a database of products subject to suspension started in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5,876 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak party handed over to the Czech party a database of products under suspension of tax started in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The database contained 3,319 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech party compared the data on the transport listed in the register started in the Czech Republic with the records of the Czech Republic terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak party compared data on the transport of goods under the suspension procedure initiated in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of data was made more difficult by the fact that the quantities of goods transported were not reported uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to unambiguously assign data on each transport in both registers, a check of the accompanying documents was carried out and no breach of the suspension scheme or cases of tax evasion was detected.
On the basis of the knowledge from the parallel controls, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the registers in order to improve the management of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the transport and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/ES of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movements under suspension of tax in the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the President of the Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic.
Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of follow-up
Introductory word
Taxation is generally a key source of public revenue.
It therefore goes without saying that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAI) should focus their attention on this area.
Examples are value added tax fraud ("VAT").
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated annually in the European Union (the "EU").
Already in 2005, participants in the VI. the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
Within this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very appropriate area for control cooperation as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic ("SAO") and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, "BRH") carried out the first parallel VAT control action in 2006.
The relevant report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not limited to a single country but is widespread across the EU, close cooperation between the SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to address this problem.
Both SAIs therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a parallel follow-up check.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject: (CZ) Administration of value added tax (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (follow-up)
Control objective:
(CZ) The aim of the audit action was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter "Germany"), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The audit action was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
The intention was also to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting control findings were intended to compare with the established best practice (if any).
The audited period was 2006 to 2008, in the case of factual contexts as well as the period preceding and following, until the end of the check.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The subsequent inspection of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
During previous parallel checks, suspicious cases of intracommunity transactions were detected.
Some of them requested further clearance.
On the basis of the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations on the administration of VAT.
The follow-up exercise was used to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspected cases.
The audit also focused on selected cases of high-risk intracommunity transactions, mutual assistance in the recovery of receivables and the implementation of VAT controls on large tax entities.
When reviewing VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, auditors obtained the following control findings:
1. Recommendations from the previous check
• Recommendation 1: Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
In previous parallel checks, the comparison of VAT registration systems in both countries revealed differences.
As different marketing authorisations cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for registering payers within the EU.
This recommendation has been presented at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 ("Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including a VAT tax identification number database.
It also amended common standards for registration and deregistration of tax payers.
The SAI expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of this document, agreed by the EU Member States under ECOFIN, no longer contains this issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to regard this intention as a relevant prevention tool to combat VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly summary reporting
In the context of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of summary reports, thereby allowing for a more timely examination of intra-community transaction values.
Council Directive No 2008/117/ES amending the 2006/112/ES Directive on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion linked to intra-Community transactions shortens the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit summary reports on a monthly basis was not introduced within the specified deadline in accordance with applicable EU rules, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports in Germany with a view to improving the reliability of VIES data and considering linking the two VAT return schemes and summary reports
The German tax administration accepted the recommendations of BRH and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing of successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful risk management criteria, components and approaches need to be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, perpetrators of fraudulent activity will be chosen by the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The check found that our two Member States use different risk management systems that have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO inspected the EUROCANET system, which enables information to be exchanged within the EU, while BRH concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected cases of intracommunity transactions
During the previous control action, commercial transactions were jointly examined for which there were doubts as to their realisation or irregularities in the reporting of commercial transactions in tax returns or summary reports by the taxpayer from both countries.
Both SAIs selected nine cases for follow-up, which included intracommunity movements of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The checks carried out by the tax authorities of the respective countries have not been concluded by the date of completion of our previous joint control action.
The follow-up audit verified that most of the tax proceedings in relation to the selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany were concluded and that adequate measures were taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT credits or avoidance of input tax refunds).
3. Control of selected cases of risky intracommunity transactions
High-risk cases of intracommunity transactions carried out by EU payers included in EUROCANET have been selected for inspection.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risk taxpayers within the EU.
The participation of Member States in this scheme is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is inconvenient for an active participant in a system if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
In view of the fact that the German tax administration was not involved in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, no information could be obtained as to which suppliers with German VAT ID were assessed as risky.
The SAO identified cases of normal commercial transactions as well as suspected involvement in carousel business or VAT fraud as part of the audit action.
Tax administrators have limited possibilities to control risky transactions, especially with regard to so-called missing traders, whereas mere physical examination of documents can be difficult to prove to the taxpayer any fraudulent conduct.
A similar situation for the tax administrator arises when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intracommunity carousel transactions.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater mutual cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and irregularities in transport documentation and to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the end consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is reluctant to actively participate in EUROCANET because of the lack of a sufficient legal base.
In Germany, other tools are being used to detect risky tax payers that have so far proved their worth to the German tax administration.
There is a need to communicate and exchange experiences between EU Member States in this area.
The EU Council reached political agreement on a proposal for a regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation lies in the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in the use of EUROCANET should provide the basis for the creation of this new VAT fraud network.
4. Mutual assistance in the recovery of claims
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States are subject to the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of processing applications for international assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is identical.
The SAO and the BRH made a comparison of the statistics submitted by both Member States for the years 2006-2008 to the European Commission.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
The two SAIs consider it useful to renegotiate statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent mismatches.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the SAIs agree that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to produce an analysis on the basis of more detailed statistics to help Member States to strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the view of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with low recovery success rates to increase the recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The SAI analysed the legal situation relating to VAT control for large tax entities (hereinafter referred to as "VDS") in both countries.
In addition, they collected information from tax authorities in the form of a questionnaire on the areas that SAI considers essential to the management of this issue.
The responses received clearly show that the situation in both countries is different.
The Czech Republic has a system that relies on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from tax checks, balance sheet and profit and loss statements, etc.) to guide the selection of risk-inclined cases.
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
The establishment of a specialised financial office for the management of VDS is planned in 2012.
There is not yet a similar system in Germany, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT control in general.
Germany has so far concentrated more on the selection of the individual cases in question, in particular on the basis of the VAT return and the summary report.
The analysis of this data is based on different risk management components that will be strengthened.
3. Progress of the control action
3.1 The Czech Republic Control Action
The audit was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by the Department of State Budget Revenue and Territorial Unions IX. Pilsen, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited persons were: Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter the "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter the "FA"): FA Brno II, FU Brno III, FU Brno IV, FU in Břeclav, FA in Domažlice, FU in Hodonín, FU in Hradec Králové, FU in Cheb, FU in Jablonec nad Nisou, FU in Karlovy Vary, FU in Králupy nad Vltavou, FU in Kraslice, FU Ostrava I, FA Ostrava III, FU in Písek, FU in Pilsen, FU for Prague 1, FA for Prague 4, FU for Prague 8, FU in Rakovník, FU in Sokolov, FU in Tábor, FU in High Toll, FU in Zlín and FU in Žamberk.
The audit conclusion of this audit action was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 Progress of the control action in Germany
The audit was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the Control Department for indirect taxes and by the staff of the designated Regional Audit Offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
Following the selection of a sample of cases, a number of Länder were informed of the mission of the control action.
In addition to interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, audits took place in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hessen, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Munich Central Tax Office), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North)
In addition, negotiations took place with the financial offices of Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-South) and financial directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
The audit findings were reported to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
In preparation of the parallel control actions, a meeting of representatives of the two audit institutions was held in September 2008 to discuss and identify the topics of control.
Finally, in December 2008, the leaders of the two SAIs signed an agreement on cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls.
At a meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the control teams informed each other about the initial results achieved during the preparation of the audit, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed a way forward.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2. - 4 December 2009.
The control teams exchanged findings between them and agreed a timetable for drawing up a joint report.
Both SAIs decided to focus on: • follow-up of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report • examination of selected cases of intracommunity transactions between Czech and German tax payers, which have not been resolved during the previous parallel check • examination of selected cases of intracommunity transactions between Czech and German tax payers, which have been classified as high risk cases • control of tax administration procedures in the area of international assistance in the recovery of VAT claims, • tax control of large companies.
A report on the results of the parallel control actions was prepared during a workshop in June 2010.
4. Check VAT management in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from previous inspection
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
The conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
On the basis of the results of the previous audit, the SAO recommended adjusting the VAT registration conditions and introducing a new rule for cancellation in the Czech Republic.
The modified conditions should make it possible to reduce the risk of possible tax evasion for VAT collection more effectively.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the tax authorities did not use the right to cancel VAT registration to payers who did not comply with obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (VAT Act).
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed an amendment to the provision introducing an obligation for tax administrators to cancel VAT registration on repeated failure to submit a VAT return.
According to the VAT Act, the tax administrator may cancel the registration of the "ex offo" tax payer in cases where: (a) the taxpayer has not performed the reason to the tax administrator for 12 consecutive months, (b) the payer fails to fulfil his obligations under this Act, (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous audit action, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the FA for Prague 1 to cancel the VAT registration at 31 January of the following calendar year for so-called non-established payers who had no obligation to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The FA for Prague 1 often did not cancel the VAT registration for these payers, as the relevant provision provided for insufficient time to cancel the registration.
This problem was removed by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the non-established tax payer in the event that the tax payer has not supplied any goods or services subject to tax or exempt goods or services with a right to deduct VAT in the previous calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly summary reporting
In the context of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of summary reports.
The Council Directive shortens the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
The obligation to submit summary reports in electronic form is also newly established.
The summary report shall be filed by the payer even if the services for which the place of performance is determined in accordance with Section 9 (1) of the Financial Regulation. 1 of the VAT Act, provided to another Member State by a taxable person in another Member State and if he is obliged to declare and pay tax on such services by their recipient.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/ES amending Directive 2006/112/ES as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports with a view to improving the reliability of data in the VIES system This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech Administration compares data on intracommunity transactions reported in VAT tax returns and summary reports of Czech payers automated in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing of successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore a priority concern and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is illustrated, inter alia, by the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009 in which an external evaluator attempted to establish the difference between the eligible and actually collected VAT levels in the 25 EU Member States (hereinafter referred to as "EU-25") during the period 2000-2006.
On the basis of the analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated amount of loss on non-collected VAT for this period is between EUR 90 billion and EUR 113 billion, while on average 12% of eligible VAT is not collected annually.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was estimated at 18%.
In the context of international cooperation, the previous control action stated that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by just one Member State.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO audited EUROCANET for information exchange in the EU.
Cases of risk intracommunity transactions carried out by EU tax payers included in EUROCANET have been selected for inspection (see Chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and improving the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved through the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should improve cooperation between responsible authorities in a way that allows fraud to be detected in their embryos.
This network should later become an important source of information when assessing intra-Community performance risks.
The ECOFIN Council approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7 October 200812, while setting out the basic principles to be followed by the network.
The EUROFISC is an already functioning system of rapid and selective exchange of information by EUROCANET, developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and supported by the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky commercial transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations of the first report revealed the following:
Recommendation 1
The conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
The German tax administration established a well-functioning system for registering tax payers, based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance drew the Commission's attention to this system in October 2007.
System improvement shall be carried out on an ongoing basis.
Currently, data from the questionnaire are processed electronically and will subsequently be used for the survey as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission has submitted a proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed work on this issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure the level of standards already achieved in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly summary reporting
On 8 April 2010, a law was adopted transposing EU directives into national law.
This Act contains provisions concerning the monthly submission of summary reports on intracommunity supplies.
Those provisions took effect on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and aggregated reports in order to improve the reliability of VIES data and to consider linking the two VAT return systems and summary reports
A joint working group consisting of workers from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance was set up.
The group developed a strategy for the automatic comparison of VAT tax returns and summary reports.
This strategy has so far been discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the working group looked at an instrument designed to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing of successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany participates in this exchange in the framework of the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of this platform and, following a written consultation of 18 October 2006, the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 Action Plan.
The members of the Platform are further divided into subgroups dealing with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • behavioural influences, • evaluation, • updating the Risk Management Guide.
Reports on the performance of these sub-groups were published at the beginning of 2010.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of conditions for VAT registration and cancellation in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included an extension of existing databases within the EU, including a VAT tax identification number database.
It also regulated common minimum standards for registration and deregistration of tax payers.
The issue of registration and cancellation has so far been left to the national legislation of the EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed work on this issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already reached in Germany did not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached political agreement on that proposal for a Regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States must implement national procedures and are only obliged to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee of those procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission has failed to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore like the Commission to make further efforts in this respect.
Monthly summary reporting
In the context of international cooperation, it was recommended in the previous control action that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of summary reports, allowing for a more timely review of intra-community transaction values.
Council Directive No 2008/117/ES amending the 2006/112/ES Directive on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion linked to intra-Community transactions shortens the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010 and took effect on 1 July 2010 in Germany.
Germany has not introduced the obligation to submit summary reports monthly according to the specified calendar, whereas the Czech Republic has (in accordance with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports in Germany with a view to improving the reliability of VIES data and considering linking the two VAT return schemes and summary reports
The German tax administration accepted the recommendations of BRH and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is ongoing so far and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing of successful risk management system criteria, components and approaches at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-inclined traders.
The SAO has inspected the EUROCANET system used for the exchange of information in the EU (see above). 4.3).
In this area, BRH concentrated on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected cases of intracommunity transactions
The previous auditing operation jointly examined the execution of commercial transactions for which there were doubts about their implementation or irregularities in the way the payers from both countries reported these transactions in their VAT tax returns or summary statements.
The two audit institutions selected nine cases involving intracommunitary movements of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany for follow-up, the control of which was not completed during the previous joint control action by the tax administrations of both countries.
1)
The Czech payer acquired goods worth EUR 22,686 from the German payer in the first quarter of 2005.
The Czech payer did not acknowledge the acquisition of goods in his VAT return because the German payer did not have VAT ID allocated during that period, but only a tax number for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator has received information that according to the German VAT law, the taxpayer supplying goods to other Member States need not have VAT ID allocated in order to exempt the intracommunitary supply of goods from VAT.
A subsequent audit of the SAO revealed that the Czech taxpayer filed an additional VAT return on the basis of a check carried out by the Czech tax administrator, in which he declared the acquisition of goods at the same value and claimed the same amount of VAT in this tax return.
2)
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to acquire goods worth EUR 12,561 from the German payer.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of these goods and did not state in his VAT return.
The German tax administration refused to cooperate on request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 as the turnover of transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence, it terminated the inspection without finding and the tax liability remained at its original level.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had received two spontaneous information from Germany pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showing that the German payer had invoiced those goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer acquired the goods from the Slovak payer and listed them in the regular VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
The Czech payer was to acquire a passenger car worth EUR 48,500 from the German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The Czech taxpayer did not grant the acquisition of the goods in question.
The tax payer did not submit VAT returns since August 2004. The tax administrator charged VAT of CZK 0 for that quarter.
On the basis of the information obtained in the context of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, in March 2007 the tax administrator invited the taxpayer to submit an additional VAT return, which was not submitted by the payer.
A subsequent audit revealed that the tax administrator performed further tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the Czech taxpayer sold the car in the Czech Republic.
The Czech Tax Administrator issued a statement of payment for the December 2004 tax period, which additionally charged VAT on the acquisition of goods from another Member State and subsequent sales of CZK 295 379.
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was annulled with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of executions of the taxable debtor's liable assets, this arrears appear to be impregnable.
4)
The Czech payer was to deliver new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany during the fourth quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005, totalling EUR 198 167.
The reply to the request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 indicated that a pending tax and criminal proceeding was taking place against the German entity in Germany.
During the subsequent inspection, BRH obtained information that after the completion of the tax procedure in Germany, it was demonstrably established that the German taxpayer had been incorporated into fraudulent activities.
Intracommunity acquisitions were taxed at EUR 182,424 (2004) and EUR 369,690 (2005).
The SAO subsequently discovered that the Czech payer was involved in carousel business with new means of transport.
On the basis of information from the German tax administration concerning the examination of the supply of goods, the Czech tax body started checking VAT for the taxation period April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the audit findings and information obtained as part of the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally charged CZK 703 031 of VAT for the period May 2005 and CZK 726 551 for the period June 2005.
5)
In February 2005, Czech payer A was to acquire a machine from a German payer totalling EUR 58 000.
This German payer was to deliver a machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech B payer in Q3 2004, but B denied the acquisition.
A subsequent audit of the SAO revealed that Payer B had acquired a machine from a German company with an organizational unit established in the Czech Republic.
The Czech taxpayer A did not declare the acquisition of goods from the German payer in his VAT return.
A reply from the German tax administrator to a request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 indicated that the German payer had not made intracommunity deliveries of the machine worth EUR 58 000 but the supply of goods within the Czech Republic.
