By subsequent inspection, BRH found that after a tax check, the intracommunity of the machine was re-qualified for domestic delivery and the VAT exemption was abolished.
6)
In the third quarter of 2004, the German taxpayer was to deliver goods worth EUR 11,600 to the Czech payer.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO subsequently discovered that the Czech tax administrator had assessed the additional VAT return filed, where the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State was wrongly indicated, including the acquisition of goods of that value.
BRH found that, after receiving a reply to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax administrator corrected the tax return of the German taxpayer and additionally charged VAT of EUR 1 600.
Further movement of goods in Germany and application of VAT in Germany is subject to tax control.
The German payer's summary report has not yet been corrected as only the payer who submitted the summary report can make corrections to the summary reports in Germany.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on whether the Czech taxpayer acquired a passenger car worth EUR 47,400 from the German taxpayer in February 2005.
The Czech tax administrator charged the Czech taxpayer CZK 0 after the tax procedure for the February 2005 tax period and informed the German tax administrator that it could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech taxpayer.
A subsequent audit of the SAO found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled in 2007 for non-compliance and the Czech tax administrator sent documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
A subsequent inspection by BRH found that the German payer had changed its registered office and that the new local tax administrator had abolished the VAT exemption for the delivery of the car to the Czech taxpayer.
The German taxpayer has not yet corrected the data in the summary report and has lodged an appeal against the tax administration's decision.
8)
According to VIES data, the German payer supplied a total value of EUR 33,205 to the Czech taxpayer between the third quarter of 2004 and the first quarter of 2005.
A subsequent audit of the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator attempted to ascertain the reasons for the differences arising from the Czech tax payer's acquisition of goods during the period from Q3 2004 to Q1 2005.
The Czech tax payer repeatedly filed an additional VAT return for the 1 quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not clarify the difference in the value of the acquired goods totalling CZK 134,273 for the period from Q3 2004 to Q1 2005, as according to the Czech tax administrator, it was not possible to accurately capture business transactions for each quarter and therefore the tax administrator accepted additional tax returns submitted.
9)
The German taxpayer delivered EUR 46,854 worth of goods to the Czech payer in the third quarter of 2004.
During the same period, the Czech payer granted intracommunity acquisitions of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of deliveries made in the context of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of delivery of goods of EUR 31,998, which corresponds to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data provided in the VIES system.
A subsequent audit of the SAO revealed that the Czech payer filed an additional tax return for the taxable period July 2004 until January 2007 following many tax urgencies.
In this tax return, the tax payer also claimed the deduction of VAT, leaving the tax liability unchanged for that tax period.
The subsequent audit verified that the majority of tax proceedings were completed in selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany and that the tax administrators in both the Czech Republic and Germany took appropriate measures (i.e. additional VAT assessment or avoidance of input tax refund).
4.3 Control of selected cases of risk intracommunity transactions
4.3.1 Audit results in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET may be an important source of information for the detection of risk operators within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with the customer data.
Starting in the first quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic is sending data on risky transactions and tax entities acting as suppliers to EUROCANET.
Within the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for inspection.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States have been collected in EUROCANET.
Given that the German tax administration did not participate in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, no information could be obtained to help establish whether suppliers with German VAT ID had been assessed by the German tax administration as risky entities.
The control action revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel or VAT fraud.
Where appropriate, tax administrations have benefited from the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• Tax administrators did not reveal any suspicions of involvement in risk transactions when verifying signal information.
Tax authorities shall monitor such tax entities on an ongoing basis for their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• The tax authorities did not show any deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT in the accounting records submitted, despite finding irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or detecting business relations with suspected or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• Verifying business transactions was complicated as some taxpayers did not cooperate with the tax authorities and could not be contacted.
The local tax authorities mostly examined the risk tax entities and the risk transactions identified in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax administrators have limited possibilities when examining risky transactions, especially in connection with the screening of so-called missing traders, and it is difficult to prove fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer only from physical control of documents.
Stricter requirements for VAT registration and more flexible cancellation of registrations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered for the purpose of reporting fictitious intra-EU supplies of goods or for the purpose of issuing formally correct tax documents to payers who are unduly receiving input VAT deductions on their basis.
In cases where there is suspicion of involvement of tax operators in carousel transactions and other fraud and imports and exports of goods from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater mutual cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help in identifying goods and irregularities in transport documentation and in monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness in the scheme, which should be removed by setting up a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Results of the inspection in Germany
BRH analysed the information available with the Federal Central Tax Office, which contained data from the EUROCANET system.
These data were a criterion for collecting six files of German tax payers for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, has refused to actively participate in EUROCANET.
Germany thus has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but only receives EUROCANET data.
The reasons for this position are set out in the following statement: it is not legally permissible for government (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis for breaching the applicable tax classification rules.
In addition, the Government has no reliable information on how such data are used by other Member States under EUROCANET. "17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has carried out analyses of EUROCANET data and has been referring them to the financial authorities of the Länder in accordance with the agreed procedure.
The German tax authorities receive control information on the direct business relationships of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in EUROCANET.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relations with traders from other Member States who also maintain trade relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is inconvenient for an active participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
As a result, the control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in the detection of VAT fraud, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
Tax administrations in both countries have a number of other tools for detecting fraudulent transactions, but a comprehensive risk management system within the EU is necessary.
The EU Council reached political agreement on the proposal for a regulation, the main contribution of which is the establishment of the EUROFISC network.
Experience gained from the use of EUROCANET data should also be part of the envisaged VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experiences at European level.
On the other hand, cases brought before courts at national and European level show that a debate between the Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intracommunity transactions may be necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
4.4.1 International assistance for the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following Directives provide a fundamental adjustment to international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council Directive No 76/308/EHS on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from operations forming part of the financing system of the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/ES amending Directive No 76/308/EHS on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/ES implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308/EHS on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims arising from certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive No. 76/308/EHS was implemented by Act No. 252/2000 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
Following the adoption of Council Directive No. 2001/44/ES, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal order while amending the aforementioned Act No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims, was adopted.
Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28.11.2008 is a new regulation in the system of international cooperation for the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU.
The Annex to the Regulation sets out new models of applications to be used from the 1.1.2009, a new electronic communication obligation and an obligation for the applicant authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
Guiding principles for providing international cooperation in the recovery of claims:
1 reciprocity;
(2) assistance shall only be granted on the basis of an application containing the prescribed requirements;
(iii) assistance shall not apply to financial claims which are punishable by criminal law in the requested State;
In providing international assistance for the recovery of claims, the national law of the State which has been requested for assistance shall be followed;
5th foreign receivables do not take precedence in recovery;
6 assistance shall be granted only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
The 7th principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has, without success, used all applicable options to recover a claim under its legal order).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines the three forms by which assistance is carried out, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending claims for recovery to other EU Member States
The local competent tax office shall send the request for information, request for receivables or request for recovery to the Czech Ministry of Finance by electronic means.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will arrange for the translation of the application into the relevant language, scan it including the annexes and send it to the competent tax administration of the designated state through the CCN/CSI network.
There are two essential requirements for recovery: the claim must be more than EUR 1,500 and must not be older than 5 years.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receiving claims for recovery from other EU Member States
When receiving an application from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the application as soon as possible, within seven days at the latest.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it shall communicate to the requesting authority the reasons for rejecting the application and indicate the specific provisions of the directive it invokes.
This communication shall be sent no later than three months after the date of confirmation of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify that the application has all the requirements of the law and should immediately transmit the application through the Financial Directorate to the locally competent tax office for processing.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax administrator, inter alia, ascertains the property of the debtor, e.g. by acquiring records from the Land Registry, checking accounts in banks, verifying the registration of vehicles at the Transport Inspectorate, etc.
After a period of six months from the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed, the Czech Ministry of Finance should communicate to the requesting authority the outcome of the investigation carried out to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities where a claim cannot be recovered, the requesting authority should also be informed thereof.
Each amount recovered by the tax administrator shall be transferred to the applicant authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not excluded that the Czech tax administrator enforcing foreign receivables may allow payment or payment in instalments if the State which requested the recovery so agrees.
During the recovery period, the debtor is subject to interest or penalty payments pursuant to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Charges.
This interest or penalty belongs to the State which requested the recovery.
In the case of accepted requests for recovery, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not advance applications to the local tax administrations in time, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the context of international assistance in the recovery of claims also in the case of applications received from Czech tax authorities.
The audit action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance failed to comply with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in recovery within six months of the date on which the request was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistics
The Czech Ministry of Finance complies with the provisions of § 13 para. 4 Act No. 191/2004 Coll. it shall process by 15 March each year statistics for the European Commission indicating the number of requests for information, service or recovery, dispatched or received in the previous year, indicating the amount of claims to which applications relate.
The European Commission shall, on the basis of supporting documents provided by all EU Member States, prepare a report on the recovery status, which it shall submit to the Council of the EU and the European Parliament.
The audit found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistics due to an error in the item of recovered receivables in 2008 by EUR 5,250 thousand, indicating the incorrect value of the recovered VAT claim (this was a shift in the decimal point after the conversion of the receivables from Czech crowns to euro value).
This error was subsequently reflected in the statistics of the European Commission.
Information on mutual assistance, including recovered amounts, can be found in the table below.
4.4.2 International assistance for the recovery of claims in Germany
Legal authorisation for international administrative assistance in tax matters is derived from European Communities law, Council Directive No 2008/55/ES of 26 May 2008 (EC Debt Recovery Directive) and Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In the interests of more accessible formulation and clarity, the EC Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive No 76/308/EHS of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have already been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply inter alia to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Debt Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by Law (EC) on the Collection of State Taxes of 3 May 2003.
The enforcement procedure in Germany is governed by the German Fiscal Code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities which are applicable in national jurisdiction and under the EC Administrative Assistance Act.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) enshrines the legal provisions governing the enforcement procedure.
The administrative actions of the tax authorities shall be governed in particular by enforcement instructions and enforcement instructions.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with representatives of the Länder with regard to the principles of administrative assistance in tax assessment and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general conditions for submitting claims for recovery are as follows:
• Legal requirements must be met (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic recovery funds have already been exhausted.
• Claims subject to recovery requests must be final.
• From the issuance of the enforcement order or the date on which the claim becomes final (i.e. is no longer subject to appeal), no more than 5 years may elapse until the date of submission of the applications.
• The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending claims for recovery to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementing departments of the tax authorities to the competent foreign office, such as the Czech Customs Office, through the intermediary office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The detailed procedure follows the Methodological Guidance on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Claims) of 19 January 2004.25 At present, the Working Group of the Federal Government and the Provincial Governments is reviewing this methodological guideline to adapt it to the Enforcement Directive.
The application, including the annexes, shall be submitted electronically to the intermediary office by the tax office.
This Office shall check the accuracy of the application in terms of content and form.
If the application is not correct, it shall be returned to the competent tax authority.
If it fulfils all the requirements, it is referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Financial Office subsequently ensures the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and also ensures translation of the request.
Procedure for receiving claims for recovery from other EU Member States
Applications for recovery received from other Member States shall be registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and sent confirmation of receipt within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office will check that the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office shall submit such requests to the intermediary office, which shall further refer them to the competent financial authorities and monitor their execution.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
Where an application is processed for more than 6 months, it shall invite the intermediate office to submit a preliminary report to be submitted pursuant to Article 16 of Commission Directive No 2002/94/DG.
Once the formal and factual formalities of the application have been checked, the implementing services shall notify the method of recovery.
Any sums recovered must be transferred to the bank account indicated in the application within one month of receipt.
Statistics
Information on mutual assistance in the recovery of receivables between Germany and the Czech Republic in the years 2006-2008 (k 31.12.2008) is contained in the table below.
4.4.3 Control of recovery, case studies
Within the framework of international cooperation, 21 requests for international assistance in the recovery of claims between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for inspection.
Ten selected cases were examined:
1.
On 20 December 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for recovery of a VAT claim for 2004 and 2005 totalling EUR 3,883, i.e. CZK 109,820, for a Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request for recovery to the tax administrator until 26.2.2008.
In order to secure the recovered receivable, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
As it was not possible to pay the entire recovered claim even by stopping the real estate, a repayment schedule was agreed with the Czech taxpayer with instalments of min. 2,000 CZK a month.
On 31 February 2009, information on the recovery status was sent to the German tax administration stating that, at 25 February 2009, this claim was partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49,600.
This amount was sent to Germany and a further instalment of CZK 28.8.2009 was sent to Germany on 3,000.
2.
On 7.1.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 180,869 in Germany, i.e. CZK 4,434,915, for VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance only sent the application to the tax administrator on 27. 11. 2008.
The tax administrator found that the debtor does not own any enforceable assets by checking the ownership of accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movable goods.
Furthermore, a local investigation found that the debtor did not stay at the address of permanent residence for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6.4.2009 and was sent to the German tax administration on 16.4.2009.
3.
On 21.11.2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for recovery relating to the turnover tax arrears and accessories of the Czech tax entity amounting to EUR 3,139, i.e. CZK 84,846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this claim to the tax administrator on 6. 8. 2008, although already on 18. 2. 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
On 9.12.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the tax administrator that the request for recovery was settled by payment of the claim by a Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also paid in the context of recovery in the Czech Republic and transferred to Germany on 27.10.2008.
Due to long periods of time in which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the tax administrators in charge, the receivables were paid twice by the entity in Germany itself and recovered by the Czech tax administrator.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been included in the claim for further recovery of EUR 6,649 to be sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance records only a claim for recovery totalling EUR 3,139. The claim for recovery totalling EUR 6,649 is not recorded in the Czech Ministry of Finance.
4.
On 15.9.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany to recover the tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed EUR 39,957 in Germany for income tax and VAT and accessories, i.e. CZK 956,654.
On 19.12.2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request to the Czech tax administrator.
The recovery procedure was initiated on 1 June 2009 and execution was ordered at the commandment of the receivable in the Czech Republic's bank accounts and the payroll deduction (withholding was CZK 7,000).
When dealing with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it questionable.
The Czech tax administrator found that the tax entity was in the past willing to repay EUR 250 per month, which was not accepted by the German tax administrator.
The tax entity promised to discuss the application with the German tax administrator in order to achieve a change in the amount of its claim.
The recovery of the claim continued at the time of the SAO control action.
5.
On 19 December 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery from Germany concerning a Czech tax entity that owed income tax for 2005 and turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories totalling EUR 113 444, i.e. CZK 3 116 304.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request to the FA for Prague 1, which is in charge of the tax administration of non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, only on 14. 11. 2008 because it was not possible to identify the local tax administrator on the basis of that address.
In the course of the investigation, the FA received information that the debtor had an income of EUR 4,704 on 19.9.2008; however, the FA could no longer issue an enforcement order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance only forwarded the request for recovery after that date.
On 26.1.2009 day, the Czech tax administrator initiated recovery and issued an enforcement order commanding the debtor's money receivables in accounts held with banks and savings and credit cooperatives.
The recovery of the claim continued at the time of the SAO control action.
6.
The Czech tax administrator requested international cooperation in recovering the VAT receivable and the costs of proceedings totalling CZK 146 223 742 on 3. 10. 2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for recovery to the German tax administration until 13.5.2008.
On 8.9.2008, the German tax administrator transferred to the Czech authorities via the Federal Bank an amount obtained from the execution of funds in the debtor's account of EUR 17,700, i.e. CZK 439,226.
An error in the conversion of the recovered amount was detected when verifying the amount recovered.
The recovered amount of CZK 146 223 742 was converted at the rate of EUR 1 = CZK 25,065 erroneously to EUR 583,378.
The correct conversion of the recovered amount is EUR 5 833 781,83.
A request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1.3.2007, the Czech tax administrator sent the Czech Ministry of Finance a request for the recovery of the tax arrears with the Czech tax entity, which owed CZK 1,970,632 for VAT and accessories, i.e. EUR 79,847.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the application to the German tax administration only on 10. 11. 2008.
On 4.2.2009, the German tax administrator called on the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant decreases in the company's turnover in the second half of 2008 and in particular in the first half of 2009 and the liquidation situation of the company, the following arrears were made: EUR 4 600 on 8/04/2009, EUR 3 000 on 6/5/2009 and EUR 2 500 on 16/6/2009.
These payments were sent to the account of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
On 23 June 2009, the German tax administrator agreed with the debtor to pay a further instalment of EUR 2,500 by 30 June 2009.
8.
The claim for recovery totalling EUR 398,653, i.e. CZK 9,832,779 including the real estate transfer tax receivable, was received from the Czech tax administrator to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22.5.2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2. 10. 2008.
On 3.4.2009, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a notification from the German tax administration that the application had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax administration justified the repayment by saying that the real estate transfer tax is not a tax within the meaning of Article 2 (1) of the Treaty. (e), (f), (g) and (b) (h) Council Directive No 2008/55/ES.
Furthermore, the German Tax Administration stated that Article 2 (1) of the Treaty does not constitute State aid. g) concerns receivables related to income tax and property tax.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive No 2008/55/ES applies to taxes on income and property listed in Article 1 (1) of the Treaty. This Decision shall enter into force on the twentieth day following that of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Union. 4 Council Directive No 77/799/EHS.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed to draw up and submit a new application for recovery excluding the real estate transfer tax arrears amounting to CZK 61,759 and indicating VAT arrears, corporate tax and personal income tax, which will be re-sent to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has received a new request from the Czech tax administrator to recover tax arrears relating to the same tax entity that owes CZK 7,079,735 in income tax and VAT.
9.
On 6.2.2006, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed CZK 3,445,782 in personal income tax and VAT, i.e. EUR 123,328.
Of this amount, CZK 1,133,967 was VAT.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the application to the German tax administration until 18.4.2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded a reply from the German tax administration from 9.7.2007 to 11.11.2008.
The reply stated that the German tax administrator issued on 11.6.2007 an enforcement order for a bank account with the bank, but that it did not have any business relations with the taxpayer.
By doing so, the German tax administration considered the application to be settled.
10.
On 26.9.2005, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT arrears totalling CZK 1,296,845, i.e. EUR 43,591.
The application from the Czech tax administrator was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10. 10. 2005.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request to the German tax administration on 15.12.2005.
Before sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax administrator executed the debtor's money in the bank accounts and the wage deduction and established a lien on the immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authority on 16.3.2005.
The reply to the request for information received by the Czech tax administrator on 16 September 2005 indicated that the Czech tax entity was staying in Germany and had an income of EUR 8,437 from the non-business activity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a reply to the request for recovery on 20.4.2006, but only forwarded it to the Czech tax administrator on 12.2.2008.
The reply stated that no recovery procedure could have been initiated in Germany on account of the debtor's insolvency - no assets had been established and his income from the business was already subject to another enforcement procedure.
In doing so, the German tax administration considered the request for recovery to be settled.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the area of international recovery assistance, all EU Member States are subject to the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of processing applications for international assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is identical.
The SAO and the BRH made a comparison of the statistics submitted by the two Member States for the period 2006-2008 to the European Commission.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In its 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay increased attention to the management of their statistics.
In its 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of mismatches in statistics had decreased, even though the number of applications had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important to renegotiate statistics at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent mismatches, otherwise the data reported by individual EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the two SAIs agree that reliable statistics should show the annual number of applications as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amount of the claims recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by the Member States, as this can assist Member States in assessing their own effectiveness in combating VAT fraud.
The fact that recovery rates can be calculated broken down by Member State, both SAIs consider it useful for Member States with lower recovery rates to step up their efforts and try to improve the recovery rate at least to the level of the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit claims for recovery on time to local tax administrations.
A similar situation was found for applications for international assistance received from Czech tax authorities.
The audit action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance failed to comply with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on International Assistance in the Recovery of Claims, because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in recovery within six months of the date on which the request was confirmed.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for controlling VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the administration of taxes and charges.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons established or established for the purpose of doing business and whose net turnover for the tax period indicated in the personal/corporate income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion or more.
The classification of the tax entity as a VDS took place after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax period, for the first time in 2003.
The tax entity ceased to be referred to as a VDS if, in three consecutive tax periods since the end of the period when it filed the tax return on the basis of which it was classified among the VDS, its net turnover for the tax period fell below that threshold.
A tax entity may not be excluded from the VDS register without carrying out a tax check on at least one tax for one tax period.
All VDS were audited at least five years apart by the end of 2009.
Since 2010, at least every 2 years a written evaluation of the tax entity must be carried out and the tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax must be eliminated by the chosen follow-up procedure.
The control of the FA is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administrator generally opts for several tax periods at once.
The SGEI was inspected by departments of specialised inspections, which are set up for a total of 13 FTs, or by staff of control departments of locally competent FTs.
The Department of Specialised Controls shall carry out tax checks within the scope specified by the Director of Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific business fields;
• entities where carrying out tax checks is extremely time-consuming and professional;
• entities with a branched territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• entities linked in chains and networks suspected of large-scale tax evasion and undue lure of excessive deductions.
The number of tax checks carried out by FA departments and the results of those inspections are set out in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed an amendment to Act No. 531/1990 Coll., on Territorial Financial Authorities, which consists of the establishment of a specialized FA with nationwide competence for selected tax entities (including for legal entities established for the purpose of doing business, which achieved turnover of more than CZK 2 billion).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls for large companies are governed by the same rules as tax controls in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • the German Fiscal Code (AO), • the Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • the Tax Control Regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory control provisions are enshrined in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - On-the-Spot Tax Check. In particular, these Articles lay down the rules on the admissibility of on-the-spot tax checks (i.e. at the premises of an undertaking), their scope in terms of subject matter, the rules on the division of responsibilities, the form and content of the control notices, the principles of control, the taxpayer's obligation to cooperate and the prerequisites for carrying out the final discussion and communication of the control report.
On-the-spot tax checks are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Administration Act Pursuant to Article 5.1 (1) in connection with Art. 19 of the Act is compulsory to participate in on-the-spot tax checks carried out by the Financial Authorities for the Federal Central Financial Office.
The participating authorities shall agree on the nature and extent of the participation of the Federal Central Tax Office in the tax controls.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the specific undertakings it selects are subject to scrutiny at the time it determines.
In such a case, it may declare the rules on the conduct and content of inspections at the premises of such companies.
Regulations on tax controls According to Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the provisions on tax checks (German abbreviation BpO 2000) were agreed by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, upper house of the German Parliament, in which the governments of the Länder are represented).
These administrative provisions apply to on-the-spot checks by the financial offices of the Länder and the Federal Central Tax Office.
Undertakings shall be classified by size at regular intervals in accordance with Article 3 BpO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to follow-up (Article 4.2 BpO).
According to Article 33.1 BpO 2000, each informed tax office must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in BpO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, it lays down the following additional methodology for tax administration:
• Uniform manual for special VAT checks in Germany;
• the USLO manual, which sets out the methodology for the use of data on intracommunity business relationships held in the VIES system;
• the ZAUBER manual, which sets out the methodology for using the ZAUBER database;
• work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits by business type.
The data are published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to control - not just large companies - must be determined at regular inspection intervals.
In general, checks on large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually announced, including VAT checks.
This means that during the inspection, checks will be carried out definitively, in particular on income, excise and VAT taxes - i.e. on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks may be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT controllers.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisational arrangements of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by checks is usually between three and five years.
BpO 2000 foresees a period of three years.
All company taxes are subject to verification.
4.5.3 Control management of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to examine individual cases of VDS inspections carried out, but focused on management issues in order to provide an overview of how tax administrations manage the issue of VAT controls in VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they collected information from tax authorities on the areas they consider essential to the management of this issue.
• What statistical records and analyses do VDS management have at its disposal regarding VAT control?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or records of rates distinguishing between combating VAT fraud and controlling VAT in general?
Czech Republic: No, ADIS does not allow such resolution with the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between the control proposed to combat VAT fraud and the general control of VAT.
• Are there any statistics or records of timeliness of VAT checks (linked to the time period of the audited transactions)?
Czech Republic: Evidence of timeliness of questioning with relevance for intracommunity acquisition of goods for selected VAT payers is reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information registered in ADIS also includes type data, how long the questioning took.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax controllers only contain information on the average time of the last check (information on the year).
This figure does not provide an overview of the selected control periods with regard to individual entrepreneurs.
The VAT auditors focus on the most recent period of the tax assessment; they also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, statistics produced at federal level for special VAT controls do not provide information on the classification of tax entities.
• There are some statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenues generated, broken down, for example, by the following criteria:
i. net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where the tax entity has unduly applied the reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only a nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax period);
iii. additional collection of tax revenue (payment of the additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech Tax Administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the amounts of tax assessed by type of tax, the number of tax entities audited and the number of tax periods audited.
Other tax practices (local investigations, complaints) are followed in the same way.
Time data and amounts of additional taxes paid shall be recorded as a separate task.
There are also statistics on general debt broken down by type of tax, but not on the declared tax or tax established by the tax authority.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT controls do not distinguish between those criteria.
Moreover, these differences are not distinguished by the majority of tax administrations visited.
• Are areas of control recorded that generate high additional revenues?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administration has the right to collect tax payers for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections of ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
Consequently, uniform statistics at federal level for tax controllers and special VAT controls do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach between the finance ministers of the Länder and the federal government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must write down their increased tax (VAT) obligation if they exceed a certain amount.
In such a case, they must specify, for example, the nature of the tax increase.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- VDS make an unjustified right to deduct input tax for supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity under § 72 para. 1 VAT Act;
• which were used for representation under § 75 para. 3 of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents which did not comply with the requirements laid down in Section 73 (1) of the Financial Regulation. 1 VAT Act;
- VDS did not distort VAT on output pursuant to § 21 para. 1 VAT Act.
Germany: It was stated that there were no regulations at federal level.
Consequently, uniform statistics at federal level for tax controllers and special VAT controls do not provide such data.
The VAT findings are not separately registered by the Länder if they arise from the tax controls of VDS.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder have to record their increased tax (VAT) obligation if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration analyse the areas of control from which there is a high "yield" and derive implications for management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they launch national audits focusing on risk commodities or on the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
Uniform statistics at federal level for tax controllers and special VAT controls do not provide data on audit areas from which high "returns" are generated.
There are different views on the analysis process as well as on case management in terms of relevance.
Some regional tax authorities provide specific information, but their use is on the tax authorities' own discretion.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
Differences in the responses of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects the amount of data from the tax checks carried out and data from the financial statements - balance sheets and profit and loss statements.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-inclined cases.
The same applies to the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, the Czech Republic is planning to establish a specialized tax office for the administration of VDS.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
This makes it more difficult to carry out those tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places greater emphasis on the choice of individual cases on the basis of the data from the tax returns submitted.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to measure the exact amount of VAT.
The two SAIs agree that Member States should be able to provide adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce shortfalls in VAT revenues.
As a result, the yield on VAT collection will increase and the level of risk detection for unreliable entrepreneurs will improve.
5. Conclusion
Cooperation between the two SAIs on parallel controls of VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and BRH.
Both SAIs have got to know each other better in the following areas: • intracommunity transactions, • VAT risk management, in particular as regards the selection of risk-inclined transactions, • assistance in the recovery of VAT claims and • VAT control of large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud strategies and differences in the above mentioned areas of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany were revealed.
The control findings have been compared and best practice identified.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to launch a debate on approaches and strategies within Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future VAT management control actions.
6. Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Edition deadline: June 2010.
